Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Definition of Hukm Shari' including Wad'i Rulings
Explaining the definition of hukm shari' with iqtida' and takhyir, and the need to include wad'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the complete Hanafi definition of hukm shari' and explain why wad'i rulings must be included separately.

Core Idea
Hukm shari' is divine address relating to actions by request, choice, or causation.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi usul definition of hukm shari'. The passage explains that the definition must include both taklifi and wad'i rulings. You will learn how iqtida' and takhyir define the five categories of taklifi rulings, and why wad'i rulings (causes, conditions, preventers) are conceptually distinct and need separate inclusion. This distinction is crucial for understanding how shari' addresses actions and their connections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
The passage gives the base definition: 'Khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin bi al-iqtida' wa al-takhyir.' Understand each term: divine address, related to actions of the legally responsible, by request or choice.
2
Analyze the exclusions
Why is 'bi al-iqtida'' necessary? To exclude mere informative statements like 'Allah created you and what you do' (37:96). Such statements are not requests, so they fall outside the definition.
The example shows how the definition filters out non-normative speech.
3
Break down iqtida'
Iqtida' covers request for action (wujub if decisive, nadb if non-decisive) and request for abandonment (tahrim if decisive, karahah if non-decisive). These are the four taklifi categories under request.
Distinguishing decisive vs non-decisive is key.
4
Understand takhyir
Takhyir gives an equal choice between doing and not doing, resulting in ibaha (permissibility). This completes the set of five taklifi rulings.
5
Evaluate the addition of aw al-wad'
Some scholars add the phrase 'aw al-wad'' (or setting) to include wad'i rulings: causes, conditions, and preventers. The passage argues for separate inclusion because wad'i rulings involve a relationship between two things, unlike the direct request/choice of taklifi rulings.
Even if causal statements imply obligations, their concept is distinct.

Because they are not related to the actions of the legally responsible, but rather are examples of clarification of events. Under the wisdom of Allah, but 'And Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) remains in the definition of ruling, because Allah's address is related to the pronoun 'kum' and its conjunct 'ma ta'malun', and this 'ma ta'malun' are actions of the legally responsible, and this address is related to them, so it remains in the definition of ruling, although it is not a ruling. So he excluded it by his saying 'by iqtida'', meaning request, because in 'He created you and what you do' there is only news that Allah is the creator of you and your deeds; there is no request in this news. Therefore, with 'bi al-iqtida'' which has the meaning of request, this address is excluded. And iqtida' means request of an action. The rulings under iqtida' are its explanation: summary: if the request is of an action, then if it is a decisive request, it is wujub; if non-decisive, its name is nadb. If the request is of abandonment, if decisive, it is tahrim; if non-decisive, it is karahah. And 'al-takhyir': under this condition, ibaha enters, because in it there is choice and option for both doing and not doing. Thus, according to some, the definition of ruling is complete with these words: 'The address of Allah Almighty related to the actions of the legally responsible by iqtida' and takhyir.' And some added 'aw al-wad'', meaning some people added the condition of 'or al-wad'' to this mentioned definition, to include the ruling by causality, conditionality, and the like, i.e., the ruling by preventing, as it is said: the presence of impurity on the one praying prevents the validity of prayer. This is also a wad'i ruling. Know that the address of the Law is two types: one is taklifi, which is related to the actions of the legally responsible by iqtida' or takhyir. The second is wad'i, which is an address that clarifies that this thing is a cause or condition for something, like the decline of the sun is a cause for prayer, and purity is a condition for prayer. These addresses are called wad'i rulings. When one of the two types, i.e., taklifi, is mentioned, it is also necessary to mention wad'i, so the condition 'aw al-wad'' should be added. And some did not mention wad'i, and nor do they add the condition 'aw al-wad'', but rather they include these wad'i rulings into iqtida' and takhyir and subsume them under taklifi rulings. They say, for example, 'the decline of the sun is a cause for prayer' means that when the decline occurs, prayer becomes obligatory. So this falls under iqtida', so there is no need to mention it separately. But the truth is the first: according to the author, the correct view is that the condition 'aw al-wad'' should be added and wad'i rulings should be mentioned independently, because the concepts of the two are distinct. The concept of wad'i ruling is the relationship of one thing to another, whether that relationship is by causality, conditionality, or other. And the concept of taklifi ruling is not a relationship of one thing to another. As for some cases where one is implied by the other, that cannot be proof that they are identical, such that mentioning one suffices for the other.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the definition of hukm shari' used by Hanafi usulis. It begins by analyzing the phrase 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin' and shows that it must be qualified by 'bi al-iqtida' wa al-takhyir' to exclude mere informative statements like 'Allah created you and what you do.' The author then explains the subcategories under iqtida' (wujub, nadb, tahrim, karahah) and under takhyir (ibaha). This much defines taklifi rulings. Then the passage discusses the addition of 'aw al-wad' to include wad'i rulings (causes, conditions, preventers). The author argues that wad'i rulings are distinct from taklifi and must be included separately, even though some scholars subsume them under iqtida' and takhyir. The truth according to the author is that they should be mentioned independently because their concepts differ: wad'i involves a relationship between two things, while taklifi does not. This distinction is important for understanding the full scope of the shari' ruling.

Key Terms
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Request (talab) for an action or abandonment, whether decisive or not
التخيير (al-takhyir): Option between doing and not doing, resulting in ibaha
الوضع (al-wad'): The type of address that establishes a thing as a cause, condition, or preventer of another ruling
الحكم التكليفي (al-hukm al-taklifi): Ruling that directly requires or prohibits an action or gives a choice
الحكم الوضعي (al-hukm al-wad'i): Ruling that relates one thing to another as cause, condition, or preventer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that wad'i rulings must be mentioned separately in the definition of hukm shari'?
A) Because they are not related to actions of the legally responsible.
B) Because their concept involves a relationship between two things, unlike taklifi rulings.
C) Because they are not derived from divine address.
D) Because they are only found in later fatawa.

Key Takeaway
The complete Hanafi definition of hukm shari' includes both taklifi (by request or choice) and wad'i (by causation, condition, or prevention) as distinct categories.

Dispute on Scope of Hukm Definition in Usul
Disputing whether the definition of hukm in usul defines the hukm used in fiqh or absolute hukm shari'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two competing views on what the usul definition of hukm defines and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Ash'ari counter-claim.

Core Idea
The usul definition of hukm is not about absolute shari rulings but specifically the rulings studied in fiqh—a distinction with practical scope consequences.

This passage presents a critical debate in usul al-fiqh: does the well-known definition of hukm shari'i (the address of Allah related to actions of the mukallaf) define the 'conventional' shari ruling of usulis, or does it define the ruling that is the subject matter of fiqh? The commentator of al-Talwih claimed the former, but the author of al-Tawdih (Sadr al-Sharia) argued for the latter. By working through this dispute, you will sharpen your ability to trace how definitions shape the scope of a discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing positions
State what the commentator (Taftazani) claims vs. what the author (Sadr al-Sharia) holds regarding what the definition 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin' defines.
The commentator says it defines the conventional shari ruling among usulis; the author says it defines the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh.
2
Examine the commentator's claimed evidence
Note that the commentator asserts that the distinction is found in Shafi'i books. The passage argues this explicit phrase is not present in those books.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i source cited
The passage quotes from Sharh al-Minhaj, which states 'al-mahdud al-hukm al-shar'i alladhi huwa fiqh la mutlaq al-hukm al-shar'i' — this directly supports the author's view.
This shows that some Shafi'is themselves consider the definition to be for the ruling that is fiqh.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does this dispute make? If the definition covers absolute shari rulings, it would include beliefs and statements (actions of the heart), expanding the scope of fiqh. The Hanafi position limits it to actions of the limbs, keeping fiqh as knowledge of practical rulings.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school (and the author) hold that the definition is for the ruling in fiqh. The commentator's objection is unfounded because the claimed distinction is not found in the sources he cites. The evidence from Sharh al-Minhaj supports the author.
This tarjih is based on textual evidence and source verification.

Source Text

قال الشارح في التلويح ولما عرف الفقه اقول الجليعني كتب الشافعية میں مذکور ہے کہ خطا الله تعالى المتعلق بافعال المکلفین یہ اس حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے جو متعارف بین الاصولیین ہے اور یہ تعریف اس حکم کی نہیں ہے جو تعریف فقہ میں ماخوذ ہے شارح کی عبارت دال ہے کہ یہ اثبات و نفی کتب شوافع میں مذکور ہے حالانکہ کہا جاتا ہے اس قسم کا اثبات یعنی یہ حکم شرعی متعارف کی تعریف ہے اور اس قسم کی نفی یعنی یہ اس حکم کی تعریف نہیں ہے جو فقہ میں ماخوذ ہے صراحہ کسی کتاب شوافع میں مذکور نہیں ہے۔ المفہوم بہنا ان يكون هذا الاثبات والنفي مذكورين في كتبهم وليس كذلك اذ لم توجد هذه العبارة في كتبهم (خسرو) والمصنف ذهب الى انه الى هذا التعريف المذكور تعريف له الى تعريف . للحكم الماخوذ في تعريف الفقه كونه تعريفا للحكم الشرعى الى المطلق المتعارف انما هو رأى بعض الاشاعرة والبعض الآخر يجعلون تعريفا للحكم الماخوذ في تعريف الفقه كل ذلك لعدم تصفحه که مصنف نے ان کی کتب کی پوری صفحہ گردانی نہیں کی ورنہ تو ایسی رائے قائم نہ کر تا علامہ صاحب کا یہ اعتراض اپنی عادت ثانویہ کے موافق ہے ورنہ کتب شوافع سے صاف محسوس ہوتا ہے بعض کے نزدیک یہ تعریف اس حکم کی ہے جو ماخوذ فی تعریف الفقہ ہے۔ دیکھتے شرح منہاج میں لکھا ہے ان قبل تقیید المتعلق بالفعل يخرج ما يتعلق بالاعتقاد والاقوال یعنی تعریف حکم میں جو قید المتعلق بافعال المکلفین کی کی گئی ہے یہ قیدان احکام کو خارج کر رہی ہے جن کا تعلق اعتقاد و اقوال سے ہے کیونکہ وہ از افعال جوارح نہیں ہیں اور افعال سے متباد را فعال جوارح ہیں حالانکہ یہ تمام احکام شرعیہ ہیں لہذا آپ کی تعریف شامل لجمیع الافراد نہ ہوئی۔ قلنا سے اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے کہا " یمکن حمل الفعل على ما يصدر من المكلف وهو اعم الذي يشمل تلك الاحكام ايمن واجباب بعضهم بان المحدود الحكم الشرعي الذي هو فقہ لا مطلق الحكم الشرعي یہ عبارت صاف دلالت کر رہی ہے کہ خطاب اللہ تعالی یہ حکم فقہی کی تعریف ہے نہ مطلق حکم شرعی کی ذا يويد المصنف ويخالف الشارح فنقول عرف بعض الاشاعرة الحكم الشرعی تو شارح کی یہ عبارت بھی صاف دلالت کر رہی ہے کہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف بانہ خطاب اللہ تعالٰی المتعلق الا یہ لبعض اشاعرہ کی رائے ہے کل اشاعرہ کی نہیں ہے یہی بات تو مصنف کہ رہا تھا تم وجہ اعتراض الشارح على المصنف - والخطابة
The commentator said in al-Talwih: 'When fiqh was defined...' It is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is that 'The address of Allah Most High related to the actions of the legally responsible' is the definition of the shari ruling that is conventional among usulis, and this definition is not for the ruling that is taken in the definition of fiqh. The commentator's phrase indicates that this affirmation and negation are mentioned in Shafi'i books, although it is said: this kind of affirmation (i.e., it is the definition of conventional shari ruling) and this kind of negation (i.e., it is not the definition of the ruling taken in fiqh) are not explicitly mentioned in any Shafi'i book. It is understood that this affirmation and negation should be present in their books, but it is not so, because this phrase is not found in their books. (Khusro) And the author holds that this mentioned definition is a definition for the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh; his considering it a definition of the absolute conventional shari ruling is only the view of some Ash'aris, and others make it a definition of the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. All this is due to his lack of thorough reading: the author did not thoroughly go through their books, otherwise he would not have formed such an opinion. The scholar's objection is in line with his secondary habit; otherwise, it is clearly felt from Shafi'i books that according to some, this definition is for the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. Look at Sharh al-Minhaj: it is written there: 'If the qualification of being related to actions excludes those rulings related to beliefs and statements, because they are not from actions of the limbs, and actions here mean actions of the limbs, although all of these are shari rulings, so your definition does not include all individuals.' In response, we say: 'It is possible to interpret action as what issues from the legally responsible, which is more general and includes those rulings...' And some answer that the defined is the shari ruling that is fiqh, not absolute shari ruling. This phrase clearly indicates that 'the address of Allah' is the definition of the fiqhi ruling, not the absolute shari ruling. This supports the author and contradicts the commentator. So we say: Some Ash'aris defined the shari ruling with this; the commentator's phrase also clearly indicates that the definition of shari ruling as 'the address of Allah Most High related to...' is the view of some Ash'aris, not all Ash'aris. This is exactly what the author was saying: you, the commentator, have no grounds for objecting to the author.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage presents a debate about what the well-known definition of hukm shari' (khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin) actually defines. The commentator of al-Talwih (Taftazani) claimed that this definition is for the 'conventional shari ruling' among usulis, not for the ruling used in the definition of fiqh. He stated that this distinction is found in Shafi'i books. The author of al-Tawdih (Sadr al-Sharia) argued that the definition is indeed for the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. The passage then examines the Shafi'i books and finds that the explicit phrase claimed by the commentator is not present. It cites a response from Sharh al-Minhaj that shows some Shafi'is consider the defined as 'the shari ruling that is fiqh'. The passage concludes that the commentator's criticism of the author is unfounded, because the view that the definition is of the absolute shari ruling is only attributed to some Ash'aris, not all. In Hanafi usul, this debate is important because it affects the scope of rulings included in fiqh; the Hanafi position tends to align with the author that the definition covers the rulings that are the subject matter of fiqh.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي (al-hukm al-shar'i): The divine address related to the actions of the legally responsible; the term is defined in usul, but there is dispute over its scope
المتعارف بين الأصوليين (al-muta'araf bayn al-usuliyyin): The conventional definition of hukm shar'i as used by usul scholars
الحكم المأخوذ في تعريف الفقه (al-hukm al-makhudh fi ta'rif al-fiqh): The ruling that is taken as the subject of the definition of fiqh, i.e., practical legal rulings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The usul definition of hukm is specifically for the rulings studied in fiqh, not absolute shari rulings, a distinction that maintains the scope of fiqh as practical legal rulings.

The Meaning of Khitab in the Definition of Hukm
Clarifying the meaning of khitab in the definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school defines 'address' (khitab) in the definition of hukm as internal speech (kalam nafsi) and defend it against the objection regarding eternity.

Core Idea
The divine address is eternal internal speech; intent to make understand suffices to call it address without an existing addressee.

In this lesson, we explore the first component of the Hanafi definition of hukm: the term 'address of Allah' (khitab Allah). The classical objection is that eternal speech cannot be called 'address' because no addressee existed in eternity. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the intent to make understand and actual address. Understanding this nuance is crucial for grasping the Hanafi theory of legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition and identify 'khitab'
Find the definition of hukm in the passage: 'al-hukm huwa khitab Allah...' Note that 'khitab' is the key term.
2
Understand khitab as internal speech
The commentator explains that 'khitab' here means internal speech (kalam nafsi), which is an eternal attribute of Allah.
This differs from external speech (kalam lafzi) that is created in time.
3
Analyze the eternity objection
Some argue that since internal speech is eternal and there was no addressee in eternity, it cannot be called 'address'.
The objection is based on the principle that address requires an existing addressee.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafis answer by distinguishing between the intent to make understand (qaṣd al-ifhām) and actual address. In eternity, Allah intended to make understanding for future responsible persons, which suffices to call it address.
They also offer two interpretations of 'khitab' to cover both verbal and internal speech.
5
State the outcome
The definition stands: 'khitab' applies to eternal internal speech via the intent to make understand.

Source Text

سمجھانے کی خاطر لیکن پھر اس مصدری معنیٰ سے نقل کر کے ما یقع بہ التخاطب کے معنی میں کر دیا گیا ہے اور تعریف حکم میں جو لفظ خطاب استعمال کیا گیا ہے مراد اس سے کلام نفسی ہے۔ ومن ذهب الى ان الكلام ان الکلام الموجه للا فہام دوسری یہ کہ الکلام المقصود منه افہام من ھو متہی تفہیمہ ۔ اب یہ تعریف جیسے کلام لفظی پر صادق آتی ہے اسی طرح کلام نفسی پر بھی صادق آتی ہے اور قصد افہام کا تعلق تو ہوتا ہی کلام نفسی سے ہے لفظی تو اسی نفسی کے سمجھانے کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ ہے۔ باقی رہا یہ سوال کہ ازل میں تو کوئی متھی للفہم موجود ہی نہیں تھا تو افہام یا قصد افہام کیسے ہو سکتی ہے لہذا ازل میں کلام نفسی کو خطاب نہ کہا جائے جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ مہینی للفہم کے لئے قصد افہام کرنا منتہی کے وجود اور حضور کو عند القصد تقاضا نہیں کرتا بلکہ جب افہام بالفعل ہوگا تو اس وقت اس کا وجود اور حضور ضروری ہو جاتا ہے۔ مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ کسی مکلف کے کسی ایک فعل کے ساتھ متعلق ہو کیونکہ جمع معرف باللام ہو یا معرف باللام کی طرف مضاف ہو دونوں صورتو میں معنی جمعیت سے منسلخ ہو کر صرف معنی جنسیتہ باقی رہتا ہے جو ایک فرد پر خواص نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام كا باحة ما فوق الاربع من النساء کیونکہ یہ بھی متعلق بفعل من افعال المکلف ہے۔ اس پر یہ اشکال وارد کیا گیا ہے کہ خطاب سے مراد کلام نفسی ہے جو صفت واحدہ ہے جس میں کوئی تعد نہیں ہے اب جتنا بھی خطابات ہیں تمام صفت واحدہ ہیں لہذا ایک ہی خطاب متعلق بجمیع افعال المكلفين ہوا تو جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ کلام نفسی اگر چہ صفت واحدہ ہے لیکن باعتبار تعدد متعلقات کے یہ متعدد ہے اس لئے خطابات متعددہ ہو جائیں گے ۔ خرج خطاب الله المتعلق باحوال ذاته يه المتعلق بافعال المکلفین کا فائدہ احتراز یہ ہے ۔ لا یقال اضافة الخطاب الى الله تعالیٰ یعنی اضافة خطاب الی اللہ تعالیٰ اس کی مقتضی ہے کہ قابلِ اطاعت صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا حکم ہے حالانکہ اس کے علاوہ اطاعت نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور اطاعت اولی الامر اور سید و سردار کی بھی واجب ہے تو اس اشکال کو دفع کیا کہ ان کی اطاعت انجاب الہی کے ساتھ واجب ہے تو حقیقتا حکم قابل اطاعت صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا ہوا۔ تو اعترض على هذا التعريف اس تعریف پر یہ اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ یہ مانع از دخول غیر نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے اندر ایک تو قصص داخل ہو رہے ہیں ۔ المبينة لاحوال المكلفين وافعالهم یعنی جو احوال مکلفین اور ان کے افعال کی تعیین کر رہے ہیں تو افعال تفسیر ہے احوال کی یا افعال سے مراد مقابل متروکات ہے اور احوال سے مراد متروکات ہیں یعنی وہ قصص جو مکلفین کے امور فعلیہ اور امور ترکیہ کی تبین کرتے ہیں اور دوسری وہ اخبار داخل ہو رہی ہیں جو اعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں کقولہ تعالیٰ وَالله خَلَقَكُرُ وَمَا تعملو من تو یہ خبر ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہیں اور تمہارے اعمال کو پیدا فرمایا تو یہ ایک خطاب جس کا تعلق اعمال اور افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بصورت اخبار ہے تو یہ دونوں تعریف حکم میں داخل ہو رہے ہیں حالانکہ حکم اصطلاحی کے افراد نہیں ہیں تو فن سید علی التعريف یعنی تعریف حکم پر اس قید کا اضافہ کیا گیا جو اس کی تخصیص کر کے ان افراد کا اخراج دے وہ ہے قولهم بالاقتضاء او التخییر یعنی حکم ایسے خطاب کو کہا جاتا ہے جس کا تعلق افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بالاقتضاد ہو یا بالتخییر اور قصص و اخبار مذکورہ کے اندر تعلق نہ بالاقتضا ہے نہ بالتخیر کیونکہ تخییر کا معنی ہے کہ اس امر کا فعل اور ترک مکلف کے لئے دونوں مباح ہیں اور اقتضا کا معنی ہے طلب پھر یہ طلب اگر فعل کی ہے مع المنع عن الترک تو یہ ایجاب ہے او بدونه یعنی منع عن الترک نہ ہو تو یہ ندب واستجاب ہے اگر طلب ترک ہے اور فعل سے منع ہے تو یہ تحریم ہے اگر فعل سے منع نہیں ہے تو یہ کراہت ہے تو اس قسم کی اقتضاء اور تخییر ان قصص وغیرہ میں نہیں ہے لہذا یہ داخل فی تعریف الحکم نہیں ہوں گے ۔ وقد يجاب بانه لا حاجة یہ اعتراض مذکور کا جواب ثانی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اقتضار تغییر کے زیادہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ یہاں قید حیثیت مراد ہے یعنی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ
Explanation of the definition of hukm (legal ruling) that is made with 'address of Allah'. Here the components of the definition are clarified. So what is the meaning of 'address' (khitab)? It is the directing of speech toward another for understanding. But then it is transferred from this infinitive meaning to the meaning of 'that by which address occurs'. And in the definition of hukm, the word 'address' is used, and by it is meant internal speech (kalam nafsi). And whoever holds that speech is eternal, there was no address with anyone in eternity because there was no addressee existing in eternity. Therefore, since internal speech is eternal, the word 'address' cannot apply to it. Hence this definition of hukm cannot apply to internal speech. Now those who have taken the position that speech cannot be called address in eternity will have to adopt one of two interpretations of 'address' in what follows so that the term 'address' can be applied to internal speech. One interpretation: 'speech directed for understanding'; the second: 'speech intended from it to make understood one who is prepared for understanding'. Now this definition applies to verbal speech and likewise applies to internal speech. And the intent to make understanding (qaṣd al-ifhām) is only related to internal speech; verbal speech is only a means and instrument for making that internal [speech] understood. As for the question that in eternity there was no one prepared for understanding, so how could making understand or the intent to make understand occur? Hence internal speech in eternity should not be called 'address'. The answer to this is given: that the intent to make understand for someone prepared for understanding does not require the existence and presence of the addressee at the time of intent. Rather, when the actual making understand occurs, then at that time its existence and presence become necessary. At the time of the intent to make understand, neither existence nor presence is necessary. Therefore, for calling internal speech 'address' in eternity, it is not necessary for an addressee prepared for understanding to exist in eternity. And the meaning of 'its relation to the actions of the responsible persons' (taʿalluq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn): In the definition of hukm, it says 'related to the actions of the responsible persons'. Apparently this indicates that hukm is called that address which is related to all actions of all responsible persons. Since such an address does not exist, it is clarified that by 'relation' is meant that it is related to one action of one responsible person. Because whether it is a definite plural (al-jamʿ al-muʿarraf bi-lām) or a plural added to a definite, in both cases the meaning of plurality is stripped and only the generic meaning remains, which can apply to a single individual. Therefore, by 'actions' is meant the genus of action, and likewise by 'the responsible persons' is meant the genus of responsible person, which can apply to a single individual. (اذلا خطاب) this is an indication of the apparent problem that has been repelled. (فدخل فی الحد خواص نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام كا باحة ما فوق الاربع من النساء) because this also is related to an action of the responsible persons. An objection is raised on this: that by 'address' is meant internal speech, which is a single attribute having no multiplicity. Now however many addresses there are, all are a single attribute. So one single address would be related to all actions of the responsible persons. The answer to this is given: that internal speech, although a single attribute, is multiple by virtue of the multiplicity of its objects of relation (mutaʿalliqāt). Therefore, addresses will become multiple. (خرج خطاب الله المتعلق باحوال ذاته يه المتعلق بافعال المکلفین) The benefit of this is exclusion. (لا یقال اضافة الخطاب الى الله تعالیٰ) i.e., the addition of address to Allah the Exalted necessitates that only Allah's command is worthy of obedience, whereas besides this, obedience to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and obedience to those in authority (ulu al-amr) and the master/leader is also obligatory. So this objection is repelled: that their obedience is obligatory by divine command, so in reality only Allah's command is worthy of obedience. So an objection was made on this definition: that it is not preventive of the entry of what is not [included], because first, stories (qiṣaṣ) enter into it, which determine the states of the responsible persons and their actions. So 'actions' is an explanatory appositive of 'states', or by 'actions' is meant what is opposite to abandoned matters, and by 'states' is meant abandoned matters, i.e., the stories that clarify the practical matters and non-practical matters of the responsible persons. And second, reports (akhbār) enter that are related to the actions of the responsible persons, such as His statement: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' This is a report: that Allah created you and your actions. So this is an address whose relation to the actions and deeds of the responsible persons is in the form of a report. So both of these enter into the definition of hukm, whereas they are not instances of the technical hukm. So (فن سید علی التعريف) i.e., a restriction was added to the definition of hukm that specifies it and excludes these instances; it is their saying: (بالاقتضاء او التخییر) meaning hukm is that address whose relation to actions of the responsible persons is by demand (iqtidāʾ) or by choice (takhyīr). And in the mentioned stories and reports, there is neither a relation by demand nor by choice. Because 'choice' means that doing or leaving the matter are both permissible for the responsible person. And 'demand' means request. Then this request, if it is for an action with prevention from leaving, it is obligation (ījāb); or without it (i.e., without prevention from leaving), it is recommendation (nadb) and desirability (istijāb). If it is a request for leaving and prevention from doing, it is prohibition (taḥrīm). If it is not prevention from doing, it is dislike (karāha). So this kind of demand and choice is not present in these stories, etc. Therefore, they will not be included in the definition of hukm. (وقد يجاب بانه لا حاجة) This is a second answer to the mentioned objection. The summary is that there is no need to add demand or choice; rather, here the 'restriction of respect' (qayd al-ḥaythiyya) is meant, i.e., 'the address of Allah the Exalted'.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the definition of hukm (legal ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The definition under discussion is: 'The address of Allah related to the actions of the responsible persons by demand or choice.' The commentator begins by clarifying each component of this definition. First, he explains the word 'address' (khitab). Originally meaning the act of directing speech to another, it is used here to refer to internal speech (kalam nafsi), which is the eternal attribute of speech in Allah. An objection arises: since internal speech is eternal and there was no addressee in eternity, how can it be called 'address'? The response distinguishes between intent to make understand (qaṣd al-ifhām) and actual making understand. In eternity, Allah intends to make understand future responsible persons, and that intent suffices for calling it address; the actual existence of the addressee is not required at the time of the intent. Next, the phrase 'related to actions of the responsible persons' is examined. It does not mean relation to all actions of all responsible persons (which is impossible), but relation to any one action of any one responsible person. This is because the definite plural in Arabic can indicate the genus, not necessarily all individuals. The commentator then addresses a subtle point: although internal speech is a single attribute, it is considered multiple because of the multiplicity of its objects of relation, so multiple addresses exist for different rulings. Then he discusses an objection: why specify 'of Allah' when obedience is also due to the Prophet and authorities? The answer: their obedience is ultimately through Allah's command, so the definition rightly restricts to Allah's address. The major objection is that the definition would include stories and reports that relate to actions of the responsible persons, such as narrative verses or the verse 'Allah created you and your actions.' These are not rulings in the technical sense (they do not demand or permit anything). To exclude them, the qualification 'by demand or choice' is added. 'Demand' includes obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and dislike; 'choice' is permissibility. Stories and reports have no such quality. Finally, a second response is mentioned: the qualification may not need explicit addition because the definition inherently implies demand/choice by the term 'address of Allah' in the context of legal rulings. The passage follows the author's order: clarifying components, addressing objections, and justifying the final form of the definition.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): The address of Allah related to the actions of the responsible persons by demand or choice
الخطاب (al-khitab): Internal speech (kalam nafsi) directed for understanding, including the intent to make understand even if no addressee exists at the time of address in eternity
قصد الإفهام (qaṣd al-ifhām): The divine intent to make the responsible persons understand the ruling, which suffices for calling the eternal internal speech 'address'

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'address' (khitab) in the Hanafi definition of hukm?
A) Verbal speech revealed in time
B) Internal speech (kalam nafsi)
C) The Quran and Sunnah
D) Any speech that communicates

Key Takeaway
The divine address in the definition of hukm refers to eternal internal speech; the intent to make understand suffices for it to be called address.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Scope of Hukm: Relation to Actions of the Responsible Persons
Explaining the scope of relation to actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of 'related to actions of the responsible persons' in the Hanafi definition of hukm, demonstrating how it applies to any one action of any one responsible person and how a single internal speech can produce multiple addresses.

Core Idea
The phrase 'related to actions of the responsible persons' means relation to any one action of any one person, not all actions; and one internal speech becomes multiple addresses by virtue of multiple objects.

In this lesson, we examine the second component of the definition: 'related to actions of the responsible persons' (al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn). The commentator clarifies that this does not mean relation to all actions of all persons, which is impossible, but rather relation to the genus of action and responsible person, applying to any single instance. Additionally, an objection about the multiplicity of addresses from a single internal speech is answered by noting that the attribute is multiple by relation to its objects. This clarification ensures that every legal ruling, even those specific to certain individuals, fits the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase in the definition
Find 'al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn' in the definition. Note that it literally says 'related to actions of the responsible persons'.
2
Understand the apparent problem
If taken literally, it would imply that a ruling must relate to all actions of all responsible persons, which is not the case for specific rulings.
3
Apply the concept of generic meaning (jins)
The commentator explains that due to the definite plural construction, the meaning becomes generic: 'actions' means the genus of action, and 'responsible persons' means the genus of responsible person. Thus, it applies to any one action of any one person.
This is based on Arabic linguistic rules in Hanafi usul.
4
Address the multiplicity objection
An objection arises: if internal speech is a single attribute, how can there be multiple addresses for different rulings? The answer: the attribute is one in essence but multiple by virtue of its different objects of relation (mutaʿalliqāt). Therefore, each ruling has its own address.
This preserves the unity of divine speech while allowing diversity of commands.
5
Confirm inclusion of specific cases
The commentator gives an example: the permissibility of marrying more than four women (khāṣṣiyat al-nabī). This is a ruling specific to the Prophet but still relates to an action of a responsible person, thus included in the definition.

الکلام الموجه للا فہام دوسری یہ کہ الکلام المقصود منه افہام من ھو متہی تفہیمہ ۔ اب یہ تعریف جیسے کلام لفظی پر صادق آتی ہے اسی طرح کلام نفسی پر بھی صادق آتی ہے اور قصد افہام کا تعلق تو ہوتا ہی کلام نفسی سے ہے لفظی تو اسی نفسی کے سمجھانے کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ ہے۔ باقی رہا یہ سوال کہ ازل میں تو کوئی متھی للفہم موجود ہی نہیں تھا تو افہام یا قصد افہام کیسے ہو سکتی ہے لہذا ازل میں کلام نفسی کو خطاب نہ کہا جائے جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ مہینی للفہم کے لئے قصد افہام کرنا منتہی کے وجود اور حضور کو عند القصد تقاضا نہیں کرتا بلکہ جب افہام بالفعل ہوگا تو اس وقت اس کا وجود اور حضور ضروری ہو جاتا ہے۔ خواص نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام كا باحة ما فوق الاربع من النساء کیونکہ یہ بھی متعلق بفعل من افعال المکلف ہے۔ اس پر یہ اشکال وارد کیا گیا ہے کہ خطاب سے مراد کلام نفسی ہے جو صفت واحدہ ہے جس میں کوئی تعد نہیں ہے اب جتنا بھی خطابات ہیں تمام صفت واحدہ ہیں لہذا ایک ہی خطاب متعلق بجمیع افعال المكلفين ہوا تو جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ کلام نفسی اگر چہ صفت واحدہ ہے لیکن باعتبار تعدد متعلقات کے یہ متعدد ہے ساتھ واجب ہے تو حقیقتا حکم قابل اطاعت صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا ہوا۔ تو اعترض على هذا التعريف اس تعریف پر یہ اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ یہ مانع از دخول غیر نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے اندر ایک تو قصص داخل ہو رہے ہیں ۔ المبينة لاحوال المكلفين وافعالهم یعنی جو احوال مکلفین اور ان کے افعال کی تعیین کر رہے ہیں تو افعال تفسیر ہے احوال کی یا افعال سے مراد مقابل متروکات ہے اور احوال سے مراد متروکات ہیں یعنی وہ قصص جو مکلفین کے امور فعلیہ اور امور ترکیہ کی تبین کرتے ہیں اور دوسری وہ اخبار داخل ہو رہی ہیں جو اعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں کقولہ تعالیٰ وَالله خَلَقَكُرُ وَمَا تعملو من تو یہ خبر ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہیں اور تمہارے اعمال کو پیدا فرمایا تو یہ ایک خطاب جس کا تعلق اعمال اور افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بصورت اخبار ہے تو یہ دونوں تعریف حکم میں داخل ہو رہے ہیں حالانکہ حکم اصطلاحی کے افراد نہیں ہیں تو فن سید علی التعريف یعنی تعریف حکم پر اس قید کا اضافہ کیا گیا جو اس کی تخصیص کر کے ان افراد کا اخراج دے وہ ہے قولهم بالاقتضاء او التخییر یعنی حکم ایسے خطاب کو کہا جاتا ہے جس کا تعلق افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بالاقتضاد ہو یا بالتخییر اور قصص و اخبار مذکورہ کے اندر تعلق نہ بالاقتضا ہے نہ بالتخیر کیونکہ تخییر کا معنی ہے کہ اس امر کا فعل اور ترک مکلف کے لئے دونوں مباح ہیں اور اقتضا کا معنی ہے طلب پھر یہ طلب اگر فعل کی ہے مع المنع عن الترک تو یہ ایجاب ہے او بدونه یعنی منع عن الترک نہ ہو تو یہ ندب واستجاب ہے اگر طلب ترک ہے اور فعل سے منع ہے تو یہ تحریم ہے اگر فعل سے منع نہیں ہے تو یہ کراہت ہے تو اس قسم کی اقتضاء اور تخییر ان قصص وغیرہ میں نہیں ہے لہذا یہ داخل فی تعریف الحکم نہیں ہوں گے ۔ وقد يجاب بانه لا حاجة یہ اعتراض مذکور کا جواب ثانی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اقتضار تغییر کے زیادہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ یہاں قید حیثیت مراد ہے یعنی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ
Explanation of the definition of hukm (legal ruling) that is made with 'address of Allah'. Here the components of the definition are clarified. So what is the meaning of 'address' (khitab)? It is the directing of speech toward another for understanding. But then it is transferred from this infinitive meaning to the meaning of 'that by which address occurs'. And in the definition of hukm, the word 'address' is used, and by it is meant internal speech (kalam nafsi). And whoever holds that speech is eternal, there was no address with anyone in eternity because there was no addressee existing in eternity. Therefore, since internal speech is eternal, the word 'address' cannot apply to it. Hence this definition of hukm cannot apply to internal speech. Now those who have taken the position that speech cannot be called address in eternity will have to adopt one of two interpretations of 'address' in what follows so that the term 'address' can be applied to internal speech. One interpretation: 'speech directed for understanding'; the second: 'speech intended from it to make understood one who is prepared for understanding'. Now this definition applies to verbal speech and likewise applies to internal speech. And the intent to make understanding (qaṣd al-ifhām) is only related to internal speech; verbal speech is only a means and instrument for making that internal [speech] understood. As for the question that in eternity there was no one prepared for understanding, so how could making understand or the intent to make understand occur? Hence internal speech in eternity should not be called 'address'. The answer to this is given: that the intent to make understand for someone prepared for understanding does not require the existence and presence of the addressee at the time of intent. Rather, when the actual making understand occurs, then at that time its existence and presence become necessary. At the time of the intent to make understand, neither existence nor presence is necessary. Therefore, for calling internal speech 'address' in eternity, it is not necessary for an addressee prepared for understanding to exist in eternity. And the meaning of 'its relation to the actions of the responsible persons' (taʿalluq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn): In the definition of hukm, it says 'related to the actions of the responsible persons'. Apparently this indicates that hukm is called that address which is related to all actions of all responsible persons. Since such an address does not exist, it is clarified that by 'relation' is meant that it is related to one action of one responsible person. Because whether it is a definite plural (al-jamʿ al-muʿarraf bi-lām) or a plural added to a definite, in both cases the meaning of plurality is stripped and only the generic meaning remains, which can apply to a single individual. Therefore, by 'actions' is meant the genus of action, and likewise by 'the responsible persons' is meant the genus of responsible person, which can apply to a single individual. (اذلا خطاب) this is an indication of the apparent problem that has been repelled. (فدخل فی الحد خواص نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام كا باحة ما فوق الاربع من النساء) because this also is related to an action of the responsible persons. An objection is raised on this: that by 'address' is meant internal speech, which is a single attribute having no multiplicity. Now however many addresses there are, all are a single attribute. So one single address would be related to all actions of the responsible persons. The answer to this is given: that internal speech, although a single attribute, is multiple by virtue of the multiplicity of its objects of relation (mutaʿalliqāt). Therefore, addresses will become multiple. (خرج خطاب الله المتعلق باحوال ذاته يه المتعلق بافعال المکلفین) The benefit of this is exclusion. (لا یقال اضافة الخطاب الى الله تعالیٰ) i.e., the addition of address to Allah the Exalted necessitates that only Allah's command is worthy of obedience, whereas besides this, obedience to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and obedience to those in authority (ulu al-amr) and the master/leader is also obligatory. So this objection is repelled: that their obedience is obligatory by divine command, so in reality only Allah's command is worthy of obedience. So an objection was made on this definition: that it is not preventive of the entry of what is not [included], because first, stories (qiṣaṣ) enter into it, which determine the states of the responsible persons and their actions. So 'actions' is an explanatory appositive of 'states', or by 'actions' is meant what is opposite to abandoned matters, and by 'states' is meant abandoned matters, i.e., the stories that clarify the practical matters and non-practical matters of the responsible persons. And second, reports (akhbār) enter that are related to the actions of the responsible persons, such as His statement: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' This is a report: that Allah created you and your actions. So this is an address whose relation to the actions and deeds of the responsible persons is in the form of a report. So both of these enter into the definition of hukm, whereas they are not instances of the technical hukm. So (فن سید علی التعريف) i.e., a restriction was added to the definition of hukm that specifies it and excludes these instances; it is their saying: (بالاقتضاء او التخییر) meaning hukm is that address whose relation to actions of the responsible persons is by demand (iqtidāʾ) or by choice (takhyīr). And in the mentioned stories and reports, there is neither a relation by demand nor by choice. Because 'choice' means that doing or leaving the matter are both permissible for the responsible person. And 'demand' means request. Then this request, if it is for an action with prevention from leaving, it is obligation (ījāb); or without it (i.e., without prevention from leaving), it is recommendation (nadb) and desirability (istijāb). If it is a request for leaving and prevention from doing, it is prohibition (taḥrīm). If it is not prevention from doing, it is dislike (karāha). So this kind of demand and choice is not present in these stories, etc. Therefore, they will not be included in the definition of hukm. (وقد يجاب بانه لا حاجة) This is a second answer to the mentioned objection. The summary is that there is no need to add demand or choice; rather, here the 'restriction of respect' (qayd al-ḥaythiyya) is meant, i.e., 'the address of Allah the Exalted'.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the definition of hukm (legal ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The definition under discussion is: 'The address of Allah related to the actions of the responsible persons by demand or choice.' The commentator begins by clarifying each component of this definition. First, he explains the word 'address' (khitab). Originally meaning the act of directing speech to another, it is used here to refer to internal speech (kalam nafsi), which is the eternal attribute of speech in Allah. An objection arises: since internal speech is eternal and there was no addressee in eternity, how can it be called 'address'? The response distinguishes between intent to make understand (qaṣd al-ifhām) and actual making understand. In eternity, Allah intends to make understand future responsible persons, and that intent suffices for calling it address; the actual existence of the addressee is not required at the time of the intent. Next, the phrase 'related to actions of the responsible persons' is examined. It does not mean relation to all actions of all responsible persons (which is impossible), but relation to any one action of any one responsible person. This is because the definite plural in Arabic can indicate the genus, not necessarily all individuals. The commentator then addresses a subtle point: although internal speech is a single attribute, it is considered multiple because of the multiplicity of its objects of relation, so multiple addresses exist for different rulings. Then he discusses an objection: why specify 'of Allah' when obedience is also due to the Prophet and authorities? The answer: their obedience is ultimately through Allah's command, so the definition rightly restricts to Allah's address. The major objection is that the definition would include stories and reports that relate to actions of the responsible persons, such as narrative verses or the verse 'Allah created you and your actions.' These are not rulings in the technical sense (they do not demand or permit anything). To exclude them, the qualification 'by demand or choice' is added. 'Demand' includes obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and dislike; 'choice' is permissibility. Stories and reports have no such quality. Finally, a second response is mentioned: the qualification may not need explicit addition because the definition inherently implies demand/choice by the term 'address of Allah' in the context of legal rulings. The passage follows the author's order: clarifying components, addressing objections, and justifying the final form of the definition.

Key Terms
المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين (al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn): Related to actions of the responsible persons; interpreted generically to mean any action of any responsible person
تعدد المتعلقات (taʿaddud al-mutaʿalliqāt): The multiplicity of objects of relation; the one attribute becomes multiple by virtue of the different rulings it relates to

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the commentator explain the phrase 'related to actions of the responsible persons' to avoid the implication that a ruling must apply to all actions of all responsible persons?
A) By arguing that the phrase is metaphorical.
B) By interpreting the definite plural as indicating the genus, not totality.
C) By adding the condition 'by demand or choice'.
D) By reinterpreting 'actions' as intentions.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'related to actions of the responsible persons' is interpreted generically to apply to any one action of any one responsible person, and the unity of divine speech does not prevent multiplicity of rulings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Condition of Demand or Choice in Hukm
Adding the condition of demand or choice to exclude stories and reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition 'by demand or choice' (bi-al-iqtiḍāʾ aw al-takhyīr) to distinguish legal rulings from stories and reports, and evaluate the need for this condition in the definition of hukm.

Core Idea
Only addresses that demand or permit an action are legal rulings; stories and reports about actions are not rulings.

In this final lesson on the definition of hukm, we focus on the crucial condition 'by demand or choice' (bi-al-iqtiḍāʾ aw al-takhyīr). The commentator explains that without this condition, the definition would include stories (qiṣaṣ) and reports (akhbār) that relate to actions of the responsible persons but do not impose obligations, prohibitions, permissions, etc. We also examine a second answer that suggests the condition might be implicit due to the context of legislation. This lesson solidifies the complete definition and its ability to exclude non-ruling addresses.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the objection to the unqualified definition
The objector points out that stories (e.g., about past prophets) and reports (e.g., 'Allah created you and what you do') relate to actions but are not rulings.
These are not considered hukm taklifi.
2
Understand 'demand' (iqtida') and its four types
Demand includes obligation (fard), recommendation (nadb), prohibition (tahrim), and dislike (karaha). These all involve a request from Allah.
This is the core of taklif (responsibility).
3
Understand 'choice' (takhyir)
Choice means the act is permissible (mubah); doing or leaving are both equal.
This is a fifth category of hukm taklifi.
4
Apply the condition to exclude stories and reports
Stories and reports do not contain demand or choice; they inform without imposing any obligation or permission. Therefore, they are excluded from the definition.
5
Evaluate the second answer (implicit condition)
Some say the condition is not needed because 'address of Allah' in the context of legislation inherently implies demand/choice. This suggests the definition could stand without explicit addition.
Despite this, most Hanafi texts include the explicit condition to be precise.

صادق نہیں آسکتی اب جو حضرات ادھر چلے گئے ہیں کہ کلام کو ازل میں خطاب نہیں کیا جاسکتا تو اسے خطاب کی دو تفسیریں آنے والی میں کوئی کرنی پڑے گی تا کہ کلام انزلی پر خطاب کا اطلاق ہو سکے ایک تفسیر یہ کہ الکلام الموجه للا فہام دوسری یہ کہ الکلام المقصود منه افہام من ھو متہی تفہیمہ ۔ اب یہ تعریف جیسے کلام لفظی پر صادق آتی ہے اسی طرح کلام نفسی پر بھی صادق آتی ہے اور قصد افہام کا تعلق تو ہوتا ہی کلام نفسی سے ہے لفظی تو اسی نفسی کے سمجھانے کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ ہے۔ باقی رہا یہ سوال کہ ازل میں تو کوئی متھی للفہم موجود ہی نہیں تھا تو افہام یا قصد افہام کیسے ہو سکتی ہے لہذا ازل میں کلام نفسی کو خطاب نہ کہا جائے جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ مہینی للفہم کے لئے قصد افہام کرنا منتہی کے وجود اور حضور کو عند القصد تقاضا نہیں کرتا بلکہ جب افہام بالفعل ہوگا تو اس وقت اس کا وجود اور حضور ضروری ہو جاتا ہے۔ بوقت قصد افہام نہ وجود ضروری ہے نہ حضور لہذا ازل میں کلام نفسی کو خطاب کہنے کے لئے کسی مخاطب منتہی الفہم کا ازل میں موجود ہونا کوئی ضروری امر نہیں ہے ۔ ومعنی تعلقه بافعال المكلفين تعریف حکم میں جو المتعلق با فعال المکلفین کہا گیا ہے اس سے بظاہر یہ معلوم ہوتا تھا کہ حکم ایسے خطاب کو کہا جاتا ہے جو جمیع مکلفین کے جمیع افعال کے ساتھ تعلق پکڑے چونکہ ایسا خطاب کوئی نہیں ہے اس لئے واضح کیا کہ تعلق سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ کسی مکلف کے کسی ایک فعل کے ساتھ متعلق ہو کیونکہ جمع معرف باللام ہو یا معرف باللام کی طرف مضاف ہو دونوں صورتو میں معنی جمعیت سے منسلخ ہو کر صرف معنی جنسیتہ باقی رہتا ہے جو ایک فرد پر خواص نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام كا باحة ما فوق الاربع من النساء کیونکہ یہ بھی متعلق بفعل من افعال المکلف ہے۔ اس پر یہ اشکال وارد کیا گیا ہے کہ خطاب سے مراد کلام نفسی ہے جو صفت واحدہ ہے جس میں کوئی تعد نہیں ہے اب جتنا بھی خطابات ہیں تمام صفت واحدہ ہیں لہذا ایک ہی خطاب متعلق بجمیع افعال المكلفين ہوا تو جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ کلام نفسی اگر چہ صفت واحدہ ہے لیکن باعتبار تعدد متعلقات کے یہ متعدد ہے اس لئے خطابات متعددہ ہو جائیں گے ۔ خرج خطاب الله المتعلق باحوال ذاته يه المتعلق بافعال المکلفین کا فائدہ احتراز یہ ہے ۔ لا یقال اضافة الخطاب الى الله تعالیٰ یعنی اضافة خطاب الی اللہ تعالیٰ اس کی مقتضی ہے کہ قابلِ اطاعت صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا حکم ہے حالانکہ اس کے علاوہ اطاعت نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور اطاعت اولی الامر اور سید و سردار کی بھی واجب ہے تو اس اشکال کو دفع کیا کہ ان کی اطاعت انجاب الہی کے ساتھ واجب ہے تو حقیقتا حکم قابل اطاعت صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا ہوا۔ تو اعترض على هذا التعريف اس تعریف پر یہ اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ یہ مانع از دخول غیر نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے اندر ایک تو قصص داخل ہو رہے ہیں ۔ المبينة لاحوال المكلفين وافعالهم یعنی جو احوال مکلفین اور ان کے افعال کی تعیین کر رہے ہیں تو افعال تفسیر ہے احوال کی یا افعال سے مراد مقابل متروکات ہے اور احوال سے مراد متروکات ہیں یعنی وہ قصص جو مکلفین کے امور فعلیہ اور امور ترکیہ کی تبین کرتے ہیں اور دوسری وہ اخبار داخل ہو رہی ہیں جو اعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں کقولہ تعالیٰ وَالله خَلَقَكُرُ وَمَا تعملو من تو یہ خبر ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہیں اور تمہارے اعمال کو پیدا فرمایا تو یہ ایک خطاب جس کا تعلق اعمال اور افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بصورت اخبار ہے تو یہ دونوں تعریف حکم میں داخل ہو رہے ہیں حالانکہ حکم اصطلاحی کے افراد نہیں ہیں تو فن سید علی التعريف یعنی تعریف حکم پر اس قید کا اضافہ کیا گیا جو اس کی تخصیص کر کے ان افراد کا اخراج دے وہ ہے قولهم بالاقتضاء او التخییر یعنی حکم ایسے خطاب کو کہا جاتا ہے جس کا تعلق افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بالاقتضاد ہو یا بالتخییر اور قصص و اخبار مذکورہ کے اندر تعلق نہ بالاقتضا ہے نہ بالتخیر کیونکہ تخییر کا معنی ہے کہ اس امر کا فعل اور ترک مکلف کے لئے دونوں مباح ہیں اور اقتضا کا معنی ہے طلب پھر یہ طلب اگر فعل کی ہے مع المنع عن الترک تو یہ ایجاب ہے او بدونه یعنی منع عن الترک نہ ہو تو یہ ندب واستجاب ہے اگر طلب ترک ہے اور فعل سے منع ہے تو یہ تحریم ہے اگر فعل سے منع نہیں ہے تو یہ کراہت ہے تو اس قسم کی اقتضاء اور تخییر ان قصص وغیرہ میں نہیں ہے لہذا یہ داخل فی تعریف الحکم نہیں ہوں گے ۔ وقد يجاب بانه لا حاجة یہ اعتراض مذکور کا جواب ثانی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اقتضار تغییر کے زیادہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ یہاں قید حیثیت مراد ہے یعنی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ
Explanation of the definition of hukm (legal ruling) that is made with 'address of Allah'. Here the components of the definition are clarified. So what is the meaning of 'address' (khitab)? It is the directing of speech toward another for understanding. But then it is transferred from this infinitive meaning to the meaning of 'that by which address occurs'. And in the definition of hukm, the word 'address' is used, and by it is meant internal speech (kalam nafsi). And whoever holds that speech is eternal, there was no address with anyone in eternity because there was no addressee existing in eternity. Therefore, since internal speech is eternal, the word 'address' cannot apply to it. Hence this definition of hukm cannot apply to internal speech. Now those who have taken the position that speech cannot be called address in eternity will have to adopt one of two interpretations of 'address' in what follows so that the term 'address' can be applied to internal speech. One interpretation: 'speech directed for understanding'; the second: 'speech intended from it to make understood one who is prepared for understanding'. Now this definition applies to verbal speech and likewise applies to internal speech. And the intent to make understanding (qaṣd al-ifhām) is only related to internal speech; verbal speech is only a means and instrument for making that internal [speech] understood. As for the question that in eternity there was no one prepared for understanding, so how could making understand or the intent to make understand occur? Hence internal speech in eternity should not be called 'address'. The answer to this is given: that the intent to make understand for someone prepared for understanding does not require the existence and presence of the addressee at the time of intent. Rather, when the actual making understand occurs, then at that time its existence and presence become necessary. At the time of the intent to make understand, neither existence nor presence is necessary. Therefore, for calling internal speech 'address' in eternity, it is not necessary for an addressee prepared for understanding to exist in eternity. And the meaning of 'its relation to the actions of the responsible persons' (taʿalluq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn): In the definition of hukm, it says 'related to the actions of the responsible persons'. Apparently this indicates that hukm is called that address which is related to all actions of all responsible persons. Since such an address does not exist, it is clarified that by 'relation' is meant that it is related to one action of one responsible person. Because whether it is a definite plural (al-jamʿ al-muʿarraf bi-lām) or a plural added to a definite, in both cases the meaning of plurality is stripped and only the generic meaning remains, which can apply to a single individual. Therefore, by 'actions' is meant the genus of action, and likewise by 'the responsible persons' is meant the genus of responsible person, which can apply to a single individual. (اذلا خطاب) this is an indication of the apparent problem that has been repelled. (فدخل فی الحد خواص نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام كا باحة ما فوق الاربع من النساء) because this also is related to an action of the responsible persons. An objection is raised on this: that by 'address' is meant internal speech, which is a single attribute having no multiplicity. Now however many addresses there are, all are a single attribute. So one single address would be related to all actions of the responsible persons. The answer to this is given: that internal speech, although a single attribute, is multiple by virtue of the multiplicity of its objects of relation (mutaʿalliqāt). Therefore, addresses will become multiple. (خرج خطاب الله المتعلق باحوال ذاته يه المتعلق بافعال المکلفین) The benefit of this is exclusion. (لا یقال اضافة الخطاب الى الله تعالیٰ) i.e., the addition of address to Allah the Exalted necessitates that only Allah's command is worthy of obedience, whereas besides this, obedience to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and obedience to those in authority (ulu al-amr) and the master/leader is also obligatory. So this objection is repelled: that their obedience is obligatory by divine command, so in reality only Allah's command is worthy of obedience. So an objection was made on this definition: that it is not preventive of the entry of what is not [included], because first, stories (qiṣaṣ) enter into it, which determine the states of the responsible persons and their actions. So 'actions' is an explanatory appositive of 'states', or by 'actions' is meant what is opposite to abandoned matters, and by 'states' is meant abandoned matters, i.e., the stories that clarify the practical matters and non-practical matters of the responsible persons. And second, reports (akhbār) enter that are related to the actions of the responsible persons, such as His statement: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' This is a report: that Allah created you and your actions. So this is an address whose relation to the actions and deeds of the responsible persons is in the form of a report. So both of these enter into the definition of hukm, whereas they are not instances of the technical hukm. So (فن سید علی التعريف) i.e., a restriction was added to the definition of hukm that specifies it and excludes these instances; it is their saying: (بالاقتضاء او التخییر) meaning hukm is that address whose relation to actions of the responsible persons is by demand (iqtidāʾ) or by choice (takhyīr). And in the mentioned stories and reports, there is neither a relation by demand nor by choice. Because 'choice' means that doing or leaving the matter are both permissible for the responsible person. And 'demand' means request. Then this request, if it is for an action with prevention from leaving, it is obligation (ījāb); or without it (i.e., without prevention from leaving), it is recommendation (nadb) and desirability (istijāb). If it is a request for leaving and prevention from doing, it is prohibition (taḥrīm). If it is not prevention from doing, it is dislike (karāha). So this kind of demand and choice is not present in these stories, etc. Therefore, they will not be included in the definition of hukm. (وقد يجاب بانه لا حاجة) This is a second answer to the mentioned objection. The summary is that there is no need to add demand or choice; rather, here the 'restriction of respect' (qayd al-ḥaythiyya) is meant, i.e., 'the address of Allah the Exalted'.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the definition of hukm (legal ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The definition under discussion is: 'The address of Allah related to the actions of the responsible persons by demand or choice.' The commentator begins by clarifying each component of this definition. First, he explains the word 'address' (khitab). Originally meaning the act of directing speech to another, it is used here to refer to internal speech (kalam nafsi), which is the eternal attribute of speech in Allah. An objection arises: since internal speech is eternal and there was no addressee in eternity, how can it be called 'address'? The response distinguishes between intent to make understand (qaṣd al-ifhām) and actual making understand. In eternity, Allah intends to make understand future responsible persons, and that intent suffices for calling it address; the actual existence of the addressee is not required at the time of the intent. Next, the phrase 'related to actions of the responsible persons' is examined. It does not mean relation to all actions of all responsible persons (which is impossible), but relation to any one action of any one responsible person. This is because the definite plural in Arabic can indicate the genus, not necessarily all individuals. The commentator then addresses a subtle point: although internal speech is a single attribute, it is considered multiple because of the multiplicity of its objects of relation, so multiple addresses exist for different rulings. Then he discusses an objection: why specify 'of Allah' when obedience is also due to the Prophet and authorities? The answer: their obedience is ultimately through Allah's command, so the definition rightly restricts to Allah's address. The major objection is that the definition would include stories and reports that relate to actions of the responsible persons, such as narrative verses or the verse 'Allah created you and your actions.' These are not rulings in the technical sense (they do not demand or permit anything). To exclude them, the qualification 'by demand or choice' is added. 'Demand' includes obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and dislike; 'choice' is permissibility. Stories and reports have no such quality. Finally, a second response is mentioned: the qualification may not need explicit addition because the definition inherently implies demand/choice by the term 'address of Allah' in the context of legal rulings. The passage follows the author's order: clarifying components, addressing objections, and justifying the final form of the definition.

Key Terms
الاقتضاء (al-iqtiḍāʾ): Demand; includes obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and dislike
التخيير (al-takhyīr): Choice; the act is permissible (mubah); doing or leaving are equal
قيد الحيثية (qayd al-ḥaythiyya): Restriction of respect; a condition that is implied by the context

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the condition 'by demand or choice' added to the definition of hukm?
A) To include all divine addresses.
B) To exclude stories and reports that do not impose obligations or permissions.
C) To make the definition longer.
D) To align with the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
The addition of 'by demand or choice' is essential to exclude non-normative addresses from the definition of hukm, ensuring that only prescriptive speeches are considered legal rulings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Definition of Hukm in Hanafi Usul: Excluding Narratives and Reports
Explaining the Hanafi definition of hukm and defending it against the objection of including narratives and reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hukm and distinguish it from qisas and akhbar by applying the condition of iqtida or takhyir.

Core Idea
Hukm is divine address concerning actions by requirement or choice – narratives lack both.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the definition of hukm is precise: it is the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible individuals by way of requirement (iqtida) or choice (takhyir). This passage from Sharh al-Taozeeh wa al-Talweeh defends this definition against an objection: that it would improperly include Quranic narratives (qisas) and reports (akhbar) about actions. We will explore why these are excluded and how the Hanafi school preserves the exclusivity of the definition.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi definition of hukm
Recall the full definition: 'Khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin bi al-iqtida aw al-takhyir'. Understand the two modes: requirement (iqtida) and choice (takhyir).
iqtida covers obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and dislikability; takhyir covers permissibility.
2
Identify the objection
The objection is that this definition includes qisas (narratives of past prophets and communities) and akhbar (reports like 'Allah created you') because they also relate to actions of the mukallafin.
The objector argues that these are rulings, which is invalid.
3
Apply the exclusion: no iqtida or takhyir
Analyze that qisas do not contain a demand (iqtida) for action or forbearance, nor do they present choice (takhyir) between equal options. They are informative, not legislative.
For example, the story of Prophet Musa does not command or forbid anything in itself.
4
Consider alternative response: haythiyya (consideration)
Understand the second response: the qisas are considered from the perspective of being already realized events, not as actions of the mukallaf from the legislative perspective; thus the definition does not apply.
Even if an admonition is derived, the narrative itself is not a hukm.

اے نہیں ہے اب جتنا بھی خطابات ہیں تمام صفت واحدہ ہیں لہذا ایک ہی خطاب متعلق بجمیع افعال المكلفين ہوا تو جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ کلام نفسی اگر چہ صفت واحدہ ہے لیکن باعتبار تعدد متعلقات کے یہ متعدد ہے اس لئے خطابات متعددہ ہو جائیں گے۔ خرج خطاب الله المتعلق باحوال ذاته يه المتعلق بافعال المکلفین کا فائدہ احتراز یہ ہے۔ لا یقال اضافة الخطاب الى الله تعالیٰ یعنی اضافة خطاب الی اللہ تعالیٰ اس کی مقتضی ہے کہ قابلِ اطاعت صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا حکم ہے حالانکہ اس کے علاوہ اطاعت نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور اطاعت اولی الامر اور سید و سردار کی بھی واجب ہے تو اس اشکال کو دفع کیا کہ ان کی اطاعت انجاب الہی کے ساتھ واجب ہے تو حقیقتا حکم قابل اطاعت صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا ہوا۔
تو اعترضت على هذا التعريف اس تعریف پر یہ اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ یہ مانع از دخول غیر نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے اندر ایک تو قصص داخل ہو رہے ہیں۔ المبينة لاحوال المكلفين وافعالهم یعنی جو احوال مکلفین اور ان کے افعال کی تعیین کر رہے ہیں تو افعال تفسیر ہے احوال کی یا افعال سے مراد مقابل متروکات ہے اور احوال سے مراد متروکات ہیں یعنی وہ قصص جو مکلفین کے امور فعلیہ اور امور ترکیہ کی تبین کرتے ہیں اور دوسری وہ اخبار داخل ہو رہی ہیں جو اعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَالله خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ تو یہ خبر ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہیں اور تمہارے اعمال کو پیدا فرمایا تو یہ ایک خطاب جس کا تعلق اعمال اور افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بصورت اخبار ہے تو یہ دونوں تعریف حکم میں داخل ہو رہے ہیں حالانکہ حکم اصطلاحی کے افراد نہیں ہیں تو فَزِيدَ عَلَى التَّعْرِيفِ یعنی تعریف حکم پر اس قید کا اضافہ کے اندر تعلق نہ بالاقتضا ہے نہ بالتخیر کیونکہ تخییر کا معنی ہے کہ اس امر کا فعل اور ترک مکلف کے لئے دونوں مباح ہیں اور اقتضا کا معنی ہے طلب پھر یہ طلب اگر فعل کی ہے مع المنع عن الترک تو یہ ایجاب ہے او داخل فی تعریف الحکم نہیں ہوں گے۔ وقد يجاب بانه لا حاجة یہ اعتراض مذکور کا جواب ثانی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اقتضار تغییر کے زیادہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ یہاں قید حیثیت مراد ہے یعنی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ المتعلق يفعل المكلف من حيث هو فعل المكلف قصص و اخبار مذکورہ کا ذکر بحیثیت فعل مکلف ہونے کے لحاظ سے نہیں بلکہ بائیں حیثیت ہے کہ انھا امور صادرات عن الموجودات یعنی امور موجودہ متحققة ہونے کے لحاظ سے بایں طور کہ ایسے امور دنیا میں متحقق اور موجود ہوچکے ہیں باقی رہا یہ سوال کہ قصص کا ذکر بغرض عبرت کے ہوتا ہے تاکہ لوگ اس سے عبرت حاصل کر کے مطیعین کا راستہ اختیار کریں اور عاصی لوگوں کے افعال سے اجتناب کریں تو یہ ایک طلب ہے اس لئے تعریف حکم ان پر صادق آگئی۔ ایک جواب تو یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ مراد حیثیت یہ ہے کہ وہ اسی خطاب سے جو مذکور ہو اس کے ساتھ مکلف ہو اور قصص کے اندر یہ نہیں ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ عبرت حاصل کرنا جو اس کی غایت و حکمت ہے اس لحاظ سے یہ حکم ہے جو فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ میں درج ہے پھر بھی قصص من حیث القصص حکم میں درج نہیں ہیں۔
No, not now. All addresses are a single attribute. Therefore, one address relates to all actions of the legally responsible individuals. The answer to this is that the inner speech (kalam nafsi), although a single attribute, is multiple due to the multiplicity of its objects, so addresses become multiple. The exclusion of the address of Allah related to His own states from that related to the actions of the legally responsible individuals has the benefit of precaution. It cannot be said that adding the address to Allah Most High necessitates that only Allah's command is worthy of obedience, while obedience to the Prophet (peace be upon him), the ulu al-amr, and masters is also obligatory. So this objection is repelled by [saying] that their obedience is obligatory with the directive of Allah (in jab ilahi), so in reality only Allah's command is worthy of obedience.
Then an objection was made to this definition: it is not exclusive of others because it includes qisas (narratives) that clarify the states and actions of the legally responsible individuals. 'Af'al' is an interpretation of 'ahwal', or by 'af'al' is meant the opposite of omitted actions, and by 'ahwal' is meant the omitted actions, i.e., the qisas that explain the actions and omissions of the legally responsible individuals. Secondly, it includes akhbar (reports) related to the actions of the legally responsible individuals, such as His statement: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' This is a report that Allah created you and your actions. This is an address related to the actions of the legally responsible individuals in the form of a report. So both of these enter into the definition of hukm although they are not instances of terminological hukm. So they added to the definition a restriction that specifies it and excludes these instances. That is their statement: 'by requirement (al-iqtida) or choice (al-takhyir).' Thus hukm is called an address related to the actions of the legally responsible individuals either by requirement or by choice. In the mentioned qisas and akhbar, there is neither a relation of requirement nor choice, because the meaning of takhyir is that both doing and leaving that matter are permissible for the legally responsible individual, and the meaning of iqtida is demand. Then if this demand is for action with prohibition of leaving, it is obligation (ijab); if without prohibition of leaving, it is recommendation (nadb/istihbab). If the demand is for leaving with prohibition of action, it is prohibition (tahrim); if without prohibition of action, it is dislikability (karaha). Thus this type of requirement and choice is not in those qisas, so they will not enter the definition of hukm. And it can be answered that there is no need—this is a second answer to the mentioned objection. The summary is that there is no need to add the restriction of requirement/choice; rather here the restriction is meant by way of consideration (haythiyya), i.e., the address of Allah Most High related to the action of the legally responsible individual from the perspective that it is an action of the legally responsible individual. The mentioned qisas and akhbar are not mentioned from the perspective of being an action of the legally responsible individual, but from the perspective that they are matters emanating from existent beings (i.e., as realized matters). The question remains: qisas are mentioned for the purpose of admonition so that people may take heed and adopt the path of the obedient and avoid the actions of the disobedient; so this is a demand, thus the definition of hukm applies to them. One answer is that the intended consideration is that one is obligated by that very address which is mentioned, and in qisas this is not present. A second answer is that taking admonition, which is its purpose and wisdom, is a hukm in the sense of the verse 'So take heed, O people of insight,' yet the qisas as qisas are not included in hukm.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of 'hukm' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins by addressing a preliminary issue: the addresses (khitabat) of Allah are all a single attribute (kalam nafsi), but multiplicity arises from the diverse objects of address. The definition of hukm is 'the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible individuals by way of requirement (iqtida) or choice (takhyir)'. The passage then handles an objection that this definition includes qisas (narratives about past communities) and akhbar (reports about creation or actions) because they also relate to the actions of the legally responsible individuals. The text provides two responses: first, that the added phrase 'by requirement or choice' excludes these, because narratives and reports do not involve a demand (iqtida) nor a choice (takhyir) between equally permissible options. Second, even if one considers that narratives are mentioned for admonition implying a demand, the address in narratives is not from the perspective of being an 'action of the legally responsible individual' (which is the locus of hukm) but rather as already occurred matters; moreover, the demand for admonition is derived from another verse ("So take heed") and not from the narrative itself as a piece of legislation. Thus the definition remains valid.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): خطاب الله المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخییر (the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible individuals by requirement or choice)
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida): طلب (demand) which includes obligation (طلب فعل مع المنع عن الترک) or recommendation (طلب فعل بدون المنع), and prohibition (طلب ترک مع المنع عن الفعل) or dislikability (طلب ترک بدون المنع).
التخییر (al-takhyir): تساوی الفعل والترک (equal permissibility of action and abandonment), i.e., ibaha (permissibility).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main response to the objection that qisas and akhbar enter the definition of hukm?
A) They are not related to actions.
B) They do not involve iqtida or takhyir.
C) They are not divine address.
D) They are only for past generations.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm is exclusive: only divine addresses that demand or permit actions constitute rulings, excluding informative narratives and reports.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Mu'tazila Objections to the Definition of Hukm and the Ash'ari Responses
Explaining the three objections of the Mu'tazila and the Ash'ari responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Ash'ari/Hanafi distinction between the eternal hukm and its originated relation (ta'alluq) to evaluate the Mu'tazila's three objections.

Core Idea
Hukm is eternal divine speech; only its relation to acts is originated — this distinction refutes the Mu'tazila.

The Mu'tazila challenged the standard definition of hukm on three fronts: its origination, the use of 'aw', and its comprehensiveness. This lesson walks through each objection and the Ash'ari/Hanafi response, clarifying key usul distinctions that protect the eternity of divine speech while accounting for temporal rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of hukm under debate
Recall that hukm is defined as 'the speech of Allah related to the acts of the legally responsible by demand or choice.' This definition is the target of Mu'tazila criticism.
The definition uses khaṭāb (internal speech) which is eternal.
2
Enumerate the three Mu'tazila objections
Identify each objection: (1) hukm is originated, so cannot be defined by something eternal; (2) 'aw' introduces doubt; (3) the definition is not comprehensive.
The objections challenge the definition's coherence and scope.
3
Analyze the first objection and the response distinguishing hukm from ta'alluq
The Mu'tazila argue hukm is originated because it is described as coming after non-existence and is caused by originated causes. The Ash'ari response denies that hukm itself is originated; only its relation (ta'alluq) to the act is originated. The hukm itself remains eternal.
Key example: 'She became permissible' refers to the relation of permissibility, not the hukm itself.
4
Analyze the second objection on 'aw' and its usage for division
The Mu'tazila claim 'aw' implies doubt, which contradicts the purpose of definition. The response explains that 'aw' here is for division (tanyī'), used when a definition covers multiple distinct types, which is valid.
In definitions, 'aw' can indicate variety, not doubt.
5
Analyze the third objection and how conditional rulings are included
The Mu'tazila say conditional rulings (causes, conditions, preventers) are not covered by 'demand' or 'choice'. The response argues they are implicitly included, or the definition is supplemented. The text notes the author did not omit preventiveness in the original.
Conditional rulings are either subsumed under demand/choice or indicated by additional phrasing.
