تقسیم اور تنوریع و تفصیل
Concerning the relation to the act of the legally responsible person in terms of it being an act of the legally responsible: the mention of stories and news is not in terms of being an act of the legally responsible, but rather in terms that they are matters emanating from existing things, i.e., as existent and realized matters in this world, in that such matters have occurred and existed in the world. As for the question that stories are mentioned for the purpose of admonition so that people may take heed and choose the path of the obedient and avoid the actions of the disobedient, this is a demand, so the definition of hukm applies to them. One answer given is that the intended aspect is that they are addressed by the same speech that is mentioned, and in stories this is not the case. Another answer is that taking admonition, which is its purpose and wisdom, is a hukm included in 'So take heed, O people of insight', but still, stories as such are not included in hukm. He said: 'And some added: The Mu'tazila objected to the mentioned definition of hukm, i.e., the speech of Allah the Exalted related to the acts of the legally responsible by demand or choice, with three objections. First: That speech (khiṭāb) means internal speech (kalām nafsī) which according to you is eternal, while hukm is originated. Using the eternal in the definition of the originated is not correct. It is said: Hukm is originated, speech is eternal, and it is not permissible to use the eternal in the definition of the originated. So your definition is not sound. The claim that hukm is originated is argued by two reasons: First, because it is described as being obtained after non-existence, i.e., hukm is described as being obtained after non-existence; it did not exist and then came into existence, and whatever is preceded by non-existence is originated. For example, it is said: 'She became permissible after she was not permissible', meaning the woman was not permissible, then after that she became permissible, and the state of permissibility is a hukm that occurs after non-existence, so it is originated. The second reason: because it is caused by an originated cause, i.e., it is an effect of an originated cause, as it is said: 'She became permissible by marriage and impermissible by divorce.' So permissibility by marriage and impermissibility by divorce are causes, both are originated. Since the effect comes after the cause, whatever comes into existence after what is originated is a fortiori originated, so hukm is originated. So how can it be correct to define it with the eternal? Second objection: The definition includes the word 'or' (aw), which is used for doubt and hesitation, i.e., to express doubt or to cause doubt in another. This contradicts definition, because the purpose of definition is to give knowledge of the defined, while doubt and hesitation cause ambiguity, which contradicts definition. Third objection: It is not comprehensive. This third objection is that this definition of hukm is not comprehensive of all individuals, because it does not include conditional rulings such as causality of the sun's decline for the obligation of prayer, conditionality of purity for prayer, and impurity being a preventer of prayer, because in these there is neither demand nor choice, although they are individuals of hukm. Therefore the definition is not comprehensive. And the author omitted in the explanation of 'aw'—meaning the author omitted mentioning preventiveness (māni‘iyya) in the explanation of situational speech (khiṭāb waḍ‘ī), although it was necessary. According to custom, this is an objection to the author. However, in the text, the author after mentioning causality and conditionality mentioned the word 'and' (wa) to indicate preventiveness etc., so the author did not omit it, but the commentator did not pay attention. The Ash'aris responded to the first objection by denial: We do not concede that hukm is described as being obtained after non-existence. Rather, the relation (ta‘alluq) of hukm is obtained after non-existence, and the relation of hukm is originated, while the hukm itself is eternal. The meaning of 'she became permissible after she was not permissible' is the relation of permissibility to the woman after it was not related, i.e., the relation of permissibility to the woman was not present before, and when marriage occurred, permissibility became related to her. So the relation is originated, not the hukm. And they deny the causation of hukm: This is the response to the second reason of the first objection. The word 'cause' (illah) is used in two senses: one is effective cause (mu’aththira), i.e., the cause that has effect in the existence of the effect, i.e., brings it from non-existence to existence. The second is cause in the sense of indicator and sign (amārah wa ‘alāma). Its function is not effecting, but it is a sign indicating the existence of the effect. An originated effective cause cannot exist for an eternal, but an originated sign can. For example, the existence of the universe is a sign (cause of knowledge) for the existence of an eternal Creator. Similarly, here marriage is a sign indicating permissibility, and divorce is a sign indicating impermissibility. Because shar‘ī acts are indicators and signs, not necessitators and effectors. Regarding the second objection: The word 'or' here—this is the response to the second objection. Its summary is that the word 'or' has two types: one is for division (tanyī‘), i.e., when a thing has multiple different types and kinds, the word 'or' is used to express them. Its use in definitions is correct when the defined has different types and kinds; then 'or' is used for division, because it becomes difficult to combine different types in one definition. So here 'or' is for division and detail.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Ash'ari/Hanafi position and the Mu'tazila over the definition of hukm (legal ruling). The definition under discussion is 'the speech of Allah related to the acts of the legally responsible by demand or choice.' The Mu'tazila raise three objections: (1) The definition uses 'speech' which is eternal (kalām nafsi), but hukm is originated (hadith) because it is described as coming into existence after non-existence and is caused by originated causes. (2) The word 'or' (aw) introduces ambiguity, contrary to the purpose of definition. (3) The definition is not comprehensive because it excludes conditional rulings like causality, conditionality, and preventiveness. The Ash'ari responses are: (1) Deny that hukm is originated; rather, the relation (ta'alluq) of hukm to acts is originated, but hukm itself is eternal. Also, what appears as causation (like marriage causing permissibility) is actually indication (amarah), not effective causation. (2) 'Or' here is used for division (tanyī') to indicate different types, which is appropriate in definitions when the defined has multiple varieties. (3) The definition is comprehensive because conditional rulings are implicitly included under 'demand' or 'choice', or the author later adds a word to include them. The text also notes a criticism that the author omitted mentioning 'preventiveness' in the explanation, but the commentator defends that the author's text included an indication. The Ash'ari responses uphold the original definition.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): The speech of Allah related to the acts of the legally responsible by demand or choice.
الخطاب (al-khiṭāb): Internal speech (kalām nafsi), which is eternal according to Hanafis.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand for an act (obligation or prohibition).
التخيير (al-takhyir): Choice (permissibility).
أو (aw): Used for division (tanyī') in definitions, not for doubt.
العلة (al-'illah): Two meanings: effective cause (mu'aththira) or indicator/sign (amarah/‘alama). Here, in shar‘, it is indicator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari/Hanafi response to the Mu'tazila's first objection, what is originated (hadith)?
A) The hukm itself
B) The relation (ta'alluq) of hukm to the act
C) The divine speech (kalam nafsi)
D) The attribute of Allah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi/Ash'ari distinction between eternal hukm and originated relation (ta'alluq) is essential to defend the definition of hukm and preserve the immutability of divine attributes.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
The Definition of Hukm and the Inclusion of Declaratory Rulings
Responding to objection about definition excluding declaratory rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Ash'ari positions on including al-hukm al-wad'i in the definition of hukm and explain the Hanafi justification for adding 'aw al-wad''.

Core Idea
Taklifi and wad'i are distinct concepts; both must be explicitly stated in the definition of hukm.

The definition of hukm shari'i is a foundational issue in usul al-fiqh. A key point of contention is whether al-ahkam al-wad'iyya (declaratory rulings like cause, condition, preventer) are included when the definition uses only 'demand or option'. This passage presents three Ash'ari responses to the objection that the definition excludes wad'i, and defends the Hanafi position that the definition must explicitly include 'aw al-wad''. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skills in analyzing definitions and appreciating how terminological precision affects legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core objection
Recognize that the initial definition – 'the address of Allah by demand or option' – is criticised for excluding declaratory rulings (ahkam wad'iyya). The objection is that the definition is not comprehensive.
2
Outline the three Ash'ari groups
Group 1: Accept the exclusion and add 'aw al-wad''. Group 2: Deny that wad'i addresses are rulings at all. Group 3: Accept wad'i as rulings but generalize iqtida' to include implied demand, thus covering wad'i without adding a term.
The commentator erroneously combined groups 1 and 3.
3
Analyse the Hanafi position
The author (Hanafi) rejects group 3's generalization because taklifi and wad'i are distinct concepts (مفهومان متغايران). Separate mention is necessary; one cannot be subsumed under the other.
The Hanafi dalil is conceptual distinctness, not textual.
4
Examine the commentator's error
The commentator (sharih) misattributes the third group's view to the first group, leading to an invalid critique. The author's argument correctly targets only those who accept wad'i as ruling but refuse to add the term.
This highlights the importance of accurately representing opposing positions in usul debates.
5
Conclude with the mu'tamad definition
The accepted Hanafi definition is: خطاب الله المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخيير او الوضع. This ensures full coverage of both taklifi and wad'i rulings.

محدود کے لئے ہے کیونکہ ایک حکم ایسا ہے جس کا تعلق فعل مکلف سے اقتضائی اور طلبی ہوتا ہے اور دوسرا قسم ایسا ہے جس کا تعلق تیری ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس تفصیل انواع کو پیش کرنے کے لئے استعمال او ضروری تھا اور دوسرا قسم او کا برائے تشکیک و تردد کے لئے ہے اس قسم کا کلمہ او تعریف میں استعمال کرنا صحیح نہیں ہوتا ۔ خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ یہ کلمہ او تنویعیہ ہے جس کا استعمال کر نا تعریف میں صحیح ہے اور یہ او تشکیکیہ نہیں جس کی استعمال تعریف میں صحیح نہیں ہوتی ۔
اما الثالث فالتن مه یہ اعتراض ثالث کے جواب کی تفصیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے التزام اور تسلیم کر لیا کہ یہ تعریف حکم احکام وضعیہ کو شامل نہیں ہے لہذا یہ جامع نہیں ہے تو انہوں نے بقصد شمول و جامعیت اوا لوضع کی قید زیادہ کر دی تا کہ احکام وضعیہ کو شامل ہو کر تعریف جامع ہو جائے تو حکم کی تعریف ان حضرات کے نز دیک خطاب اللہ تعالى المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخير او الوضع ہوگی یہ اشاعرہ کا ایک فریق ہوا۔ واجاب بعضهم بعض اشاعرہ نے اس اعتراض کا جوا یہ دیا کہ ہم سرے سے تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے کہ خطاب وضع حکم ہے اور ہم اس خطاب کا نام حکم ہی نہیں رکھتے اگرچہ ہمارے علاوہ بعض حضرات نے اس کا حکم ہونا تسلیم کر لیا ہے تو یہ صرف ان ہی کی اصطلاح ہے۔ فلا مشاحة في الاصطلاح لہذا ان ہی پر تغییر تعریف لازم ہے ہمارے اوپر لازم نہیں یہ اشاعرہ کا دوسرا گروہ ہے۔ ولو سلم فلا نسلمان شارح نے اس تسلیمی جواب کو اس دوسرے فریق کی طرف منسوب کر دیا یعنی پہلا جواب ان کی طرف سے عدم تسلیمی تھا اور ان ہی کی طرف سے یہ تسلیمی جواب ہے حالانکہ یہ صحیح نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ اشاعرہ کا تیسرا فریق ہے جو خطاب وضعی کا حکم ہونا تو تسلیم کرتا ہے لیکن او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کرنے کی ضرورت تسلیم نہیں کرتا بلکہ اقتضاء کی تعمیم کرکے ان خطابات کو اقتضا ، ضمنی میں ترج کرتا ہے تو یہ درحقیقت وہی حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ فلانسلو خروجها عن الحد يعني ان خطابات وضعیه کا خروج از تعریف حکم ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کیونکہ ہماری مراد بالاقتضاء، والتغییر سے عام ہے خواہ صریح ہو یا ضمنی تو خطاب وضع اقتضاء ضمنی کے قبیلہ سے ہے اور اسی میں درج ہے کیونکہ سبینہ دلوک سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس وقت نماز واجب ہے اور شرطیہ طہارت کا معنی یہ ہے کہ صلوٰۃ میں طہارت واجب ہے اور بدون الطہارت نماز کا ادا کر نا حرام ہے اور مانعیت نجاست سے مقصود یہ ہے کہ نجاست کے ہوتے ہوئے ادائیگی نماز حرام ہے یا یہ کہ حالتِ صلوٰۃ میں اس کا ازالہ واجب ہے کذا في جميع الاسباب والشور والمواقع تو تمام اسباب اور شروط و موانع میں یہی تاویل کر کے اقتضاء ضمنی میں درج کیا جائے گا تو ا و الوضع کی قید کے اضافہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ۔ اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس بارہ میں اشاعرہ کے تین گروہ ہیں ایک وہ جنہوں نے الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ تسلیم کر لیا دوسرا گروہ وہ ہے جنہوں نے سرے سے خطاب وضع کا حکم ہونا تسلیم ہی نہیں کیا اور نہ قید اوا لوضع کا اضافہ کیا تیسرا گروہ وہ ہے جو خطاب وضع کو حکم ہونا تو تسلیم کرتا ہے لیکن او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ نہیں کرتا بلکہ اقتصار کی تعمیم کر کے خطاب و صنعی کو اقتضا ضمنی میں درج کرتا ہے کما قال عضد الدین فی شرح مختصر الاصول ان الاشاعرة في هذا المقام ثلاث فرق منهم من يسم الوضعى حكما ومنهم من سماه حكما و زاد قيد الوضع ومنهم من سماه حكما و اورجر فيه بجعل الاقتضاء اعم من المريح والضمنی مصنف نے فرقہ اولیٰ جو خطاب وضعی کو حکم ہی نہیں کہتا ان کا سرے سے ذکر ہی نہیں کیا اور فرقہ ثانیہ کی رائے یعنی اوالوضع کے اضافہ کو اختیار کیا فرقہ مثاللہ کی رائے یعنی اقتضاء کی تعمیم کو رد کیا شارح نے فرقہ اولیٰ اور ثالثہ کو ایک قرار دے دیا اور انت خبیر سے حسب عادت مصنف " پر رد کرنا شروع کر دیا جس کی کوئی حقیقت اس صورت میں باقی نہیں رہتی کماستری ۔ ذهب المصنف الى ان الحق یعنی مصنف نے اسی رائے کو اختیار کیا کہ جب خطاب وضعی کو حکم ھے تسلیم کیا جاتا ہے تو پھر او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کر نا حق ہے کیونکہ خطاب دو قسم ہے ایک تکلیفی اور دوسرا وضعی۔ فلما ذكر احدهما هو التكليفي جو کہ بلفظ الاقتضاء او التخيير مذکور ہے وجب ذكر الاخر عني خطاب وضعی کا ذکر کر نا بھی ضروری ہے لہذا او الوضع کی قید زیادہ کرنی چاہیئے اور اس کی کوئی وجہ نہیں کہ اقتضاء و تخییر جو کہ حکم تکلیفی کی تعبیر ہے اس میں اسے درج کیا جائے۔ لانھما مفهومان متغایران یعنی یہ دونوں باعتبار مفہوم کے متغایر ہیں اور ایک کا بعض صور میں دوسرے کے ساتھ لزوم کا ہو جاتا اس کی دلیل نہیں ہے کہ دونوں آپس میں متحد ہیں لہذا ان دونوں انواع کا الگ الگ عبارت کے ساتھ ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے۔ وانت خبير بانه لا توجیه یعنی مصنف نے جو کچھ ذکر کیا ہے یہ اشاعرہ کی اس کلام کی توجیہ کسی صورت میں نہیں ہو سکتی ۔ اما اولا اولا یہ کہ خصم یعنی اشاعرہ خطاب وضعی کا حکم ہوتا سرے سے تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتا اور بعض اقسام خطاب یعنی ما سو اخطاب وضع کو حکم کہتا ہے تو اس پر کیسے واجب ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ اوالوضع کی قید کا ذکر کرے بلکہ اس کے نزدیک اس قید کا ذکر صحیح ہی نہیں ہوسکتا آپ کو تفصیل سابقہ سے معلوم ہوچکا ہے کہ یہ اشاعرہ کا گروہ اول ہے جس کا مصنف نے بالکل ذکر ہی نہیں کیا اور نہ ان پر رد کیا اور نہ ان کی کلام کی توجیہ کی لہذا شارح کی یہ بحث بالکل ساقط ہے۔ اما ثانيا فلانه يمنع دیکھیئے کہ شارح اس ثانی بحث کو گروہ اول کی رائے سمجھ کر اعتراض کر رہا ہے حالانکہ یہ فرقہ ثالثہ کی رائے تھی کہ خطاب وضع کو حکم تسلیم کرتے تھے لیکن او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ نہیں کرتے
It is for the defined because there is one ruling that relates to the act of the mukallaf in terms of demand and request, and another type that relates to placement. Therefore, to present this detail of types, the use of 'aw' was necessary. The second type of 'aw' is for hesitation and doubt; this type of word 'aw' is not correct to use in a definition. The summary of the answer is that this word 'aw' is divisional (tanwi'iyya), the use of which in definition is correct, and it is not 'aw' of doubt (tashkikiyya) whose use in definition is not correct. As for the third, al-tanwiyah: This is the detail of the response to the third objection. The summary is that some Ash'aris conceded and accepted that this definition does not include declaratory rulings (ahkam wad'iyya), so it is not comprehensive. Therefore, with the intention of inclusion and comprehensiveness, they added the condition of al-wad' so that it would include declaratory rulings and the definition would become comprehensive. Thus the definition of hukm according to these people would be: 'The address of Allah Almighty related to the acts of the mukallafin by demand, option, or placement (bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir aw al-wad').' This is one group of Ash'aris. And some of them answered: Some Ash'aris responded to this objection by saying that we do not at all accept that declaratory address (khitab wad') is a ruling, and we do not name this address as a ruling, although besides us some people have accepted it as a ruling, so it is only their terminology. There is no dispute in terminology. Therefore, altering the definition is required upon them, not upon us. This is the second group of Ash'aris. 'And if we concede, we do not concede': The commentator (sharih) attributed this concessive response to this second group, meaning the first response from them was non-acceptance, and the same group gave this concessive response, but this is not correct. Rather, this is a third group of Ash'aris who accept that declaratory address is a ruling, but do not accept the need to add the condition of al-wad'. Instead, they generalize the meaning of iqtida' and include these addresses in implied demand (iqtida' dimni). So indeed, these people say that we do not accept its exclusion from the definition. That is, we do not accept the exclusion of declaratory addresses from the definition of hukm, because by iqtida' and takhyir we mean general, whether explicit or implicit. So declaratory address (khitab wad') falls under implied demand and is included therein, because the meaning of 'sun's rising' is that prayer is obligatory at that time, and the meaning of 'purity as a condition' is that purity is obligatory in prayer and performing prayer without purity is prohibited, and the meaning of 'impurity as a preventer' is that performing prayer while impurity exists is prohibited, or that its removal during prayer is obligatory. Likewise in all causes (asbab), conditions (shurut), and preventers (mawani'), this interpretation will be applied and included under implied demand. So there is no need to add the condition of al-wad'. From this detail, it becomes known that there are three groups of Ash'aris in this matter: one group who accepted the addition of the condition of al-wad'; a second group who did not accept declaratory address as a ruling at all and did not add the condition of al-wad'; a third group who accept declaratory address as a ruling but do not add the condition of al-wad', rather they generalize the meaning of iqtida' and include declaratory address under implied demand, as said by 'Adud al-Din in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Usul: 'Indeed the Ash'aris in this context are three groups: some who do not call wad'i a ruling; some who call it a ruling and add the condition of wad'; and some who call it a ruling but interpret it by making iqtida' general including explicit and implied.' The author (musannif) did not mention the first group at all, who do not call declaratory address a ruling, and he adopted the opinion of the second group, i.e., the addition of al-wad', and rejected the opinion of the third group, i.e., the generalization of iqtida'. The commentator (sharih) combined the first and third groups as one, and began to refute the author according to his usual manner with 'and you are informed' (wa anta khabir), which has no reality left in this case as has been unveiled. 'The author held that the truth is...': That is, the author adopted this opinion: when declaratory address is accepted as a ruling, then adding the condition of al-wad' is correct, because address (khitab) is of two types: one is taklifi (obligatory) and the other is wad'i (declaratory). So when one of them is mentioned, which is taklifi, expressed by the terms iqtida' or takhyir, it is necessary to mention the other, i.e., declaratory address must be mentioned. Therefore, the condition of al-wad' should be added, and there is no reason to include it in iqtida' and takhyir, which are expressions for taklifi ruling. Because they are two distinct concepts; the fact that one sometimes accompanies the other in some cases is not evidence that they are united. Hence it is necessary to mention both types with separate phrases. 'And you are informed that there is no justification': That is, whatever the author has mentioned cannot be a justification for this statement of the Ash'aris in any way. Firstly, because the opponent, i.e., the Ash'ari, does not accept at all that declaratory address is a ruling, and calls only some types of address, i.e., other than declaratory, as ruling. So how can it be required of him to mention the condition of al-wad'? Rather, according to him, mentioning this condition is not even correct. You have learned from the previous detail that this is the first group of Ash'aris, which the author did not mention at all, nor did he refute them, nor did he justify their statement. Therefore, the commentator's discussion is completely invalid. Secondly, because it prevents... Look: the commentator, thinking that this second discussion is the opinion of the first group, is objecting, whereas it was the opinion of the third group, who accept declaratory address as a ruling but do not add the condition of al-wad'.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the definition of hukm (legal ruling) and whether it includes al-hukm al-wad'i (declaratory rulings such as cause, condition, preventer). The context is a commentary on a definition given by the author (musannif) which likely was: 'The address of Allah ... by demand or option' (bi'l-iqtida' aw al-takhyir). The objection is that this excludes wad'i rulings. The passage presents three Ash'ari responses. The first group (some Ash'aris) concede the exclusion and add 'or placement' (aw al-wad') to the definition. The second group rejects that wad'i addresses are rulings at all, so no modification needed in their view. The third group accepts they are rulings but interprets iqtida' broadly to include implied demand, thus incorporating wad'i under iqtida' without adding a separate term. The commentator (sharih) mistakenly conflates the first and third groups, while the author had already chosen the second group's addition (aw al-wad') as correct. The commentator then criticizes the author for not addressing the first group, but the author's argument stands because the first group does not even accept wad'i as ruling, so no addition is required from them. The author's position is that since taklifi and wad'i are distinct concepts, they must be listed separately in the definition. This follows the Hanafi method of precise terminology in usul, ensuring the definition is comprehensive and unambiguous.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): The address of Allah Almighty related to the acts of the mukallafin by demand, option, or placement (خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخيير او الوضع)
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand (talab) for an act, either explicit (صريح) or implied (ضمني)
الوضع (al-wad'): Placement, referring to declaratory rulings such as cause, condition, preventer
التخيير (al-takhyir): Option, giving the mukallaf a choice (e.g., mubah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Hanafi school insist on adding 'aw al-wad'' to the definition of hukm?
A) Because declaratory rulings are not rulings according to some scholars.
B) Because taklifi and wad'i are distinct concepts that require separate mention.
C) Because the third Ash'ari group's generalization of iqtida' is invalid.
D) Because the commentator combined the first and third groups incorrectly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm explicitly includes declaratory rulings (aw al-wad') because taklifi and wad'i are distinct concepts that cannot be subsumed under one term.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Necessity of Including al-Wad' in the Definition of Hukm Shar'i
Analyzing the necessity of adding the qualifier 'wad'i' to the definition of hukm shar'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school insists on including the qualifier 'al-wad'' in the definition of hukm shar'i and analyze the Ash'ari disagreement.

Core Idea
Hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are distinct types; subsuming one under the other conflates their necessary concomitants.

In usul al-fiqh, the definition of hukm shar'i is contested. Some later Ash'aris attempted to define it simply as divine address, while Hanafis insist on distinguishing between hukm taklifi (obligation/permission) and hukm wad'i (cause, condition, validity). This passage from al-Tawdih defends the necessity of adding the qualifier 'al-wad'', arguing that the two categories are distinct in reality and cannot be merged. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the structure of Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Ash'ari positions
List the three groups: 1) Denies wad'i address is a ruling; 2) Accepts wad'i as a ruling but adds the qualifier; 3) Accepts wad'i as a ruling but subsumes it under hukm taklifi by generalizing iqtida.
The author adopts position 2 and rebuts position 3. The first group is dismissed.
2
Understand the author's main argument
The author argues that when hukm taklifi is mentioned by iqtida or takhyir, hukm wad'i must be mentioned separately because they are two different types of address. The mere fact that they often accompany each other does not make them identical.
This is the core of the Hanafi insistence on including al-wad' in the definition.
3
Analyze the commentator's error
The commentator (Taftazani) mistakenly conflates the first and third groups, then criticizes the author for not addressing the first group. The text rebuts that the author only rebutted the third group, and the commentator's criticism is invalid.
This clarifies the structure of the discourse.
4
Recognize the distinction of necessary concomitants
The author uses 'al-mafhum min' (concept derived from) to refer to necessary concomitants, not definitions. Hukm wad'i yields 'connection of one thing to another' as a necessary concomitant, while hukm taklifi yields 'obligation or prohibition' – these are mutually exclusive, proving the categories are distinct.
This logical move avoids the charge of inaccuracy.
5
Apply the argument to modern usul reasoning
Consider how this distinction affects the classification of rulings: for example, the validity of a contract (hukm wad'i) is separate from the obligation to fulfill it (hukm taklifi). Mixing them leads to confusion.

او الوضع کی قید زیادہ کرنی چاہیئے اور اس کی کوئی وجہ نہیں کہ اقتضاء و تخییر جو کہ حکم تکلیفی کی تعبیر ہے اس میں اسے درج کیا جائے۔ لانھما مفهومان متغایران یعنی یہ دونوں باعتبار مفہوم کے متغایر ہیں اور نے بالکل ذکر ہی نہیں کیا اور نہ ان پر رد کیا اور نہ ان کی کلام کی توجیہ کی لہذا شارح کی یہ بحث بالکل ساقط ہے۔ اما ثانيا فلانه يمنع دیکھیئے کہ شارح اس ثانی بحث کو گروہ اول کی رائے سمجھ کر اعتراض کر رہا ہے حالانکہ یہ فرقہ ثالثہ کی رائے تھی کہ خطاب وضع کو حکم تسلیم کرتے تھے لیکن او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ نہیں کرتے تھے بلکہ اقتضا ضمنی میں درج کر کے خطاب تکلیفی میں داخل کرتے تھے ان پہ مصنف نے رد کیا ہے بقوله لان المفهوم من الحكم الوضعي تعلق شي بشئ آخر اس عبارت کے ساتھ مصنف صرف تفایر مفہوم نہیں بتلا رہا بلکہ یہ ثابت کر رہا ہے کہ حکم تکلیفی اور حکم وضعی نوعان مقباسنان و حقیقتان مختلفان فكيف يندرج اور یہ دونوں لازم آپس میں متباین ہیں اور تباین لوازم دلیل ہوتا ہے تبدین ملزومات کی تو جب خطاب وضعی اور خطاب تکلیفی آپس میں متباستین ہیں تو ایک متباین کے اندر تعمیم کر کے دوسرے متبائن کو اس میں داخل له في تغاير مفهو ميهما یہاں صرف تغایر مفہو مین نہیں ہے بلکہ تباین مفہومین ہے لہذا ایک متباین دوسرے متبائن کو شامل نہیں ہو سکتا فيلزم ضرر عدم الجامعية كيف يتحد مفهوم العام والخاص ليس بينها عموم و خصوص بل بينهما تباين على ان المفهوم من الخطاب الوضعي یہ اعتراض بھی فضول ہے کیونکہ مصنف " خطاب وضعی کا مفہوم و معنی پیش نہیں کر رہا بلکہ اس کا لازم پیش کر رہا ہے جو ملزوم سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے اور حکمین کے لازمین مقباستین پیش کر کے ملزومین کے تباین کو ثابت کر رہا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ المفہوم من الحكم الوضعي و المفہوم من التكليفی کہا ہے مفہوم الحكم الوضعی و مفہوم التکلیفی نہیں کہا۔ اب شارح کا اعتراض بالتسامح مندفع ہے۔ قال المصنف في التوضيح وبعضهم عرف الحكم الشرعي بهذا اى بعض المتأخرين الخ متابعین اشعری میں سے بعض متأخرین محکم شرعی کی یہی تعریف مذکورہ کی۔ انہوں نے کہا حکم شرعی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ انا کا نام ہے یعنی بعض حضرات کے نزدیک خطاب اللہ تعالٰی مطلق حکم کی تعریف تھی کمام سابقاً اور بعض متأخرين من الاشاعرہ کے نزدیک یہ تعریف مطلق حکم کی نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تعریف صرف
There are those who accepted the addition of the restriction of al-wad'. The second group is those who did not accept at all that wad'i address is a ruling and did not add the restriction of al-wad'. The third group is those who accept that wad'i address is a ruling but do not add the restriction of al-wad'; rather they generalize iqtida and include wad'i address under implicit iqtida. As 'Adud al-Din said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Usul: 'The Ash'aris in this context are three groups: some do not call wad'i a ruling; some call it a ruling and add the restriction of al-wad'; some call it a ruling and include it by making iqtida general...' The author did not mention the first group at all, and he chose the opinion of the second group (adding al-wad') and rejected the opinion of the third group (generalizing iqtida). The commentator merged the first and third groups and began to criticise the author in his usual manner with 'you are aware', which has no reality in this case. The author adopted the correct opinion: when wad'i address is accepted as a ruling, then adding the restriction of al-wad' is correct because address is of two types: taklifi and wad'i. So when one of them (taklifi) is mentioned by the words iqtida or takhyir, mentioning the other (wad'i address) is also necessary, so the restriction of al-wad' should be added. There is no reason to include it in iqtida and takhyir which are expressions of hukm taklifi, because they are two distinct concepts. Sometimes one may accompany the other in some cases, but that does not prove they are identical; so it is necessary to mention both types separately. 'You are aware that there is no justification' - meaning what the author mentioned cannot justify the Ash'ari statement. Firstly, because the opponent (the Ash'aris) does not accept wad'i address as a ruling at all, and calls only some types of address (other than wad'i) as ruling, so how can he be required to mention the restriction of al-wad'? Rather, according to him, mentioning that restriction is not even valid. You have already known from the previous detail that this is the first group which the author did not mention at all, nor did he refute them or justify their statement; hence the commentator's discussion is completely invalid. Secondly, because it is prevented - see, the commentator is objecting thinking this second discussion is the opinion of the first group, whereas it was the opinion of the third group: they accepted wad'i address as a ruling but did not add the restriction of al-wad'; rather they included it under implicit iqtida and made it part of taklifi address. The author refuted them with his statement: 'Because the concept of hukm wad'i is the connection of one thing to another.' With this phrase, the author is not merely indicating the difference of concepts, but is proving that hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are two distinct types with different realities; how can one be included in the other? For two distinct things cannot be included in each other. The author, while pointing to this distinction, says that 'the concept from hukm wad'i is connection of one thing to another' - he is not presenting the meaning of hukm wad'i, but rather its necessary concomitant. So he says 'the concept from hukm wad'i', meaning what is understood from hukm wad'i as a necessary concomitant is the connection of one thing to another; it is not intended that the meaning of wad'i address is this. Hence the commentator's subsequent discussion in which he accuses the author of inaccuracy becomes invalid. And from hukm taklifi, as a necessary concomitant, this concept of connection of one thing to another is not obtained; rather, what is understood from it as a necessary concomitant is the obligation or prohibition of an act, and these two concomitants are distinct. The distinction of concomitants proves the distinction of the things accompanied. So when hukm wad'i and hukm taklifi are distinct from each other, how can one distinct thing be included in another by generalization? Now the commentator's justification that 'taklifi address is more general and includes it' is useless, because how can one distinct thing include another distinct thing? Therefore, there is merely a difference of concepts here; in fact there is a distinction of concepts. So one distinct thing cannot include another, leading to the harm of lack of universality. The objection about how the concept of general and particular can be unified is also futile because there is no general-particular relationship between them; rather there is distinction. Moreover, the concept from wad'i address... this objection is also unnecessary because the author is not presenting the meaning of wad'i address, but rather its necessary concomitant, which is understood from the accompanied thing. He presents the distinct concomitants of the two rulings to prove the distinction of the accompanied things. That is why he said 'the concept from hukm wad'i' and 'the concept from hukm taklifi', not 'the concept of hukm wad'i' and 'the concept of hukm taklifi'. Hence the commentator's objection of inaccuracy is repelled. The author said in al-Tawdih: 'And some define hukm shar'i as this' - i.e., some later followers of Ash'ari defined hukm shar'i with this mentioned definition. They said that hukm shar'i is the name of the address of Allah ta'ala. That is, according to some, the address of Allah was the definition of absolute ruling as mentioned earlier, and according to some later Ash'aris, this definition is not of absolute ruling but rather only of...
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is an expansion and explanation of a definitional issue in usul al-fiqh: whether the qualifier 'al-wad'' (linguistic/firmative) must be added when defining 'hukm shar'i' (legal ruling). The author, Sadr al-Shari'a (in al-Tawdih), holds that it must, because hukm wad'i and hukm taklifi are distinct categories. The commentator (presumably Taftazani in al-Talwih) had criticized this, but the text defends the author's position.

The passage first outlines three Ash'ari views: (1) wad'i address is not a ruling at all; (2) it is a ruling but requires the qualifier 'wad'i'; (3) it is a ruling but can be subsumed under hukm taklifi by generalizing the term 'iqtida' (requirement). The author of al-Tawdih adopts the second view and rejects the third. The commentator mistakenly conflates the first and third groups. The text then provides a logical argument: since hukm taklifi (expressed by iqtida or takhyir) and hukm wad'i are two different types of address, they must be mentioned separately. Their frequent co-occurrence does not make them identical. The commentator's objection that the first group rejects wad'i rulings entirely is irrelevant because the author did not address that group. The third group's attempt to include wad'i under taklifi via a generalized iqtida is invalid because the concepts (and their necessary concomitants) are mutually distinct. Hukm wad'i necessarily implies a connection between two things (e.g., cause and effect, condition and conditioned), while hukm taklifi implies obligation or prohibition. These are distinct concomitants, proving the distinctness of the rulings themselves. Therefore, they cannot be subsumed under one another. The author's use of 'al-mafhum min' (the concept from) rather than 'mafhum' (the concept of) indicates he is referring to necessary concomitants, not direct definitions, thus avoiding inaccuracy. Finally, the passage notes that some later Ash'aris defined hukm shar'i simply as 'the address of Allah', but this is not accepted as a definition of absolute ruling.

Key Terms
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): A ruling that establishes a relationship between two things, such as cause and effect, condition and conditioned, or validity and invalidity.
حكم تكليفي (hukm taklifi): A ruling that imposes an obligation, prohibition, or option (iqtida or takhyir) on the mukallaf.
اقتضاء (iqtida): Requirement or demand; used to express a commanding or prohibiting aspect of hukm taklifi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i?
A) They are identical in meaning.
B) They are distinct types; one cannot be included in the other.
C) Hukm wad'i is a subset of hukm taklifi.
D) Hukm taklifi is a subset of hukm wad'i.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition of Hukm Shar'i: The Fuqaha's Technical Usage
Presenting the definition of hukm shar'i and addressing objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Ash'ari definition of hukm shar'i as 'khitab Allah' and the Hanafi fuqaha's definition as 'ma thabata bi al-khitab', and explain why the latter is more comprehensive, especially regarding rulings for non-mukallafin.

Core Idea
Hanafi fuqaha define hukm as the result of divine address, not the address itself.

This lesson delves into the fundamental definition of hukm shar'i (shar'i ruling), a core concept in Usul al-Fiqh. We will explore two competing definitions: that of later Ash'ari scholars who define it as 'the address of Allah' (khitab Allah), and that of the Hanafi fuqaha who define it as 'what is established by the address' (ma thabata bi al-khitab). The passage explains the linguistic and technical reasoning behind the Hanafi position and highlights a critical objection to the Ash'ari definition concerning rulings involving children (non-mukallafin). By understanding this debate, you will grasp how subtle shifts in definition can have practical consequences in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing definitions
The text presents two definitions of hukm shar'i: one by later Ash'aris ('the address of Allah') and the Hanafi fuqaha's technical usage ('what is established by the address, such as obligation and prohibition'). Note the difference between the source of the ruling (the address) and the ruling itself (the legal consequence).
The Ash'ari definition is narrower, while the Hanafi definition is broader and more practical.
2
Understand the linguistic shift from majaz to haqiqah
The Hanafi usage of 'hukm' for the result of the address is initially a metaphorical extension (majaz), but due to widespread use among fuqaha, it becomes a transferred technical term (manqul) and eventually a technical reality (haqiqah istilahiyyah). This legitimizes the definition within the Hanafi school.
This reasoning demonstrates how technical terminology develops in Islamic legal sciences.
3
Analyze the first objection: definition does not match fuqaha's term
The first objection is that the Ash'ari definition defines 'hukm shar'i' as the address itself, but the fuqaha use 'hukm' for what is established by the address. Therefore, the definition fails to define the intended term. This highlights the importance of precise terminology.
The objection assumes that the goal is to define the fuqaha's technical term, not a broader concept.
4
Evaluate the second objection and its rebuttal
The second objection: the Ash'ari definition excludes rulings pertaining to non-mukallafin (e.g., a child's prayer being valid or recommended). The proposed rebuttal that such rulings actually pertain to the guardian is rejected because a child's own acts (like Islam or prayer) are directly his. Thus, the definition is not comprehensive.
This objection demonstrates that a definition of hukm must cover all shar'i rulings, including those related to children, as recognized in Hanafi fiqh (e.g., validity of a child's sale).

The author said in al-Tawdih: 'And some of them defined hukm shar'i as this' i.e., some of the later scholars among the followers of Ash'ari defined hukm shar'i with this aforementioned definition. They said: 'Hukm shar'i is the name for the address of Allah Almighty.' That is, according to some, the address of Allah was the definition of absolute hukm, as earlier. And according to some later Ash'aris, this definition is not of absolute hukm but only of hukm shar'i. So the definition of absolute hukm according to these later scholars would be 'the attribution of a command to another'. And the fuqaha apply it – i.e., the fuqaha in their terminology do not apply the term 'hukm' to the address itself, but to what is established by the address (ma thabata bi al-khitab). For example, obligation and prohibition that are established by the address – they apply the term to these. And this is, linguistically, majaz, because the verbal noun is applied to the object, like 'creation' applied to the created thing. Similarly, the application of 'khitab' to what is established by the address would be majaz. But since it has become widespread (sha'a) in the terminology of the fuqaha that 'hukm' is applied to what is established by the address, therefore it becomes a transferred (manqul) technical term, and a transferred technical term becomes a reality in the terminology of the user. Hence it will be a technical reality (haqiqah istilahiyyah). Then upon this – the definition of hukm as the address of Allah – various objections are mentioned. First: that the technical term (al-hukm al-mustalah) – i.e., in the terminology of the fuqaha, 'hukm' is applied to what is established by the address and not to the address itself – so this mentioned definition cannot be the definition of the hukm that is technical among the fuqaha, although the intended thing in the definition was this technical hukm. So what was intended was not defined, and what was defined is unintended. Second objection: it excludes what pertains to the act of a child (sabi). This is another objection to the aforementioned definition, i.e., rulings that pertain to the child's act, such as the validity of his sale, his embracing Islam, his performing prayer – their validity in the eyes of the Shari'ah are rulings, but this definition does not include them. Also, the child's prayer being recommended (mandub) and similar things, e.g., acceptance of gift, validity of marriage, recommendability of fasting and Hajj, invalidity of the child's divorce – all these are shar'i rulings, but this definition does not include them because in your definition 'pertaining to the acts of the mukallafin' excludes them. Since the child is not mukallaf, these matters are not related to the act of a mukallaf, so the definition is not comprehensive. If it is said: 'He is under guardianship' – this is a response to the same objection. If one answers that these matters are related to the act of the guardian (wali) who is mukallaf, therefore they become rulings under that aspect, not from the aspect of the child's act. Then we say: with this the author refutes this response, because the child's embracing Islam is valid and his prayer is valid and recommended – these are not related to the act of the guardian but to the child's own act. So in these matters, your mentioned response is not correct. And regarding other than Islam and prayer – i.e., besides Islam and prayer, your response is also not correct in the remaining matters, because the attachment of a right to the child's property and the attachment of a right to his liability – this also...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage covers the definition of hukm shar'i according to later Ash'ari scholars, who restrict it to 'the address of Allah'. The author then explains the usage of the term 'hukm' among the fuqaha: they use it to refer to what is established by the address (like obligation, prohibition) rather than the address itself. This usage is initially metaphorical but becomes a technical reality due to its widespread adoption. The passage then lists two objections to defining hukm as khitab Allah: first, it does not match the fuqaha's technical term which refers to the result of the address; second, it excludes rulings pertaining to the acts of non-mukallafin (e.g., children). The response that such rulings are attributed to the guardian is rejected because some acts (like a child's Islam or prayer) are directly the child's own acts. The argument is that the definition of hukm shar'i must encompass all shar'i rulings, including those relating to children, which the khitab-based definition fails to do.

Key Terms
حكم شرعي (hukm shar'i): Later Ash'aris define it as 'the address of Allah pertaining to the acts of the mukallafin'; fuqaha define it as 'what is established by that address'.
خطاب الله (khitab Allah): The divine address as found in Quran and Sunnah.
ما ثبت بالخطاب (ma thabata bi al-khitab): What is established by the address, i.e., the legal consequences like obligation, prohibition.
مصطلح (mustalah): The technical term used by fuqaha, referring to the established ruling rather than the address.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the child is not addressed by the khitab.
B) Because the child's prayer is not valid.
C) Because the definition only applies to adults.
D) Because the child's prayer is not a ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fuqaha define hukm as the practical result of divine address (ma thabata bi al-khitab), not the address itself, making their definition more inclusive of rulings involving non-mukallafin.

Refining the Definition of Hukm: Minors and Qiyas
Critical refinement of the definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two objections to the standard Hanafi definition of hukm and explain how the commentator resolves them by including minors under 'servants' and treating qiyas as a revealer of the divine address.

Core Idea
Hukm addresses all servants; qiyas reveals an existing address, not a new one.

The Hanafi definition of hukm as 'the address of Allah related to the actions of those obligated' has been critiqued for failing to cover actions of minors and rulings derived through qiyas. In this passage, the commentator defends the definition by proposing a slight rewording and clarifying the role of qiyas. Let us follow the logical steps of this refinement to see how the definition remains comprehensive.

Guided Path
1
Recall the standard definition
Start with the known Hanafi formulation: 'al-hukm huwa khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-mukallafin.' Identify that 'mukallaf' refers to the legally responsible adult.
This definition is the baseline being critiqued.
2
First objection: minors excluded
The commentator notes that rulings also apply to minors (sabi) even though they are not fully obligated. For example, the guardian performs duties on behalf of the minor. The definition must include such actions.
The fix: replace 'al-mukallafin' with 'al-ibad' (servants), which includes minors.
3
Second objection: qiyas-based rulings appear excluded
Rulings derived through qiyas (analogy) lack a direct textual address. According to the objection, they would fall outside the definition because no explicit khitab exists.
This challenges the definition's comprehensiveness.
4
Response: qiyas reveals the address
The commentator argues that qiyas does not create a new ruling; it reveals that the same address from the original case (maqis 'alayhi) applies to the derived case (maqis). Thus, the khitab is already present—qiyas is only a manifestor (muzhir).
This preserves the definition: qiyasi rulings are included because they are covered by an existing address.
5
Revised definition
The complete definition becomes: 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-ibad' (the address of Allah related to the actions of the servants), which encompasses actions of minors and rulings known through qiyas.
The definition remains tied to the divine address, avoiding the need to include qiyas as an independent source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حکم شرعی ہے اس کے بعد ولی کا ان حقوق کو ادا کرنا دوسرا حکم ہے جو اس پر مترتب ہے اس کا عین تو نہیں ہے بہر حال خود فعل صبی کے ساتھ حکم متعلق ہے اور اسی طرح اور بھی احکام ہیں جو فعل صبی کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں جن کا ذکر باب الحکم میں آجائے گا فینبغی ان یقال الخ پس لائق اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ سجات، با فعال المکلفین کے با فعال العباد کہا جائے تاکہ یہ تعریف احکام متعلقہ بفعل الصبی کو شامل ہو جائے کیونکہ عباد میں وہ بھی داخل ہے ويخرج منه ما ثبت بالقياس یعنی وہ احکام جو ثابت بالقیاس ہیں وہ احکام بھی اس تعریف حکم سے خارج ہیں کیونکہ ان کے متعلق خطاب اللہ واقع نہیں ہے لہذا تعریف حکم جامع نہ ہوئی یہ تیسرا اعتراض ہوا ۔ الا ان یقال یہ اسی ماثبت بالقیاس کو تعریف حکم میں داخل کرنے کی صورت ہے تاکہ اشکال مذکور دفع ہو جاتے چونکہ ان یقال بوجہ ان مصدریہ کے بحکم مصادر ہے اس حکم کی تفصیل کرتے ہوئے کہا اعلوات المصادر یعنی مصادر کبھی قائم مقام ظرف کے واقع ہو جاتی ہیں جیسے کہا جاتا ہے آیتک طلوع الفجر جس سے مراد وقت طلوع الفجر ہوتی ہے فقولہ الا ان يقال من هذا القبیل یعنی ان یقال بھی مصدر واقع بمقام ظرف ہے اور یہ استثناء مفرغ ہے من قولہ ويخرج منه ما ثبت بالقياس یعنی ما ثبت بالقیاس جمیع اوقات میں خارج از حکم تعریف ہے الا وقت قولہ في جواب الاشكال يدرك بالقیاس او یعنی قیاس کے ساتھ معلوم ہو جاتا ہے کہ خطاب اس حکم قیاسی میں بھی وارد ہے لاانه ثبت بالقیاس یعنی وہ حکم قیاس کے ساتھ ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ قیاس یہ ظاہر کرتا ہے کہ جو خطاب مقیس علیہ میں وارد ہے وہی اس مسئلہ قیاسی میں بھی وارد ہے تو مثبت خطاب ہوا قیاس صرف مظہر حکم ہوا لہذا اب مسائل قیاسیہ تعریف حکم میں داخل ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ یہ بھی خطاب اللہ میں درج ہیں۔
The ruling is a shar'i ruling; after that, the guardian's fulfillment of those rights is a second ruling that depends on it, not its essence. Nevertheless, the ruling pertains to the minor's own action. Similarly, there are other rulings related to the minor's action that will be mentioned in the chapter on rulings. So it is appropriate to say: whether with the actions of the obligated (mukallafin) or with the actions of the servants (ibad), so that this definition includes rulings pertaining to the minor's action, because the minor is also included among the servants. And from it is excluded what is established by qiyas, meaning rulings established by qiyas are excluded from this definition of hukm because there is no address (khitab) of Allah concerning them. So the definition is not comprehensive; this is the third objection. Unless one says: this is a way to include what is established by qiyas into the definition of hukm, so that the mentioned objection is repelled. Because the phrase 'illā an yuqāl' (unless one says) is, with respect to the masdariyyah, in the place of a noun. The explanation of this ruling: sometimes masdars stand in place of a zarf, as one says 'ātīka ṭulūʿ al-fajr' meaning the time of sunrise. So his statement 'illā an yuqāl' is of this type, meaning 'an yuqāl' is a masdar that stands in the place of a zarf, and this is a disconnected exception from his statement 'wa yakhruju minhu mā thabata bil-qiyās'. That is, 'mā thabata bil-qiyās' is excluded from the definition of hukm at all times except at the time of his statement in response to the objection, 'it is known by qiyas', meaning qiyas makes known that the address (khitab) is also present in this qiyāsī ruling, because it (the ruling) is not established by qiyas alone; rather, qiyas shows that the address that is in the original (maqīs ʿalayhi) is also present in this qiyāsī issue. So the address is established, and qiyas is only a revealer of the ruling. Therefore, qiyāsī issues will now be included in the definition of hukm, because they are also included in the address of Allah.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the definition of hukm (ruling) as 'the address of Allah related to the actions of those obligated'. The commentator presents two objections. First, the definition should explicitly include actions of minors (sabi), because minors are also subject to rulings, even though they are not fully obligated (mukallaf). The fix is to say 'actions of the servants' (afāl al-ʿibād) instead of 'actions of the obligated' (afāl al-mukallafīn), as minors are included in 'servants'. Second, rulings derived by qiyas (analogy) appear to be excluded because there is no direct address (khitāb) of Allah about them. However, the commentator responds that this is not a problem: qiyas does not establish a ruling independently but rather reveals that the same address from the original case applies to the derived case. Thus, the address (khitāb) is present in qiyas-based rulings, and they are included in the definition. This demonstrates that the definition of hukm is comprehensive when properly understood.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The address of Allah related to the actions of the servants (ibad), including both obligated persons and minors, and encompassing rulings known via qiyas.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction that makes manifest (muzhir) the divine address that already exists in the original case.
خطاب (khitab): The direct address of Allah, which is the source of all rulings, whether explicit or revealed through qiyas.
صبي (sabi): A minor who is not mukallaf but whose actions are still subject to certain rulings (e.g., validity of worship, property rights).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To exclude non-Muslims from the definition
B) To include actions of minors (sabi) under the definition
C) To emphasize that only adults are addressed
D) To remove any reference to obligation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm is comprehensive when 'ibad' is used and when qiyas is understood as a revealer of the divine address, thus covering actions of minors and analogically derived rulings.

Resolving Objections to the Definition of Hukm: Including Acts of the Heart
Addressing objections to the definition of hukm and their resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi interpretation of 'afʿāl' as general (shāmil) resolves two key objections to the definition of hukm, and apply this analysis to ensure comprehensiveness and avoid redundancy in usul definitions.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'afʿāl' includes both physical and spiritual actions, making definitions comprehensive and avoiding repetition.

The definition of hukm shari must cover all actions commanded or prohibited by the Lawgiver. Two objections arise: that spiritual commands (like 'believe') are excluded if 'afʿāl' is only physical, and that mentioning 'afʿāl' in hukm and 'amaliyyah' in fiqh causes redundant repetition. This passage shows how the Hanafi school resolves both by taking 'afʿāl' in its most general sense, encompassing actions of both limbs and heart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
The fourth objection claims that spiritual commands like 'āmīnū' (believe) and 'faʿtabirū' (take heed) are excluded if 'afʿāl' means only physical actions. The fifth objection notes that repeating 'afʿāl' in hukm and 'amaliyyah' in fiqh leads to redundancy.
These objections challenge the comprehensiveness and conciseness of the definitions.
2
Understand the Hanafi stance on 'afʿāl'
The passage clarifies that 'afʿāl' in the definition of hukm is general (ʿāmm), including both physical acts (afʿāl al-jawāriḥ) and spiritual acts (afʿāl al-qulūb).
This is a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: words are taken in their full general sense unless there is evidence for restriction.
3
Apply the general meaning to repel the fourth objection
With 'afʿāl' including spiritual acts, commands like 'āmīnū' and 'faʿtabirū' fall under the definition of hukm because they are actions of the heart.
4
Distinguish 'afʿāl' from 'amaliyyah' to repel the fifth objection
The word 'amaliyyah' (practical) in the definition of fiqh is restricted to physical actions only. Since 'afʿāl' in hukm covers both, and 'amaliyyah' covers only physical, there is no semantic overlap and thus no repetition.
5
Summarize the principle
The Hanafi school uses the broader interpretation of 'afʿāl' to achieve a comprehensive definition of hukm that includes all types of actions, while distinguishing it from the term 'amaliyyah' to avoid redundancy.
This demonstrates the importance of precise usul terminology and the role of interpretation in resolving apparent contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ايضا يخرج نحو امنوا يہ حکم کی تعریف مذکور پر چو تھا اعتراض ہے کہ امنوا اور فاعتبروا با وجود احکام شرعیہ ہونے کے اس تعریف سے خارج ہو رہے کیونکہ آپ کی تعریف میں با فعال کی قید انہیں خارج کر رہی ہے کیونکہ افعال سے مراد جوارح اور ظاہری اعضاء کے افعال مراد ہیں اور وجوب تصدیق جو آمنوا سے مراد ہے اور وجوب اعتبار جو فاعتبروا سے مقصود ہے یہ افعال جوارح نہیں ہیں بلکہ ان کا تو تعلق قلب سے ہے لہذا یہ خارج ہیں تعریف جامع نہ ہوئي ويقع التكرار بين العملية الخير حكم كي تعريف مذکور پر پانچواں اعتراض ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر حکم کی تعریف مذکور کو تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو فقہ کی تعریف میں تکرار واقع ہو جائے گا کیونکہ فقہ کی تعریف العلم بالاحکام الشرعیة العملیہ ہے اور حکم کی تعریف میں افعال المکلفین کا ذکر ہے جو کہ یہ بھی احکام عملیہ ہیں اور پھر فقہ کی تعریف میں عملیہ کی قید جو افعال کا ہم معنی ہے لہذا افعال المکلفین اور عملیہ ان دونوں کے ذکر سے تکرار واقع ہو جائے گا تو تعریف فقہ اس صورت میں یہ ہوگی العلم بخطابات اللہ تعالٰی المتعلقة بافعال المكافين العملية فيقع التکرار خطابات اللہ تعالیٰ اتو یہ لفظ احکام کی تفسیر ہے جو کہ حدفقہ میں واقع ہے اس تکرار کی موجب حکم کی تعریف مذکورہ ہے ۔ الا ان یقال نعنی اتو یہ اشکال با تکرار کے دفع کرنے کی توجیہ ہے خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ افعال سے مراد عام ہے خواہ فعل جوارح ہو یا فعل قلب اور لفظ عملیہ جو کہ حد فقہ میں واقع ہے اس سے مراد صرف افعال جوارح ہیں تو جب افعال اور عملیہ کا مفہوم ایک نہ رہا تو موجب تکرار نہیں ہوگا تو اس مراد افعال سے جیسے تکرار کا اشکال دفع ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح جو پہلے آمنوا اور فاعتبروا کے خروج کا اعتراض کیا گیا تھا اس کا جواب بھی نکل آیا کہ جب حکم کی تعریف میں افعال سے مراد عام ہے خواہ فعل جوارح ہو یا فعل قلب تو حکم کی تعریف امنوا اور فاعتبروا کو شامل ہو جائے گی کیونکہ یہ افعال قلب ہیں لہذا افعال المکلفین میں درج ہو جائیں گے.
Also, examples like 'āmīnū' (believe) and 'faʿtabirū' (take heed) are excluded. This is the fourth objection to the mentioned definition of hukm: that despite being shar'i rulings, they are excluded from this definition because the definition's restriction to actions (bi-afʿāl) excludes them, since actions mean actions of the limbs and external organs, while the obligation of belief (taṣdīq) intended by 'āmīnū' and the obligation of consideration (iʿtibār) intended by 'faʿtabirū' are not actions of the limbs but are related to the heart. So they are excluded, and the definition is not comprehensive. And repetition occurs between 'amaliyyah and ... (garbled) is the fifth objection to the mentioned definition of hukm. Its summary is: if the mentioned definition of hukm is accepted, then repetition will occur in the definition of fiqh, because fiqh is defined as 'knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings' (al-ʿilm bi al-aḥkām al-sharʿiyyah al-ʿamaliyyah), and in the definition of hukm there is mention of 'actions of the obligated' (afʿāl al-mukallafīn), which are also practical rulings. Then in the definition of fiqh, the restriction 'practical' (ʿamaliyyah) is synonymous with actions, so mentioning both 'actions of the obligated' and 'practical' causes repetition. In that case, the definition of fiqh would be knowledge of the addresses of Allah related to the practical actions of the obligated, and repetition occurs. The word 'addresses' (khiṭābāt) is an interpretation of 'rulings' (aḥkām) that occurs in the definition of fiqh, and the mentioned definition of hukm is the cause of this repetition. Unless one says: this is an explanation to repel the objection of repetition. Its summary is that 'actions' (afʿāl) is general, including both actions of the limbs and actions of the heart, while the word 'practical' (ʿamaliyyah) that occurs in the definition of fiqh refers only to actions of the limbs. So when the meaning of 'actions' and 'practical' is not the same, no repetition occurs. Thus with this meaning of 'actions' (afʿāl), just as the objection of repetition is repelled, similarly the earlier objection regarding the exclusion of 'āmīnū' and 'faʿtabirū' is also answered: when in the definition of hukm 'actions' is general, including both actions of the limbs and actions of the heart, then the definition of hukm will include 'āmīnū' and 'faʿtabirū' because they are actions of the heart, and thus they are included in the actions of the obligated.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents two additional objections to the definition of hukm and their unified response. The fourth objection notes that commands like 'āmīnū' (believe) and 'faʿtabirū' (take heed) are spiritual acts (afʿāl al-qalb), not physical acts (afʿāl al-jawāriḥ), and thus are excluded if 'afʿāl' in the definition means only physical actions. The fifth objection points to redundancy: if 'afʿāl' appears in the definition of hukm, and 'ʿamaliyyah' (practical) appears in the definition of fiqh, both refer to actions, creating unnecessary repetition. The commentator resolves both by interpreting 'afʿāl' broadly to include both physical and spiritual actions. This broader interpretation ensures that spiritual commands like 'āmīnū' are included in the definition of hukm, and since 'afʿāl' in the hukm definition covers all actions while 'ʿamaliyyah' in the fiqh definition is restricted to physical acts, there is no overlap and hence no repetition. This preserves the comprehensiveness of both definitions.

Key Terms
أفعال القلوب (afʿāl al-qulūb): Actions of the heart, such as belief and reflection, which are also considered actions in the definition of hukm
أفعال الجوارح (afʿāl al-jawāriḥ): Actions of the physical limbs, which are specified as the subject of 'amaliyyah in the definition of fiqh
عملي (ʿamalī): Practical, referring to physical actions only in the context of the definition of fiqh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the broader interpretation of 'afʿāl' resolve both the fourth and fifth objections?
A) By making 'afʿāl' specific to physical actions
B) By including spiritual actions, covering commands like 'āmīnū', and by distinguishing 'afʿāl' from 'amaliyyah' (which is only physical) to avoid repetition
C) By removing 'afʿāl' from the definition
D) By using a different term

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the word 'afʿāl' in the definition of hukm is general, including both physical and spiritual actions, which makes the definition comprehensive and avoids redundancy with the term 'amaliyyah' in the definition of fiqh.

Clarifying the Definition of Hukm: The Role of Lam al-'Ahd
Resolving confusion between definitions of absolute hukm and shar'i hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of lam al-'ahd to determine whether a definition of hukm is for absolute or shar'i hukm, and evaluate the implications for the definition of fiqh.

Core Idea
The lam in 'al-hukm' is for 'ahd, making it the shar'i hukm, not absolute.

In this passage from Al-Talwih, the commentator corrects a misunderstanding in Al-Tawdih regarding the definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah'. The author of Al-Tawdih thought that some scholars defined hukm absolutely while others added 'shar'i', leading to confusion. Al-Talwih clarifies that the lam in 'al-hukm' is the lam of 'ahd, which refers specifically to the shar'i hukm. Moreover, many Ash'ari texts explicitly define 'al-hukm al-shar'i' as 'khitab Allah'. This lesson examines the usul principles behind this linguistic analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The author of Al-Tawdih objects to defining hukm as 'khitab Allah' without 'shar'i', assuming it creates two definitions: absolute and shar'i.
2
Analyze the commentator's response
Al-Talwih argues that the lam in 'al-hukm' is lam al-‘ahd, making it specific to shar'i hukm. This removes ambiguity.
Lam al-‘ahd refers to a specific known entity.
3
Examine the explicit Ash'ari texts
Many Ash'ari books explicitly define 'al-hukm al-shar'i' as 'khitab Allah', confirming the definition is for shar'i hukm.
4
Understand the consequence for the definition of fiqh
If the definition were for absolute hukm, then 'shar'iyyah' in fiqh would be redundant. Al-Talwih explains that 'shar'i' in fiqh means 'dependent on Shari'ah', not the divine address, so no redundancy.
5
Evaluate the overall refinement
Al-Talwih successfully refutes the objection, showing the definition is consistent and the author's concern is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح في التلويح قول بعضهم عرف ذكر في بعض المختصرات یعنی بعض مختصر كتابون میں تعریف حکم کے متعلق یوں کہا گیا ہے الحکم خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ الر یعنی الحکم کو مطلق رکھا گیا ہے اس کے ساتھ شرعی کی قید نہیں کی گئی لیکن ان کے نزدیک الحکم کی لام عہد کی ہے اور معہود حکم شرعی ہے تو تعریف در حقیقت حکم شرعی کی ہوتی ـ وصوح في كثير من الكتب الا یعنی بہت سی کتب اشاعرہ میں خہ۔ تصریح کر دی گئی ہے الحکم الشرعی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ تو یہاں شرعی کی قید بالتصریح مذکور ہے فتوهم المصنف او یعنی مصنف کو وہم ہوا کہ بعض کے نزدیک یہ حکم مطلق کی تعریف ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک یہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے حالانکہ ایسے نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تمام اشاعرہ کے نزدیک حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے۔ تو ہم مصنف کا اعتراض در حقیقت ساقط ہے ہم پہلے شرح منہاج کی یہ عبارت نقل کر چکے ہیں " اجاب بعضهم بان المحدود الحكم الشرعي الذي هو فقه الى المتعلق بالجوارح لا مطلق الحكم الشرعي انتهى كلامه فهذا يؤيد المصنف بانهم اختلفوا من التوشيح - قال المصنف اذا كان هذا ان یعنی مصنف نے کہا کہ اگر یہ تعریف مذکور حکم مطلق کی تعریف ہو تو قمعنی الشریعی پھر لفظ شرعی جو فقہ کی تعریف العلم بالاحکام الشرعیہ میں مذکور ہے تو اس کا معنیٰ ما يتوقف على الشرع ہوگا کو جوب الصلاة والصوم اور ماورد به خطاب الشرع نہیں ہو گا ور نہ تو قید شرعیہ بے فائدہ ہو جائے گی کیونکہ جب حکم مطلق کی تعریف خطاب اللہ تعالٰی کے ساتھ ہے تو یہی ماورد بہ خطاب الشروع ہے اگر شرعیہ کا لفظ جو فقہ کی تعریف میں واقع ہے اس کا معنی بھی یہی ہو تو پھر یہ قید فضول
The commentator said in Al-Talwih: The statement of some scholars – defined, mentioned in some abridged books – that they defined hukm as: 'The address of Allah ta'ala' (al-hukm khitab Allah ta'ala), meaning they left hukm absolute and did not restrict it with 'shar'i'. But according to them, the lam in 'al-hukm' is for 'ahd (specific reference), and the referent is the shar'i hukm, so in reality the definition is for the shar'i hukm. And it is made explicit in many books of the Ash'aris: 'al-hukm al-shar'i is the address of Allah ta'ala.' So here the restriction 'shar'i' is explicitly mentioned. Thus the author (of Al-Tawdih) wrongly imagined that according to some this is the definition of absolute hukm and according to some it is the definition of shar'i hukm, whereas it is not so; rather, according to all Ash'aris, it is the definition of shar'i hukm. Therefore the author's objection is actually invalid. We have previously quoted this statement from Sharh al-Minhaj: 'Some answered that the defined thing is the shar'i hukm that is fiqh-related (fiqhi) pertaining to actions of the limbs, not absolute shar'i hukm.' End of his statement. This supports the author that they differed from Al-Tawshih? The author said: If this is the case, then if the mentioned definition is for absolute hukm, then the meaning of 'shar'i' (in the definition of fiqh) would be 'what depends on the Shari'ah' (ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'), like the obligation of prayer and fasting, and not 'what is brought by the address of the Shari'ah' (ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'), otherwise the restriction 'shar'iyyah' would be futile, because if the definition of absolute hukm is 'address of Allah', then that is precisely 'what is brought by the address of the Shari'ah'. If the word 'shar'iyyah' in the definition of fiqh also means that, then this restriction would be superfluous.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator (Al-Talwih) on the author (Al-Tawdih)'s understanding of the definition of hukm. Some scholars defined hukm simply as 'khitab Allah' without the word 'shar'i'. The author of Al-Tawdih assumed that this created confusion: some took it as a definition of absolute hukm, others as shar'i hukm. Al-Talwih corrects this: the lam in 'al-hukm' is for 'ahd (specific), indicating the shar'i hukm. Moreover, many Ash'ari texts explicitly state 'al-hukm al-shar'i' as the definition. Thus, the author's objection is based on a misunderstanding. Additionally, the author had argued that if the definition were for absolute hukm, then adding 'shar'iyyah' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant. Al-Talwih counters by noting that some scholars differentiate: the 'shar'i' hukm in fiqh's definition means rulings that depend on Shari'ah (like obligation of prayer), not the absolute address. This nuance resolves the redundancy issue. The passage demonstrates careful refinement of terminology in Usul al-Fiqh.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The address of Allah, with the lam for 'ahd indicating the shar'i hukm
لام العهد (lām al-ʿahd): The definite article lam that refers to a specific, known entity (here, the shar'i hukm)
شرعي (sharʿī): Relating to the Shari'ah; in the definition of fiqh, it means 'what depends on the Shari'ah'

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) By adding 'shar'i' to the definition
B) By stating that the lam in 'al-hukm' is for 'ahd, referring specifically to shar'i hukm
C) By claiming the definition is for absolute hukm
D) By rejecting the definition entirely

Key Takeaway
The lam al-'ahd in 'al-hukm' conclusively defines it as the shar'i hukm, rendering objections based on omission of 'shar'i' invalid.

Definition of Hukm Shar'i and Its Implications for Fiqh
Discussing definition of hukm shar'i and objections to its inclusivity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two competing definitions of hukm shar'i (khatab Allah vs. ma thabata bi al-khatab) and explain how each affects the scope of fiqh.

Core Idea
How we define hukm determines whether rulings like wujub al-iman fall inside or outside fiqh.

This passage examines the foundational definition of hukm shar'i in Hanafi usul. The author considers the definition of hukm as khatab Allah ta'ala and analyses its consequences for the definition of fiqh. A key issue is whether the term 'shar'iyya' in the definition of fiqh becomes redundant if hukm itself already implies shar'i. The discussion also addresses whether rulings of belief (like wujub al-iman) belong to fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
State the two possible definitions of hukm shar'i: (1) khatab Allah (the divine address itself) and (2) ma thabata bi al-khatab (what is established by the address, i.e., wujub, hurma, etc.).
These correspond to different usages in Hanafi usul.
2
Relate definitions to fiqh
The definition of fiqh is 'knowledge of the shar'i rulings' (al-ahkam al-shar'iyya). Understand how each definition of hukm affects the meaning of 'shar'i' in that context.
If hukm = khatab Allah, then 'shar'i' means 'what is brought by the Shari'a address'; if hukm = ma thabata, then 'shar'i' means 'what depends on the Shari'a'.
3
Analyze redundancy of 'shar'iyya'
If hukm is defined as khatab Allah, does the word 'shar'iyya' in the definition of fiqh become redundant? The passage argues no, because 'shar'i' then means 'mawrud bihi' not 'mutawaqif', so it adds specification.
This avoids the same meaning being repeated.
4
Determine inclusion of wujub al-iman
Under the definition of hukm as khatab Allah, wujub al-iman is included because there is a divine address about iman. Under the definition as ma thabata, it is excluded because iman does not depend on the Shari'a; rather the Shari'a depends on it.
This shows the practical consequence of the definition.
5
Understand the rational indicator
The passage uses a rational indicator (qarina aqliyya) to reconcile definitions: reason witnesses that the word 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh intends wujub and hurma, not the address itself.
Thus, when defining hukm as khatab, we interpret it as 'ma khutiba bihi'.

بے فائدہ ہو جائے گی اور جب شرعیہ کا معنی ہو ما يتوقف على الشرع تو پھر یہ قید مفید ہوگی اور وجوب ایمان اور تصدیق بالنبی جو حکم معنی خطاب اللہ میں درج تھے ان کو تعریف فقہ سے خارج کر دے گی کیونکہ ایمان اور تصدیق بالنبي موقوف على الشرع نہیں ہیں بلکہ شریعت ان پر موقوف ہے لہذا یہ اس قید کے ساتھ خارج از فقہ ہو جائیں گے۔ واذا كان تعريفا للحكم الشرعي الا یعنی جب خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہو تو فمعنی الشرعی یعنی لفظ شرعی جو فقہ کی تعریف میں مذکور ہے اس کا معنی انس وقت ما ورد به خطاب الشرع ہوگا لا ما يتوقف على الشرع والاركان الحد اهم الا ورنہ تو حكم شرعی کی تعریف جو خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے یہ عام من المحدود ہو جائے گی محدود سے مراد حکم شرعی ماخوذ فی تعریف الفقہ ہے ۔ لتناوله مثل وجوب الایمان یعنی حد جو خطاب الله تعالیٰ کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے وہ وجوب ایمان وغیرہ کو شامل ہے کیونکہ خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ ان کے ساتھ وارد ہے۔ مع ان المحدود یعنی حکم شرعی جو ماخوذ فی الفقہ ہے اگر اس کا معنی ما يتوقف على الشرع ہو تو یہ وجوب ایمان کو شامل نہیں ہے کیونکہ وجوب ایمان موقوف على الشرع نہیں تو محدود یعنی حکم شرعی ماخوذ في الفقہ معنی ما تتوقف خاص ہو جائے گا اور حکم شرعی کی حد خطاب اللہ تعالی اس سے عام ہو جائے گی تو لکان الحدائم من المحدود -
