الثاني ان الحكوا خلاصہ اس جواب کا یہ ہے کہ حقیقتاً حکم وجوب حرمت کا نام نہیں بلکہ ایجاب و تحریم کا نام ہے جو صفات الہیہ میں سے ہیں لہذا اس کی تعریف میں لفظ خطاب اللہ استعمال کرنا صحیح ہے اور ما خوطب بہ کے معنی میں کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور وجوب و حرمت پسا طلاق حکم بنابر مسامحت ہے چونکہ حکم بمعنی ایجاب اور تحریم کا یہ اثر مرتب ہیں لہذا مجازا انہیں حکم کہ دیا گیا ہے۔ الثالث ان الحکم خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ حکم خود خطاب اللہ کا نام ہے کیونکہ ایجاب مین ہے قول افعل کا لیکن فعل مکلف کے لئے اس قول سے کوئی صفت حقیقیہ قائمہ بالفعل نہیں اور چونکہ یہ قول متعلق بالمعدوم ہے اس لئے اس کے متعلق یعنی فعل مکلف کے لئے کوئی صفت قائمہ ماخوذه من القول نہیں ہے بس یہی قول خطاب بعینہ حکم ہے جب اس کی نسبت الی الحاکم ہو تو اسے ایجاب کہتے ہیں جب اس کی نسبت اس فعل کی طرف ہو جس کے بارہ میں یہ قول واقع ہوا ہے تو اسے وجوب کہتے ہیں تو وجوب و ایجاب ذاتاً ایک ہی شئی نہیں کیونکہ یہ دونوں بعینہ قول افعل کا نام ہیں اور مختلف بالاعتبار ہیں یعنی اس اعتبار سے کہ اس قول کی نسبت الی الحاکم ہو تو ایجاب اگر اس کی نسبت الی فعل المکلف ہو تو اس کا نام وجوب ہے بہر حال حقیقتاً یہ نفس خطاب کا نام ہے لہذا ما خوطب یہ کی تاویل کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ۔ فلذلك یعنی چونکہ ایجاب و جوب میں ذاتاً اتحاد ہے اس لئے یہ حضرات اقسام حکم کبھی وجوب و حرمت اور کبھی ایجاب و تحریم اور کبھی وجوب تحریم قرار دیتے ہیں جیسے اصول ابن حاجب میں ہے۔ الثاني انه غير منعکس تعریف حکم پر یہ دوسرا اعتراض ہے یعنی یہ تعریف جامع بجميع الافراد نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس تعریف میں افعال مکلفین کا لفظ موجود ہے وہ احکام جو غیر مکلفین کے افعال کے
It will become useless, and when the meaning of shar'iyya is 'that which depends on the Shari'a', then this restriction will be beneficial, and it will exclude from the definition of fiqh wujub al-iman and tasdiq bi al-nabi which were included in the meaning of hukm under khatab Allah, because iman and tasdiq bi al-nabi are not dependent on the Shari'a; rather the Shari'a depends on them, so with this restriction they become excluded from fiqh. And if it is a definition of al-hukm al-shar'i, i.e., when khatab Allah ta'ala is the definition of hukm shar'i, then the meaning of al-shar'i (the word shar'i mentioned in the definition of fiqh) will be 'that which is mentioned by the address of the Shari'a' not 'that which depends on the Shari'a' and [otherwise] the definition of hukm shar'i made with khatab Allah ta'ala would be more general than the defined term (mahdud). The mahdud refers to hukm shar'i taken in the definition of fiqh. Because it includes such as wujub al-iman, i.e., the boundary made with khatab Allah ta'ala includes wujub al-iman etc., because khatab Allah ta'ala occurs concerning them, while the mahdud (i.e., hukm shar'i taken in fiqh) if its meaning is 'that which depends on the Shari'a' then it does not include wujub al-iman because wujub al-iman is not dependent on the Shari'a. So the mahdud (hukm shar'i taken in fiqh) in the meaning of 'that which depends' becomes specific, and the boundary of hukm shar'i (khatab Allah) is more general than it, so the boundary would be more general than the defined term. His saying: 'fa al-hukmu 'ala hadha' i.e., on this assumption, when the definition of hukm shar'i is khatab Allah ta'ala, then the definition of absolute hukm is 'attribution of command to the intended person' etc., and khatab Allah ta'ala will not be the definition of absolute hukm, otherwise in the definition of fiqh the restriction of shar'iyya with al-ahkam would be redundant because when the definition of hukm shar'i is khatab Allah ta'ala, then the meaning of shar'i is 'what is brought by the address of the Shari'a' not 'what depends on the Shari'a', then surely in the definition of fiqh as al-'ilm bi al-ahkam al-shar'iyya, the mention of shar'iyya would be repetitive because this is the meaning of hukm and this is the meaning of shar'iyya. If it is said: the gist of the question is that at that time the shar'i rulings of fiqh would include wujub al-iman etc., although these are not among the shar'i rulings of fiqh. We say, with the reply [given] that later the restriction of 'amaliyya mentioned in the definition of fiqh will exclude them. His saying: 'wa al-fuqaha' i.e., in the terminology of jurists, hukm is truly called 'what is established by address' such as wujub and hurma, even though this is a linguistic metaphor because linguistically it is the application of the masdar to the maf'ul, i.e., applying al-hukm to al-mahkum, but in juristic terminology it becomes real. His saying 'ma [naqasa] 'alayhi' the definition of hukm, although the author has answered some of the objections and not others. The first [objection]: the intended meaning is that the main intended definition was of that hukm which is conventional among the jurists, and they call 'what is established by address' hukm, like wujub and hurma which are attributes of the act of the mukallaf. The jurists do not call the address itself, which is among the attributes of Allah ta'ala, a hukm. In summary, what was intended was not defined; what was defined is not intended. It was answered in several ways: first, just as applying hukm to ma thabata bi al-khitab is not in the masdar meaning, but rather it means 'what is judged' similarly in the definition of hukm, the word khitab is intended to mean 'what is addressed' due to a rational indicator (qarina 'aqliyya), i.e., reason witnesses that the word hukm mentioned in the definition of fiqh intends wujub and hurma, and wujub and hurma are not names of the address itself but rather names of 'what is addressed', so khitab is intended to mean 'what is addressed'. Second, [summary]: that truly hukm is not the name of wujub and hurma, but rather the name of ijab and tahrim which are among the divine attributes, so using the word khitab Allah in its definition is correct, and there is no need to interpret it as 'what is addressed'. And wujub and hurma are called hukm by tolerance since hukm in the meaning of ijab and tahrim are their effects, so they are metaphorically called hukm. Third: that hukm is itself the name of khitab Allah, because ijab is the saying 'do' but this saying does not produce a real attribute subsisting in the action of the mukallaf; and since this saying is related to the non-existent, there is no attribute derived from the saying standing for the action of the mukallaf. Rather this saying, the address itself, is hukm. When it is attributed to the ruler, it is called ijab; when attributed to the action concerning which this saying occurred, it is called wujub. So wujub and ijab are not identical in essence because both are exactly the name of the saying 'do' and differ by consideration: by consideration of attribution to the ruler it is ijab; by attribution to the action of the mukallaf it is wujub. In any case, truly it is the name of the address itself, so there is no need for interpretation as 'what is addressed'. Therefore, since there is unity in essence between ijab and wujub, these scholars sometimes state the divisions of hukm as wujub and hurma, and sometimes as ijab and tahrim, and sometimes as wujub and tahrim, as in usul of Ibn Hajib. The second [objection]: that it is not reciprocal (ghayr mun'akis), i.e., this definition is not comprehensive of all individuals because this definition contains the word 'actions of the mukallafin' whereas rulings concerning actions of non-mukallafin...

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion on the definition of hukm shar'i as presented in the text. The author examines a prior definition that defines hukm as khatab Allah ta'ala (the address of Allah) and then analyses its implications for the definition of fiqh as knowledge of shar'i rulings. The key issue is whether the restriction 'shar'iyya' in the definition of fiqh becomes redundant if hukm itself includes the shar'i element. The discussion also addresses the scope of fiqh, specifically whether rulings like wujub al-iman (obligation of faith) should be included in fiqh or not. The passage then presents three objections to the definition of hukm and their respective responses. The first objection concerns the mismatch between what is defined (khatab Allah) and what is intended (what is established by address, i.e., wujub and hurma). The responses include rational interpretation, metaphorical usage, and the view that hukm is actually the address itself. The second objection (incomplete at the page end) points that the definition is not comprehensive because it includes only actions of mukallafin, whereas rulings exist for non-mukallaf actions as well. The commentary follows the author's order: first explaining the consequences of taking 'shar'i' in different senses, then presenting the objections and responses. All arguments are within the Hanafi usul tradition, with references to rational proofs and the authority of jurists' terminology.

Key Terms
حکم شرعی (hukm sharʿī): The definition under debate: khaṭāb Allāh taʿālā (address of Allah) or what is established by that address (wujub, hurma).
ما ثبت بالخطاب (mā thabata bi al-khiṭāb): What is established by the address, i.e., the ruling (wujub, hurma) that becomes an attribute of the action.
خطاب اللہ (khiṭāb Allāh): The divine address itself, considered by some as the real hukm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rational indicator (qarina aqliyya) that justifies interpreting 'khatab' in the definition of hukm as 'ma khutiba bihi'?
A) The word 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh means wujub and hurma, not the address itself.
B) The address cannot be defined because it is divine.
C) The definition must be literal, not metaphorical.
D) Jurists never use 'hukm' for the address.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm shar'i is contested; the Hanafi jurists predominantly use hukm to refer to the resulting qualification in the action, not the divine address itself.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
10 min
Objections to the Definition of Hukm Shar'i and Their Resolutions
Discussing definition of hukm shar'i and objections to its inclusivity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three objections to defining hukm as khatab Allah and explain the Hanafi responses to each.

Core Idea
Objections to the definition sharpen our understanding: how we define hukm determines what is included in fiqh.

This passage continues the discussion by presenting objections to defining hukm shar'i as khatab Allah. The first objection is that the definition defines something (the address) that is not what the jurists intend (the ruling). Three responses are given. The second objection is that the definition is not comprehensive because it only applies to actions of mukallafs. The third objection is implied but not fully developed. The author aims to defend the definition and clarify the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first objection
State the first objection: the defined term (hukm as address) does not match the intended concept (ruling as attribute of action, like wujub/hurma).
This is the core criticism: the definition is 'akhass min al-mahdud' or 'does not correspond'.
2
Examine the first response
The first response uses a rational indicator (qarina aqliyya) to interpret 'khatab' as 'what is addressed' (ma khutiba bihi), aligning the definition with the intended meaning.
This is based on the context of fiqh definition.
3
Examine the second response
The second response argues that hukm in its real sense is the address itself (the divine attribute of ijab/tahrim), and wujub/hurma are metaphorical applications of the term.
This defense maintains the literal definition as correct.
4
Examine the third response
The third response posits that ijab and wujub are essentially the same thing (the address 'do') considered from different perspectives: attribution to the ruler (ijab) and to the action (wujub). Thus, hukm is the address itself.
This unifies the two concepts.
5
Identify the second objection
The second objection is that the definition is not comprehensive (ghayr mun'akis) because it includes only actions of mukallafs, whereas rulings exist for non-mukallafs as well.
The passage mentions this but the discussion is cut off; the response likely involves the restriction 'amaliyya' in fiqh definition.

الثاني ان الحكوا خلاصہ اس جواب کا یہ ہے کہ حقیقتاً حکم وجوب حرمت کا نام نہیں بلکہ ایجاب و تحریم کا نام ہے جو صفات الہیہ میں سے ہیں لہذا اس کی تعریف میں لفظ خطاب اللہ استعمال کرنا صحیح ہے اور ما خوطب بہ کے معنی میں کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور وجوب و حرمت پسا طلاق حکم بنابر مسامحت ہے چونکہ حکم بمعنی ایجاب اور تحریم کا یہ اثر مرتب ہیں لہذا مجازا انہیں حکم کہ دیا گیا ہے۔ الثالث ان الحکم خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ حکم خود خطاب اللہ کا نام ہے کیونکہ ایجاب مین ہے قول افعل کا لیکن فعل مکلف کے لئے اس قول سے کوئی صفت حقیقیہ قائمہ بالفعل نہیں اور چونکہ یہ قول متعلق بالمعدوم ہے اس لئے اس کے متعلق یعنی فعل مکلف کے لئے کوئی صفت قائمہ ماخوذه من القول نہیں ہے بس یہی قول خطاب بعینہ حکم ہے جب اس کی نسبت الی الحاکم ہو تو اسے ایجاب کہتے ہیں جب اس کی نسبت اس فعل کی طرف ہو جس کے بارہ میں یہ قول واقع ہوا ہے تو اسے وجوب کہتے ہیں تو وجوب و ایجاب ذاتاً ایک ہی شئی نہیں کیونکہ یہ دونوں بعینہ قول افعل کا نام ہیں اور مختلف بالاعتبار ہیں یعنی اس اعتبار سے کہ اس قول کی نسبت الی الحاکم ہو تو ایجاب اگر اس کی نسبت الی فعل المکلف ہو تو اس کا نام وجوب ہے بہر حال حقیقتاً یہ نفس خطاب کا نام ہے لہذا ما خوطب یہ کی تاویل کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ۔ فلذلك یعنی چونکہ ایجاب و جوب میں ذاتاً اتحاد ہے اس لئے یہ حضرات اقسام حکم کبھی وجوب و حرمت اور کبھی ایجاب و تحریم اور کبھی وجوب تحریم قرار دیتے ہیں جیسے اصول ابن حاجب میں ہے۔ الثاني انه غير منعکس تعریف حکم پر یہ دوسرا اعتراض ہے یعنی یہ تعریف جامع بجميع الافراد نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس تعریف میں افعال مکلفین کا لفظ موجود ہے وہ احکام جو غیر مکلفین کے افعال کے
It will become useless, and when the meaning of shar'iyya is 'that which depends on the Shari'a', then this restriction will be beneficial, and it will exclude from the definition of fiqh wujub al-iman and tasdiq bi al-nabi which were included in the meaning of hukm under khatab Allah, because iman and tasdiq bi al-nabi are not dependent on the Shari'a; rather the Shari'a depends on them, so with this restriction they become excluded from fiqh. And if it is a definition of al-hukm al-shar'i, i.e., when khatab Allah ta'ala is the definition of hukm shar'i, then the meaning of al-shar'i (the word shar'i mentioned in the definition of fiqh) will be 'that which is mentioned by the address of the Shari'a' not 'that which depends on the Shari'a' and [otherwise] the definition of hukm shar'i made with khatab Allah ta'ala would be more general than the defined term (mahdud). The mahdud refers to hukm shar'i taken in the definition of fiqh. Because it includes such as wujub al-iman, i.e., the boundary made with khatab Allah ta'ala includes wujub al-iman etc., because khatab Allah ta'ala occurs concerning them, while the mahdud (i.e., hukm shar'i taken in fiqh) if its meaning is 'that which depends on the Shari'a' then it does not include wujub al-iman because wujub al-iman is not dependent on the Shari'a. So the mahdud (hukm shar'i taken in fiqh) in the meaning of 'that which depends' becomes specific, and the boundary of hukm shar'i (khatab Allah) is more general than it, so the boundary would be more general than the defined term. His saying: 'fa al-hukmu 'ala hadha' i.e., on this assumption, when the definition of hukm shar'i is khatab Allah ta'ala, then the definition of absolute hukm is 'attribution of command to the intended person' etc., and khatab Allah ta'ala will not be the definition of absolute hukm, otherwise in the definition of fiqh the restriction of shar'iyya with al-ahkam would be redundant because when the definition of hukm shar'i is khatab Allah ta'ala, then the meaning of shar'i is 'what is brought by the address of the Shari'a' not 'what depends on the Shari'a', then surely in the definition of fiqh as al-'ilm bi al-ahkam al-shar'iyya, the mention of shar'iyya would be repetitive because this is the meaning of hukm and this is the meaning of shar'iyya. If it is said: the gist of the question is that at that time the shar'i rulings of fiqh would include wujub al-iman etc., although these are not among the shar'i rulings of fiqh. We say, with the reply [given] that later the restriction of 'amaliyya mentioned in the definition of fiqh will exclude them. His saying: 'wa al-fuqaha' i.e., in the terminology of jurists, hukm is truly called 'what is established by address' such as wujub and hurma, even though this is a linguistic metaphor because linguistically it is the application of the masdar to the maf'ul, i.e., applying al-hukm to al-mahkum, but in juristic terminology it becomes real. His saying 'ma [naqasa] 'alayhi' the definition of hukm, although the author has answered some of the objections and not others. The first [objection]: the intended meaning is that the main intended definition was of that hukm which is conventional among the jurists, and they call 'what is established by address' hukm, like wujub and hurma which are attributes of the act of the mukallaf. The jurists do not call the address itself, which is among the attributes of Allah ta'ala, a hukm. In summary, what was intended was not defined; what was defined is not intended. It was answered in several ways: first, just as applying hukm to ma thabata bi al-khitab is not in the masdar meaning, but rather it means 'what is judged' similarly in the definition of hukm, the word khitab is intended to mean 'what is addressed' due to a rational indicator (qarina 'aqliyya), i.e., reason witnesses that the word hukm mentioned in the definition of fiqh intends wujub and hurma, and wujub and hurma are not names of the address itself but rather names of 'what is addressed', so khitab is intended to mean 'what is addressed'. Second, [summary]: that truly hukm is not the name of wujub and hurma, but rather the name of ijab and tahrim which are among the divine attributes, so using the word khitab Allah in its definition is correct, and there is no need to interpret it as 'what is addressed'. And wujub and hurma are called hukm by tolerance since hukm in the meaning of ijab and tahrim are their effects, so they are metaphorically called hukm. Third: that hukm is itself the name of khitab Allah, because ijab is the saying 'do' but this saying does not produce a real attribute subsisting in the action of the mukallaf; and since this saying is related to the non-existent, there is no attribute derived from the saying standing for the action of the mukallaf. Rather this saying, the address itself, is hukm. When it is attributed to the ruler, it is called ijab; when attributed to the action concerning which this saying occurred, it is called wujub. So wujub and ijab are not identical in essence because both are exactly the name of the saying 'do' and differ by consideration: by consideration of attribution to the ruler it is ijab; by attribution to the action of the mukallaf it is wujub. In any case, truly it is the name of the address itself, so there is no need for interpretation as 'what is addressed'. Therefore, since there is unity in essence between ijab and wujub, these scholars sometimes state the divisions of hukm as wujub and hurma, and sometimes as ijab and tahrim, and sometimes as wujub and tahrim, as in usul of Ibn Hajib. The second [objection]: that it is not reciprocal (ghayr mun'akis), i.e., this definition is not comprehensive of all individuals because this definition contains the word 'actions of the mukallafin' whereas rulings concerning actions of non-mukallafin...

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion on the definition of hukm shar'i as presented in the text. The author examines a prior definition that defines hukm as khatab Allah ta'ala (the address of Allah) and then analyses its implications for the definition of fiqh as knowledge of shar'i rulings. The key issue is whether the restriction 'shar'iyya' in the definition of fiqh becomes redundant if hukm itself includes the shar'i element. The discussion also addresses the scope of fiqh, specifically whether rulings like wujub al-iman (obligation of faith) should be included in fiqh or not. The passage then presents three objections to the definition of hukm and their respective responses. The first objection concerns the mismatch between what is defined (khatab Allah) and what is intended (what is established by address, i.e., wujub and hurma). The responses include rational interpretation, metaphorical usage, and the view that hukm is actually the address itself. The second objection (incomplete at the page end) points that the definition is not comprehensive because it includes only actions of mukallafin, whereas rulings exist for non-mukallaf actions as well. The commentary follows the author's order: first explaining the consequences of taking 'shar'i' in different senses, then presenting the objections and responses. All arguments are within the Hanafi usul tradition, with references to rational proofs and the authority of jurists' terminology.

Key Terms
حکم شرعی (hukm sharʿī): The definition under debate: khaṭāb Allāh taʿālā (address of Allah) or what is established by that address (wujub, hurma).
ما ثبت بالخطاب (mā thabata bi al-khiṭāb): What is established by the address, i.e., the ruling (wujub, hurma) that becomes an attribute of the action.
خطاب اللہ (khiṭāb Allāh): The divine address itself, considered by some as the real hukm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the responses to the first objection (that the definition defines the address not the ruling)?
A) Using a rational indicator to interpret khitab as ma khutiba bihi.
B) Arguing that hukm is truly the address itself.
C) Claiming that the definition of fiqh excludes wujub al-iman.
D) Establishing the identity of ijab and wujub.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi responses to objections demonstrate that defining hukm as khatab Allah is defensible through careful interpretation of terminology.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
10 min
Inclusion of Actions of Minors in the Definition of Hukm
Debating whether Ash'ari definition of hukm excluding minors is valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Ash'ari definition of hukm through the Hanafi critique concerning actions of minors, and identify the key points of the dispute.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm must encompass all actions of servants, including minors, because wad'i rulings and direct shari obligations apply to them.

This passage presents a dispute between the Ash'ari school and the Hanafi-oriented author regarding the proper definition of hukm. The Ash'aris restrict hukm to actions of mukallafeen (legally responsible persons). The Hanafis object that this excludes rulings that clearly pertain to minors, such as the validity of their sale, Islam, and prayer. The text works through objections and counter-objections, ultimately criticizing the Ash'ari commentator's responses as forced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the Ash'ari definition of hukm and the Hanafi objection: the definition should include actions of all 'ibad (servants), not just mukallafeen.
2
Examine the Ash'ari response
The Ash'ari commentator claims that rulings appearing to relate to minors actually concern the guardian (wali) because minors are not addressed by law.
3
Analyze the author's two-part rebuttal
The author lists direct rulings on minors (validity of sale, Islam, prayer) and argues that the attachment of a right to the minor's property/liability is a ruling itself, not the guardian's action.
4
Evaluate the commentator's counter-arguments
The commentator argues that sihha/fasād are rational rulings and that recommendation of prayer is directed at the guardian. Note the hadith cited.
5
Assess the Hanafi rejoinder conclusion
The text refutes each counter-argument, showing the original obligation is on the minor, sihha depends on Shariah, and wad'i rulings apply. The commentator's arguments are deemed forced.

ساتھ متعلق ہیں مثلاً جو احکام افعال صبیان کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں وہ اس تعریف سے خارج ہو یہ ہے ہیں حالانکہ وہ بھی افراد حکم میں ہیں۔ فالا ولی ان یقال تو بہتر یہ تھا کہ افعال مکلفین کی بجائے افعال العباد کہنا چاہئے تھا ۔ وقد اجيب عن ذلك في كتبهم الى كتب الاشاعره بان الاحكام یعنی وہ احکام جن کے متعلق یہ خیال گذرتا ہے کہ یہ فعل صبح کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں وہ حقیقتاً فعل صبح کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں بلکہ فعل ولی کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتے ہیں جیسے ولی پر ہی واجب ہے کہ وہ مال صبی سے حقوق ادا کرے اور ولی تو مکلف ہے لہذا متعلق با فعال المکلفین ہو گئے۔
وردة المصنف أو لا مصنف نے اولاً اس جواب کو بایں طور رد کیا کہ صبی کی بیع کا جائز ہوتا جب کہ اس کو ولی سے اذن حاصل ہو ۔ صحة اسلامہ یعنی اسلامی اعمال کا مع الاقرار ادا کرنا كما هو مذكور معنى الاسلام فی الحدیث اسی طرح صحت صلوٰۃ اور اس کا مندوب ہونا یہ تمام امور ایسے ہیں جو براہ راست صبح کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں اور ان امور میں ولی کو کوئی دخل بھی نہیں ہے تو تعلق بفعل الولی کا جواب کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے و ثانیا یعنی ثانیا اس جواب کو رد کرتے ہوئے کہا تعلق الحق بمال الصبی اور تعلق حق بذمہ صبی یہ ایک ایسی شئی ہے جس کا تعلق صبح کے ساتھ ہے اور پھر اس کے بعد ولی کا ادا کرنا ایک ایسا حکم ہے جو اس پر مرتب ہے اس کا عین نہیں ہے تو اعتراض ان امور کے متعلق تھا جن کا تعلق صیبی سے ہے لہذا ان کے متعلق تعلق بفعل الولی کا حجاب درست نہیں ہے۔
ولا يتأتى هذا السوال شارح یہاں سے رد على المصنف کر رہا ہے کہ فعل صبی کا سوال کرے سے ان اشاعرہ پر واقع ہی نہیں ہوتا جنہوں نے حکم کی تعریف مذکور کی ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک کوئی حکم متعلق بالصبی ہے ہی نہیں بجز اداء الحق من مالہ کے اور یہ ادائے حق ولی کے ذمہ ہے نہ کہ بذمہ صبی لہذا تعریف حکم پر اعتراض بفعل الصبی بے فائدہ ہے ۔
تو لا یخفی پھر یہ بھی مخفی نہیں ہے کہ تعلق الحق بمالہ وذمتہ کسی صورت میں حکم ہو ہی نہیں سکتا کیونکہ اس کا تعلق بالا فعال نہیں ہے اگرچہ المکلفین کے بجائے العباد لے آئیں تو داخل فی الحکم نہیں ہو سکتا جب یہ افراد محدود سے نہیں ہے تو اس کو داخل تحت المحد کر نیکی سعی فضول و عبث ہے وبان الصحة والفساد مصنف نے جواز بیع و صحتہ اسلام صبح کے متعلق کہا تھا کہ اس کا تعلق بفعل ولی نہیں ہے تو اس کے متعلق شارح رد کر رہا ہے کہ صحت و فساد سرے سے احکام شرعیہ میں سے نہیں ہیں بلکہ یہ احکام عقلیہ ہیں کیونکہ صحت کا مفہوم کون الماتی به موافقا لما ورد به الشرع ہے یعنی جو چیز لائی گئی ہے اور ادا کی گئی اگر یہ موافق شریعت ہے تو اس کا نام صحتہ ہے اگر مخالف ہے تو اس کا نام فساد ہے اب ایک امر کا شریعت کے موافق و مخالف ہونا یہ مدرک بالعقل ہے لہذا یہ احکام عقلیہ میں سے ہیں نہ احکام شرعیہ سے لہذا ان کا احکام شرعیہ سے خارج رہنا ہی مناسب ہے جیسے ایک شخص کا مصلی ہونا یا تارک صلوٰۃ ہونا احکام شرعیہ میں درج نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ احکام عقلیہ یا حسیہ ہیں اور جواز بیع کا معنی صحت بیع ہے جو کہ احکام عقلیہ میں سے ہے شرعیہ میں سے نہیں ومعنی کون صلاته مندوبة صبح کی صلوٰۃ کا مندوب ہونا یہ بھی فعل صبی کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہے بلکہ فعل ولی کے ساتھ متعلق ہے یعنی ولی مامور ہے کہ صبی کو صلوٰۃ کی ادائیگی پر تحریض ترغیب کرے اور اس کو امر کرے نماز کے ادا کرنے کا یہی معنی ہے کون صلوۃ الصبی مندوبہ کا جیسے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے مروهم بالصلوٰۃ وهم ابناء سبع ۔ شارج نے جو مصنف پر رد کیا ہے یہ تمام کا تمام مبنی على التعسف ہے۔ اولاً جو کہا کہ فعل صبی کے ساتھ کوئی حکم متعلق نہیں بلکہ فعل ولی کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں کیونکہ ادائے حقوق از مال صبی ولی پر واجب ہے اس کا جواب یوں دیا گیا ہے کہ ادار الحق من مال الصبی کا وجوب یہ مسبوق ہے بثبوت الحق في ماله او ذ متہ یعنی اولاً ادائے حقوق ذمہ صبی اور مال صبی میں واجب ہوگا تو پھر ادائیگی ہوگی جب وجوب اولاً بذمہ صبی ہے تو ہ دار بھی اولا میسی پر واجب ہوگی البتہ شریعت نے ولی کو نا ئب فی الا درہ قرار دیا ہے تو نیا بہ ادا وہی کرے گا تو اصالہ اور اولاً خطاب کا تعلق فعل صبح سے ہوگا چونکہ وہ مکلف نہیں ہے اور مکلفین کا لفظ اس کو شامل نہیں لہذا عباد کا لفظ ہوتا کہ اس کو شامل ہو سکے۔
ثانیاً یہ کہ فعل صیبی کے ساتھ جو خطاب متعلق ہے اگرچہ حکم تکلیفی میں داخل نہ ہو تو اس سے تو انکار نہیں ہو سکتا کہ اتلاف صبی یعنی صبی کسی دوسرے شخص کے مال کو تلف کر دے تو یہ سبب ہے وجوب ضمان کا تو اس صورت میں حکم وضعی کے اندر داخل ہو گا تو بھی بجائے مکلفین کے عباد ہوتا کہ یہ حکم وضعی حکم کی تعریف میں داخل ہو سکے پھر شارح نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ تعلق حقی ہمالہ و بذمتہ حکم نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اس کا تعلق بالا فعال نہیں ہے یہ بھی تحسف من الشارح ہے کیونکہ تعلق حق جمال الصبی و بذمتہ یہ ایسے ہی ہے جیسے تعلق حق بمالی البالغ ہوتا ہے مراد اس سے یہ ہوتی ہے کہ شریعت حکم دیتی ہے کہ اس کے مال سے اتنا مقدار ادا کی جائے لہذا یہ حکم شرعی تو ہوا لیکن مکلفین کا لفظ اس کو تعریف میں داخل نہیں ہونے دیتا اس لئے لفظ عباد کا لانا بہتر ہے۔ شارح نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ صحت و فساد احکام شرعیہ میں سے نہیں بلکہ یہ احکام عقلیہ میں سے ہے یہ بھی مبنی بر تعسف ہے کیونکہ عقل کے ساتھ یہ معلوم کرنا کہ ماتی به موافق شرع ہے یا مخالف یہ حکم بعد ورود الشرع ہو سکتا ہے لہذا موافقت و مخالفت کا فیصلہ دینا موقوف على الشرع
They are related; for example, rulings that are related to actions of minors are excluded from this definition, even though they are also instances of hukm. So first, it would be better to say 'actions of servants' instead of 'actions of legally responsible persons.' And it has been answered in their books to the Ash'ari books that the rulings regarding which it is thought that they are related to the action of the minor, in reality they are not related to the action of the minor but are related to the action of the guardian, just as it is obligatory upon the guardian to discharge rights from the property of the minor, and the guardian is mukallaf, so they become related to the actions of the mukallafeen. Then the author first rejected this answer in this manner: The validity of the minor's sale occurs when he has permission from his guardian; the validity of his Islam, i.e., performing Islamic actions with acknowledgment, as the meaning of Islam is mentioned in the hadith; similarly, the validity of his prayer and its being recommended—all these matters are directly related to the minor, and the guardian has no involvement in these matters; so how can the answer of relation to the action of the guardian be correct? And secondly, while rejecting this answer, he said: The attachment of a right to the property of the minor and the attachment of a right to the liability of the minor are a thing that is related to the minor, and thereafter the guardian's discharge is a ruling that is consequent upon it, not the same thing. So the objection was concerning those matters that are related to the minor; therefore, the answer of relation to the action of the guardian is not correct for them. And this question does not arise here; the commentator from here is refuting the author, saying that the question of the action of the minor does not actually apply to those Ash'aris who mentioned the definition of hukm, because according to them, no ruling is related to the minor except the discharge of a right from his property, and this discharge of right is the responsibility of the guardian, not the liability of the minor; therefore, the objection to the definition of hukm regarding the action of the minor is futile. Then it is not hidden that the attachment of a right to his property and liability cannot in any case be a hukm because it is not related to actions; even if we bring 'the servants' instead of 'the legally responsible,' it cannot be included in hukm. Since it is not from the limited individuals, striving to include it under the limited is futile and absurd. And regarding sihha and fasād: The author said that the permissibility of sale and validity of the minor's Islam are related to the minor, that they are not related to the action of the guardian. Concerning this, the commentator refutes that sihha and fasād are not from the legal rulings at all; rather, they are rational rulings because the meaning of sihha is 'the thing brought being in accordance with what the Shariah has brought' i.e., if a thing is brought and performed, if it is in accordance with the Shariah, its name is sihha; if it is contrary, its name is fasād. Now, the conformity or opposition of a matter to the Shariah is known by reason; therefore, they are from rational rulings, not from legal rulings. Hence, their being outside legal rulings is appropriate, just as a person's being a person praying or a person abandoning prayer is not included in legal rulings; rather, these are rational or sensory rulings. And the meaning of permissibility of sale is the validity of the sale, which is from rational rulings, not from legal ones. And the meaning of 'his prayer being recommended'—the minor's prayer being recommended—this too is not related to the action of the minor but is related to the action of the guardian, i.e., the guardian is commanded to incite and encourage the minor to perform prayer and to command him to perform prayer; this is the meaning of 'the minor's prayer being recommended,' just as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Command them to pray when they are seven years old.' The commentator's refutation of the author is entirely based on force. Firstly, what he said that no ruling is related to the action of the minor, but they are related to the action of the guardian, because the discharge of rights from the property of the minor is obligatory upon the guardian; it is answered that the obligation of discharging rights from the property of the minor is preceded by the establishment of the right in his property or liability. That is, initially, the discharge of rights is obligatory in the liability of the minor and his property; then the discharge occurs. When the obligation is initially upon the liability of the minor, then the due is also initially upon him. However, the Shariah has made the guardian a deputy in the discharge; so the deputy performs the discharge. Thus, the original and primary address is related to the action of the minor; since he is not mukallaf and the word 'mukallafeen' does not include him, therefore, the word 'ibad' would be used to include him. Secondly, that the address related to the action of the minor, even if it is not included in taklifi rulings, it cannot be denied that the minor's causing damage, i.e., the minor destroys another person's property, then this is a cause for the obligation of compensation; in this case, it will be included in wad'i rulings. So also, instead of 'mukallafeen,' 'ibad' would be used so that this wad'i ruling could be included in the definition of hukm. Then the commentator said that the attachment of a right to his property and liability cannot be a hukm because it is not related to actions; this too is force from the commentator because the attachment of a right to the property of the minor and his liability is just like the attachment of a right to the property of an adult. By this, it is meant that the Shariah rules that such an amount be discharged from his property; therefore, it is a legal ruling, but the word 'mukallafeen' does not allow it to enter the definition. Hence, bringing the word 'ibad' is better. The commentator's saying that sihha and fasād are not from legal rulings but from rational rulings is also based on force because to know with reason whether what is brought is in accordance with the Shariah or contrary is a judgment that can only occur after the advent of the Shariah; therefore, deciding conformity or opposition is dependent on the Shariah.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the definition of 'hukm' (legal ruling) as given by the Ash'ari school and whether it correctly includes or excludes actions of minors (sighar). The opening lines state the objection: the Ash'ari definition restricts rulings to actions of mukallafeen (legally responsible persons), but there are rulings that clearly pertain to minors, such as the validity of their sale, the validity of their Islam, and the recommendation of their prayer. Therefore, the objector suggests that the definition should use 'af'al al-'ibad' (actions of servants) instead of 'af'al al-mukallafeen'. The text then presents the Ash'ari response, found in their books: those rulings that seem to relate to minors actually relate to the guardian (wali), because it is the guardian who is obligated to discharge rights from the minor's property. The author (musannif) is then quoted as rejecting this response in two ways: first, by listing rulings that directly concern the minor without guardian involvement—validity of sale (which requires permission but is the minor's action), validity of Islam (the minor's own acknowledgement), validity of prayer and its recommendation—all are directly about the minor, not the guardian. Second, the attachment of a right to the minor's property or liability is itself a ruling (hukm) that pertains to the minor; the guardian's subsequent discharge is a separate ruling consequent upon it. The commentator (sharh) then refutes the author, arguing that according to the Ash'aris, no ruling actually attaches to the minor except the discharge of rights, which is the guardian's responsibility, so the objection misses its mark. The commentator further argues that the attachment of a right is not a ruling because it is not related to an action, and even if one substitutes 'af'al al-ibad', it still does not fit because it is not an action. He then addresses the points about sihha (validity) and fasad (corruption), claiming they are not legal rulings (ahkam shar'iyya) but rational rulings (ahkam aqliyya), because determining compliance with Shariah is a rational judgment. Similarly, the recommendation of a minor's prayer is actually a recommendation for the guardian to command the minor, based on the hadith 'Command them to pray at seven.' The text then criticizes the commentator's refutation as forced (mabni 'ala al-ta'assuf). It provides counterarguments: first, the obligation to discharge rights from the minor's property is preceded by the right being established on the minor's liability or property, so the original obligation is on the minor; the guardian is merely a deputy. Hence the primary address is to the minor, but he is not mukallaf, so 'ibad' would be more inclusive. Second, the minor's actions like causing damage (itlaf) give rise to wad'i rulings (e.g., liability for compensation), which are also rulings. Third, the attachment of a right is indeed a legal ruling, similar to that for adults, but the term 'mukallafeen' excludes minors, so again 'ibad' is better. Finally, sihha and fasad cannot be purely rational because they depend on Shariah; determination of conformity requires prior knowledge of the law, thus they are legal rulings. This debate highlights a core issue in usul al-fiqh: the scope of the definition of hukm and whether it must be confined to actions of those who are legally capable (mukallaf). The Hanafi position, as reflected in the musannif's reasoning, tends to include rulings that affect minors, either directly or via guardianship, and thus prefers a broader definition using 'af'al al-ibad'.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): A legal ruling as defined by Ash'aris: a communication from the Lawgiver concerning the actions of mukallafeen. The passage challenges this definition by arguing it should include all actions of servants.
صحة (sihha): The attribute of an act being in conformity with Shariah; argued by some to be a rational ruling (hukm aqli) but here defended as a legal ruling (hukm shar'i).
فساد (fasād): The attribute of an act being contrary to Shariah; like sihha, debated as rational vs. legal.
مكلف (mukallaf): A legally responsible person, i.e., one who is adult, sane, and has ability (ahliyya) to be addressed by Shariah.
صبي (sabi): A minor child who is not mukallaf. The text discusses whether rulings address him directly or through his guardian.
ولي (wali): Guardian, who is responsible for managing the minor's affairs and discharging his duties.
حكم تكليفي (hukm taklifi): A ruling that involves a demand (command, prohibition) upon a mukallaf.
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): A ruling that establishes a cause, condition, or preventer; e.g., causation of liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does the commentator (sharh) argue that sihha (validity) is not a legal ruling (hukm shar'i)?
A) Because it applies only to minors, not to mukallafeen.
B) Because it is determined by reason, not by Shariah.
C) Because it does not involve an action.
D) Because it is a wad'i ruling, not a taklifi ruling.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm in Hanafi usul should encompass all servants (ibad), not only mukallafeen, because rulings of validity, recommendation, and wad'i causation apply to minors directly.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Including Children in Hukm Shari
Refuting the claim that children are outside hukm shari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that children's actions are subject to hukm wadi and hukm taklifi through guardians, identify the reasoning for preferring 'ibad' over 'mukallafin', and evaluate the commentator's arguments.

Core Idea
Children's actions are subject to hukm wadi and, via guardians, to hukm taklifi; the definition of hukm must use 'ibad' to include them.

This passage tackles a fundamental definitional issue in usul al-fiqh: should the definition of hukm shari be limited to actions of the mukallaf? The commentator argues yes, while the author (following Hanafi fuqaha) insists that children are not entirely outside shari rulings—they are addressed through guardians and through hukm wadi. The debate hinges on the proper terminology and scope of the definition. This lesson unpacks the arguments, examines the key hadith, and clarifies why 'ibad' is the preferred term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Dispute
What does the commentator claim about children and hukm? State the author's counter-claim. The commentator argues that no hukm connects to the child's action; the author says hukm wadi (e.g., liability for damage) and hukm taklifi (via guardian commands) both apply.
2
Analyze the Dalil
How does the hadith 'مروهم بالصلوٰۃ وهم ابناء سبع' support the author? The imperative 'muru' shows that sharia addresses children's actions through guardians, proving a shari connection.
This is a zanni dalil, but sufficient for the point.
3
Examine the Definition Refinement
Why does the author propose replacing 'mukallafin' with 'ibad'? Because 'mukallafin' excludes children, but hukm wadi (like daman) and hukm taklifi (via guardians) apply to them. 'Ibad' is broader and inclusive.
Consider the thamarah: children's actions are mandub or valid/invalid in a shari sense.
4
Evaluate the Refutation
How does the author refute the commentator's views on validity/corruption and mandub? Validity (sihha) according to fuqaha is discharging duty, a shari concept (not rational). Mandub for the child's prayer is not limited to guardian encouragement—the child can earn reward directly (e.g., Ali's pride).
The commentator follows Mutakallimin definition; author insists on fuqaha's terminology.

الصبی مندوبہ کا جیسے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے مروهم بالصلوٰۃ وهم ابناء سبع ۔ شارج نے جو مصنف پر رد کیا ہے یہ تمام کا تمام مبنی على التعسف ہے۔ اولاً جو کہا کہ فعل صبی کے ساتھ کوئی حکم ادائے حقوق ذمہ صبی اور مال صبی میں واجب ہوگا تو پھر ادائیگی ہوگی جب وجوب اولاً بذمہ صبی ہے تو ہ دار بھی اولا میسی پر واجب ہوگی البتہ شریعت نے ولی کو نا ئب فی الا درہ قرار دیا ہے تو نیا بہ ادا وہی کرے گا تو اصالہ اور اولاً خطاب کا تعلق فعل صبح سے ہوگا چونکہ وہ مکلف نہیں ہے اور مکلفین کا لفظ اس کو شامل نہیں لہذا عباد کا لفظ ہوتا کہ اس کو شامل ہو سکے۔ ثانیاً یہ کہ فعل صیبی کے ساتھ جو خطاب متعلق ہے اگرچہ حکم تکلیفی میں داخل نہ ہو تو اس سے تو انکار نہیں ہو سکتا کہ اتلاف صبی یعنی صبی کسی دوسرے شخص کے مال کو تلف کر دے تو یہ سبب ہے وجوب ضمان کا تو اس صورت میں حکم وضعی کے اندر داخل ہو گا تو بھی بجائے مکلفین کے عباد ہوتا کہ یہ حکم وضعی حکم کی تعریف میں داخل ہو سکے پھر شارح نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ تعلق حقی ہمالہ و بذمتہ حکم نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اس کا تعلق بالا فعال نہیں ہے یہ بھی تحسف من الشارح ہے کیونکہ تعلق حق جمال الصبی و بذمتہ یہ ایسے ہی ہے جیسے تعلق حق بمالی البالغ ہوتا ہے مراد اس سے یہ ہوتی ہے کہ شریعت حکم دیتی ہے کہ اس کے مال سے اتنا مقدار ادا کی جائے لہذا یہ حکم شرعی تو ہوا لیکن مکلفین کا لفظ اس کو تعریف میں داخل نہیں ہونے دیتا اس لئے لفظ عباد کا لانا بہتر ہے۔ شارح نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ صحت و فساد احکام شرعیہ میں سے نہیں بلکہ یہ احکام عقلیہ میں سے ہے یہ بھی مبنی بر تعسف ہے کیونکہ عقل کے ساتھ یہ معلوم کرنا کہ ماتی به موافق شرع ہے یا مخالف یہ حکم بعد ورود الشرع ہو سکتا ہے لہذا موافقت و مخالفت کا فیصلہ دینا موقوف على الشرع ہوا تو یہ حکم شرعی ہوگا نہ کہ عقلی ثانیا یہ کہ صحت و فساد کا جو مفہوم شارح نے پیش کیا ہے یہ مذہب متکلمین پر ہے نہ کہ مذہب فقہا پر حالانکہ یہاں مفہوم اصطلاح فقہا۔ والا معتبر ہے اور اما مذہب الفقہاء من الشافعية فصحة الفعل عبارة عن كونه مسقطاً للقضاء والفساد خلافه و هذا امر شرعی بلاشبہہ کیونکہ مسقط قضاء ہونا یا نہ ہونا اس کی معرفت شریعت سے حاصل ہوتی ہے لہذا یہ احکام شرعیہ میں درج ہے نہ کہ عقلیہ میں ۔ اس کے بعد شارح نے جو صلوٰۃ صبح کے مندوب ہونے کا مفہوم پیش کیا ہے کہ ولی مامور ہے کہ اسے ترغیب دے یہ بالکل تعسف ظاہر ہے کیونکہ مندوب کا معنی استحقاق ثواب ہے تحریض ولی اس سے ایک امر خارج ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ اپنے بچپن میں اسلام لانے پر فخر کیا کرتے تھے اور ثانیاً یہ کہ ایسا صبی جو ممیز ہے اس کا کوئی ولی اور متولی نہیں ہے اور نہ کسی نے اسے تحریض و ترغیب کی ہے اگر لوگوں کو دیکھ کر وہ صلوٰۃ وصوم ادا کرتا ہے تو ندب اس میں موجود ہے یہاں ولی کا کوئی تعلق بھی نہیں ہے اس کے متعلق شارح کیا جواب دے گا بہر حال مکلفین کی بجائے لفظ عباد بہتر ہے
It is named corruption. Now the conformity or opposition of a matter to sharia is intellectually perceived, so these are rational rulings, not sharia rulings; thus it is appropriate for them to remain outside sharia rulings. For example, a person being a prayer-offerer or a prayer-abandoner is not included among sharia rulings; rather they are rational or sensory rulings. And the permissibility of a sale means its validity, which is among rational rulings, not sharia ones. And the meaning of 'his prayer being mandub' – the morning prayer being mandub – is not connected to the child's action but to the guardian's action: the guardian is commanded to motivate and encourage the child to perform prayer and to command him to do so. That is the meaning of 'the child's prayer being mandub', as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Command them to pray when they are seven years old.' The commentator's refutation of the author is entirely based on misrepresentation. Firstly, his claim that no ruling is connected to the child's action, but rather to the guardian's action, because the guardian is obligated to discharge rights from the child's wealth – the response given is: the obligation of discharging rights from the child's wealth is preceded by the establishment of the right in his wealth or liability; meaning, firstly the discharge of rights becomes obligatory upon the child's liability and wealth, then the discharge occurs. Since the initial obligation is upon the child's liability, the command is also initially upon him; the sharia has appointed the guardian as a deputy in performance, so the deputy will perform. Therefore, the address essentially and initially connects to the child's action; since he is not a legally responsible person (mukallaf) and the word 'mukallafin' does not include him, the word 'ibad' (servants) would include him. Secondly, the connection of the address to the child's action, even if it does not enter into hukm taklifi, cannot be denied: if a child destroys someone else's property, it is a cause for the obligation of compensation; in that case it enters into hukm wadi. So also there, instead of 'mukallafin', 'ibad' would be better so that this hukm wadi could enter the definition. Then the commentator's statement that the connection of the right to the child's wealth or liability cannot be a ruling because it does not connect to actions is also misrepresentation by the commentator, because the connection of the right to the child's wealth or liability is like the connection of the right to the wealth of an adult – the meaning is that sharia rules that this amount should be paid from his wealth. So this is a sharia ruling, but the word 'mukallafin' does not allow it to enter the definition; thus the word 'ibad' is better. What the commentator said – that validity and corruption are not among sharia rulings but rather among rational rulings – is also based on misrepresentation, because determining by reason whether something conforms to or opposes sharia can only be after the revelation of sharia. Therefore, deciding conformity or opposition depends on sharia, so it is a sharia ruling, not a rational one. Secondly, the meaning of validity and corruption that the commentator presented is according to the school of the Mutakallimin, not the Fuqaha; however here the meaning according to the terminology of the Fuqaha is accepted. According to the school of the Fuqaha among the Shafi'is, the validity of an act is defined as its being a means of discharging the qada (duty), and corruption is the opposite. This is undoubtedly a sharia matter because whether it discharges the qada or not is known from sharia. Therefore, it is included among sharia rulings, not rational ones. Afterwards, the commentator's presentation of the meaning of the morning prayer being mandub – that the guardian is commanded to encourage it – is clearly a misrepresentation, because the meaning of mandub is deserving of reward; the guardian's encouragement is a separate matter. This is why Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) used to take pride in having embraced Islam in his childhood. Secondly, a child who is discerning may have no guardian or caretaker, and no one encourages or motivates him; if he performs prayer and fasting by observing people, then mandub is present in his action. Here the guardian has no connection. What answer will the commentator give regarding this? In any case, instead of 'mukallafin', the word 'ibad' is better.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the commentator's claim that children's actions are not subject to shari rulings. The author argues that children's actions are connected to hukm wadi (e.g., liability for damage) and, through guardians, to hukm taklifi. The hadith 'Command them to pray at seven' shows that sharia addresses children indirectly. The commentator's view that validity/corruption are rational is rejected as based on the Mutakallimin's definition, not the Fuqaha's; for the Fuqaha, validity is a shari concept (discharging duty). The author also rejects the commentator's interpretation of mandub for the child's prayer as merely the guardian's encouragement, arguing that the child's own action can be mandub, as seen in Ali's pride in early Islam and in cases where a discerning child prays without a guardian.

Key Terms
حکم وضعی (hukm wadi): A shari ruling that establishes a cause, condition, or preventer for a legal effect, without directly requiring action or abstinence.
مکلف (mukallaf): A person who is legally responsible and addressed by shari obligations (taklif).
مندوب (mandub): An action whose performance is recommended but not obligatory; deserving of reward.
صحت (sihha): Validity of an act: according to the Fuqaha, discharging the duty (isqat al-qada).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author prefer the term 'ibad' over 'mukallafin' in the definition of hukm shari?
A) Because 'ibad' is a Qur'anic term that sounds more respectful.
B) Because 'ibad' includes children, who are subject to hukm wadi and hukm taklifi via guardians.
C) Because the commentator refused to use 'mukallafin'.
D) Because 'ibad' is easier to pronounce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position emphasizes that children are within the scope of hukm shari, requiring the definition to use 'ibad' rather than 'mukallafin' to include them.

Scope of Fi'l al-Mukallaf: Including Heart Actions
Responding to objections that the definition excludes actions of the heart and theoretical beliefs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school includes actions of the heart and theoretical matters under 'fi'l al-mukallaf' and assess the impact on the definition of hukm.

Core Idea
Fi'l al-mukallaf includes both heart actions and physical actions — shari rulings apply to both.

In this passage, the author tackles two objections that the definition of hukm is too narrow: it excludes actions of the heart (like belief) and theoretical matters. The response hinges on the interpretation of 'fi'l al-mukallaf'. Understanding this expansion is crucial for a correct grasp of the scope of Islamic rulings in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objections
State the fourth and fifth objections: the definition excludes actions of the heart (e.g., obligation of iman) and theoretical matters (nazariyyat), limiting rulings to physical actions.
The objectors assume 'fi'l' is only physical.
2
Locate the Hanafi response
The answer is that 'fi'l al-mukallaf' is general ('amm) and includes both physical and heart actions.
The text ends mid-sentence but the principle is clear.
3
Dissect the legal definition
Analyze 'fi'l al-mukallaf' as a technical term: it is the object of hukm, encompassing any voluntary action by the mukallaf, whether external or internal.
Hanafi usul emphasizes linguistic generality.
4
Apply the definition
Show how rulings like wajib al-iman (obligation of belief) are included under this broad definition, as well as theoretical obligations like i'tibar and qiyas.
This defends the definition's comprehensiveness.
5
Evaluate the impact
Understand that this expansion means shari rulings cover internal acts (intentions, beliefs) and theoretical knowledge, not just limb actions.
This aligns with the scope of fiqh as per Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع انه غیر شامل چوتھا اعتراض یہ ہے کہ یہ تعریف ان احکام کو شامل نہیں ہے جو افعان قلب سے متعلق ہیں جیسے وجوب الایمان بمعنی التصدیق اور وجوب الاعتبار والقیاس کیونکہ حکم کی تعریف میں جو افعال المکلفین کا لفظ ہے اس سے متبادر افعال الجوارح ہیں الخامس پانچواں اعتراض یہ کہ جب تعریف حکم میں تعلق بفعل المکلف ہے تو مختص بالعملیات ہو جائے گا نظریات نکل جائیں گے کیونکہ فعل مكلف مختص بفعل الجوارح ہے لہذا تہ ریف فقہ میں العملیہ کی قید لغو اور ضائع ہو جائے گی۔ واجاب عنهما ان دونوں اعتراضوں سے یعنی رابع وخامس سے جواب دیا کہ فعل مکلف سے مراد عام ہے خواہ
The fourth: it is not inclusive. The fourth objection is that this definition does not include those rulings that relate to actions of the heart, such as the obligation of iman in the sense of tasdiq (affirmation) and the obligation of i'tibar (taking lesson) and qiyas, because in the definition of hukm the word 'af'al al-mukallafin' (actions of the legally responsible) is used, and from it the apparent meaning is physical actions (af'al al-jawarih). The fifth: the fifth objection is that when the definition of hukm connects to the action of the mukallaf, it will be limited to practical matters (amaliyyat), and theoretical matters (nazariyyat) will be excluded, because the action of the mukallaf is specifically physical actions. Therefore, the restriction of 'amaliyya' in the definition of fiqh would be redundant. And the answer to both: these two objections, i.e., the fourth and fifth, are answered by saying that 'fi'l al-mukallaf' is general, whether...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth and fifth objections to the definition of hukm. The fourth objection says that rulings about actions of the heart (e.g., obligation of faith) are not covered because 'fi'l al-mukallaf' is understood as physical actions. The fifth objection says that the definition would only cover practical matters, excluding theoretical matters like belief, making the 'amaliyya' qualification in fiqh definition redundant. The combined response is that 'fi'l al-mukallaf' is general and includes both physical and heart actions. The text ends mid-sentence, but the response continues on the next page.

Key Terms
افعال قلب (af'al al-qalb): Actions of the heart, such as belief (iman), intention, and reflection.
نظریات (nazariyyat): Theoretical matters that are objects of belief and knowledge, as opposed to practical actions.
عملیات (amaliyyat): Practical actions performed by the limbs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He says that theoretical matters are not part of fiqh.
D) He claims that actions of the heart are not subject to hukm.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'fi'l al-mukallaf' is interpreted broadly to include both physical actions and actions of the heart, thus making the definition of hukm inclusive of rulings on belief and theoretical matters.

Objections to the Definition of Hukm Shar'i and Responses
Critiquing and defending the Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five main objections to the Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i as khitab Allah and explain how Hanafi usul scholars responded, particularly regarding qiyas, heart actions, and the qualification 'amaliyya'.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm shar'i is defended by showing qiyas as a manifestation, heart actions as included, and 'amaliyya' as a necessary qualifier to exclude theoretical rulings.

In this lesson, we examine several objections raised against the Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i. The commentator systematically addresses each objection, clarifying the precise meanings of key terms and defending the definition's comprehensiveness. Understanding these objections and responses deepens your appreciation of Hanafi usul methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under critique
Recall the Hanafi definition: hukm shar'i is the divine address (khitab Allah) relating to the actions of the legally responsible persons (mukallafin). This definition is the target of the objections.
2
Examine each objection
The passage presents five objections: (1) definition of validity/invalidity is theological not juristic, (2) meaning of mandub is misrepresented as requiring a guardian, (3) rulings from qiyas are not covered, (4) heart actions (e.g., iman) are excluded, (5) the term 'amaliyya' in fiqh definition is redundant. Work through each.
3
Follow the commentator's response to each
For each objection, note how the commentator refutes or qualifies it. Key responses: validity/invalidity are shari matters; mandub is about reward not guardianship; qiyas is a manifestation (muzhir) of an existing ruling; 'fi'l al-mukallaf' includes both heart and limb actions; 'amaliyya' excludes theoretical rulings (nazariyyat).
4
Understand the key terminological distinctions
The responses rely on precise terms: muzhir vs. muthbit for qiyas; 'fi'l al-mukallaf' as broad; 'amaliyya' as specific to limb actions. These distinctions are essential for the defense.
Note the parallel argument: the same issue with qiyas also applies to Sunnah and ijma', resolved similarly.
5
Evaluate the final resolution regarding 'amaliyya'
The deepest debate concerns whether 'amaliyya' is redundant. The commentator offers multiple resolutions: some argue that rulings like 'hujjiyyat al-ijma' are not hukm in the terminological sense; others reinterpret 'wujub al-‘amal bi-muqtada' as obligation of istidlal and ifta'. This shows the sophistication of Hanafi usul.

ہوا تو یہ حکم شرعی ہوگا نہ کہ عقلی ثانیا یہ کہ صحت و فساد کا جو مفہوم شارح نے پیش کیا ہے یہ مذہب متکلمین پر ہے نہ کہ مذہب فقہا پر حالانکہ یہاں مفہوم اصطلاح فقہا۔ والا معتبر ہے اور اما مذہب الفقہاء من الشافعية فصحة الفعل عبارة عن كونه مسقطاً للقضاء والفساد خلافه و هذا امر شرعی بلاشبہہ کیونکہ مسقط قضاء ہونا یا نہ ہونا اس کی معرفت شریعت سے حاصل ہوتی ہے لہذا یہ احکام شرعیہ میں درج ہے نہ کہ عقلیہ میں ۔ کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ اپنے بچپن میں اسلام لانے پر فخر کیا کرتے تھے اور ثانیاً یہ کہ ایسا صبی جو ممیز ہے اس کا کوئی ولی اور متولی نہیں ہے اور نہ کسی نے اسے تحریض و ترغیب کی ہے اگر لوگوں کو دیکھ کر بالقیاس حکم کی تعریف مذکور پر تفسیرا اعتراض ہے کہ یہ تعریف اس حکم کو شامل نہیں ہے جو ثابت بالقیاس ہے کیونکہ قیاسی حکم میں خطاب اللہ واقع نہیں ہے اور حکم کی تعریف خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ کے ساتھ کی گئی لہذا یہ تعریف جامع نہیں ہے اجاب حاصل جواب یہ کہ قیاس مظہر حکم ہوتا ہے مثبت حکم نہیں ہوتا یعنی قیاس یہ امر ظاہر کرتا ہے کہ جو نص مقیس علیہ میں واقع ہے یہ قیاسی حکم اسی کے تحت درج ہے اور قیاس کا مظہر حکم ہونا فی الواقع ہوتا ہے یا فی زعم المجتہد اگر مجتہد مخفی ہو تو لا يخفى عليك یعنی یہی سوال صرف حکم ثابت بالقیاس میں نہیں بلکہ ثابت بالسنۃ والا جماع میں بھی ہے کیونکہ خطاب اللہ ان میں بھی واقع نہیں ہے تو جواب اس کا بھی یہی ہے کہ سنہ و اجماع ہر ایک کا شف عن خطاب اللہ تعالٰی ہے اور معرف اور ان کے اولہ للاحکام ہونے سے یہی مراد ہے کہ یہ کاشف اور معرف ہیں۔ الرابع انه غیر شامل چوتھا اعتراض یہ ہے کہ یہ تعریف ان احکام کو شامل نہیں ہے جو افعان قلب سے متعلق ہیں جیسے وجوب الایمان بمعنی التصدیق اور وجوب الاعتبار والقیاس کیونکہ حکم کی تعریف میں جو افعال المکلفین کا لفظ ہے اس سے متبادر افعال الجوارح ہیں الخامس پانچواں اعتراض یہ کہ جب تعریف حکم میں تعلق بفعل المكلف ہے تو مختص بالعملیات ہو جائے گا نظریات نکل جائیں گے کیونکہ فعل مكلف مختص بفعل الجوارح ہے لہذا تہ ریف فقہ میں العملیہ کی قید لغو اور ضائع ہو جائے گی۔ واجاب عنهما ان دونوں اعتراضوں سے یعنی رابع وخامس سے جواب دیا کہ فعل مکلف سے مراد عام ہے خواہ فعل قلب ہو یا جوارح لہذا وجوب ایمان اور وجوب اعتبار داخل تحت الحکم ہو جائیں گے اور عملیہ سے مراد وہ افعال ہیں جو مختص بالجوارح ہیں لہذا عملیہ کی قید لغو نہیں ہوگی بلکہ تعریف فقہ سے وجوب ایمان وغیرہ جو متعلق بفعل الجوارح نہیں ہیں انہیں خارج کر دے گی ۔ ولقائل ان يقول اذا حمل الحکم مصنف نے عملیہ کی قید کو تکرار سے بچانے کے لئے جو جواب دیا ہے قائل کا یہ اعتراض اسی پر ہے خلاصہ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ فقہ کی تعریف میں اگر لفظ حکم کو اصطلاحی معنی یعنی خطاب اللہ تعالٰی المتعلق پر محمول کیا جائے تو عملیہ کی قید یقینا مکر رہے کیوں کہ وجوب ایمان شرعیہ کی قید سے خارج ہو جائے گا کیونکہ جب حکم اصطلاحی مراد ہو تو اس وقت شرعیہ کا معنی ما توقف علی الشرع تھا لکما مر سابقا اور ایمان اور تصدیق بالنبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام چونکہ موقوف على الشرع نہیں ہیں لہذا یہ قید شرعیہ سے خارج ہو جائیں گے عملیہ کی قید کو ان کے لئے مخرج بنانا تحصیل حاصل اور اخراج مخرج ہے اس صورت میں مصنف نے حکم شرعی کو دو قسم بنایا تھا ایک نظری جیسے اجماع کا حجت ہونا اور دوسرا عملی تو عملیہ کی قید کے ساتھ اس وقت احکام نظریہ کا اخراج کیا تھا تو شارح نے اس کو رد کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ مثل كون الاجماع حجة 4 یہ خود حکم مصطلح میں داخل نہیں ہے کیونکہ حکم مصطلح میں جو قید بالاقتضاء والتخییر ہے وہ اس کے لئے مخرج ہے اس لئے عملیہ کی قید کا بجز تکرار کے اور کوئی فائدہ معتد بہا نہیں لایقال یہ شارح کے رد کا جواب دینے کی کوشش ہے جس کو شارح رد کرنا چاہتا ہے حاصل یہ ہے کہ سنت اور اجماع وقیاس کے حج ہونے کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ ان کے مقتضیٰ پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے لہذا یہ اقتضا ضمنی میں داخل ہو جائیں گے تو اس پر لانا نقول سے رد کر دیا کہ پھر قید عملیہ سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے کیونکہ جب ان کے مقتضا پر عمل کرنا واجب ہوا تو یہ احکام عملیہ میں داخل ہو جائیں گے پھر اخراج کیسے صحیح ہوگا ۔ و يمكن ان يقال سے شارح نے عملیہ کو مکرر ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے یہ توجیہ کر دی کہ ہو سکتا ہے جواز الا جائے اور وجوب قیاس حکم شرعی ہیں لیکن عملی نہیں ہیں لہذا عملیہ کے ساتھ ان کا اخراج ہو سکتا ہے اور بعض حضرات نے پہلے جواب کو یعنی یہ کہ سنت اور اجماع کے مقتضا پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے اس کا معنی یہ لیا ہے کہ وجوب العمل بمقتضاها سے مراد وجوب الاستدلال بہا والافتاء بموجبها یعنی مسائل پر ان سے استدلال کرنا واجب ہے اور اس کے موجب وہ مقتضا کے موافق فتویٰ دینا لازم ہے تو یہ امر عملیات سے نہیں لہذا عملیہ کی قید اس صورت میں ان کے لئے مخرج ہو جائے گی۔ قال المصنف في التوضيح والشرعية ما لا تدرك لولا خطاب الشارع فقہ کی تعریف العلم بالاحکام الشرعیہ میں چونکہ حکم کی تفسیر خطاب اللہ تعالٰی سے کی گئی تھی تو اس وقت شرعیہ سے مراد وہ احکام
Then this would be a shari ruling, not a rational one. Secondly, the understanding of validity and invalidity that the commentator presented belongs to the school of the theologians, not the school of the jurists, whereas here the understanding of the terminology of the jurists is authoritative. As for the school of the Shafi'i jurists, the validity of an act is defined as it being that which removes liability, and invalidity is the opposite, and this is undoubtedly a shari matter because knowing whether it removes liability or not is obtained from the Shari'ah. Therefore, it is included in shari rulings, not rational ones. After that, the commentator presented the meaning of mandub for the morning prayer as that the guardian is commanded to encourage it. This is clearly far-fetched, because mandub means deserving reward; the guardian's urging is something external. This is why 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) used to boast about embracing Islam in his childhood. Secondly, such a discriminating child has no guardian or caretaker, and no one has exhorted or encouraged him. If he performs prayer and fasting by observing people, then nadb is present in that, and the guardian has no connection. What answer will the commentator give regarding this? In any case, the word 'ibad (servants) is better than mukallafin (legally responsible persons). Third: The definition does not encompass the ruling established by qiyas. This is an objection to the definition: the definition does not include the ruling established by qiyas, because in a qiyasi ruling there is no khitab of Allah, and the definition of hukm was made with the khitab of Allah, so this definition is not comprehensive. The answer: Qiyas is a manifestation of the ruling, not an establisher of the ruling. That is, qiyas shows that the ruling that exists in the nass upon which the analogy is based, the qiyasi ruling falls under it. The manifestation of the ruling by qiyas either occurs in reality or in the ijtihad of the mujtahid if it is hidden. It is not hidden from you that the same question exists not only in the ruling established by qiyas but also in that established by the Sunnah and ijma', because the khitab of Allah is not present in them either. Its answer is likewise: the Sunnah and ijma' each unveil the khitab of Allah, and they are identifiers. The intended meaning of their being sources of rulings is that they are revealers and identifiers. Fourth: It does not include rulings related to acts of the heart, such as the obligation of iman in the sense of tasdiq and the obligation of consideration and qiyas, because in the definition of hukm, the word 'af'al al-mukallafin' primarily indicates acts of the limbs. Fifth: When the definition of hukm connects to the action of the mukallaf, it will be specific to amaliyyat (practical matters), and nazariyyat (theoretical matters) will be excluded, because fi'l al-mukallaf is specific to acts of the limbs. Therefore, the qualification 'amaliyya' in the definition of fiqh becomes superfluous and wasted. He responded to both objections, i.e., the fourth and fifth, saying that 'fi'l al-mukallaf' is general, whether it is an act of the heart or limbs. Hence, the obligation of iman and the obligation of consideration will be included under the hukm. And 'amaliyya' refers to those acts that are specific to the limbs, so the qualification 'amaliyya' will not be superfluous; rather, the definition of fiqh excludes the obligation of iman and others that are not related to acts of the limbs. And one may object: When the hukm is interpreted (as the author did to avoid repetition of the qualification 'amaliyya' in the definition of fiqh), the objection of the objector is directed at this. The summary of the objection is that if in the definition of fiqh the word 'hukm' is taken in its terminological meaning, i.e., the khitab of Allah relating to the actions of the mukallafin, then the qualification 'amaliyya' would certainly be repetitive, because the obligation of iman would be excluded by the qualification 'shar'iyya'. Since when hukm is meant terminologically, then 'shar'iyya' means 'that which is not known except through the khitab of the Lawgiver', as previously mentioned, and iman and tasdiq of the Prophet (peace be upon him) are not dependent on the Shari'ah, so they would be excluded by the qualification 'shar'iyya'. Making the qualification 'amaliyya' an exclude for them would be a repetition and an exclusion of what is already excluded. In this case, the author had divided shari hukm into two types: nazari, like ijma' being a proof, and amali. So with the qualification 'amaliyya', at that time the exclusion of nazari rulings was made. Then the commentator rejected this, saying that 'such as ijma' being a proof' itself is not included in the terminological hukm, because the terminological hukm includes the qualification of demand (iqtida') and choice (takhyir), which excludes it. Therefore, the qualification 'amaliyya' has no significant benefit other than repetition. 'La yuqalu' is an attempt to answer the commentator's rejection, which the commentator wants to refute. The gist is that the purpose of the Sunnah, ijma', and qiyas being proofs is that acting upon their implications is obligatory. Hence, this obligation is included within the demand (iqtida') implicitly. Then it is refuted by 'la yuqalu' that then they would not be excluded by the qualification 'amaliyya', because when acting upon their implications is obligatory, they enter into amali rulings. Then how can exclusion be valid? 'Wa yumkinu an yuqala': The commentator provided this explanation to avoid the repetition of 'amaliyya': it is possible that jawaz al-qiyas and wujub al-qiyas are shari rulings, but they are not amali. Therefore, they can be excluded by 'amaliyya'. Some scholars took the first answer, i.e., that acting upon the implications of the Sunnah and ijma' is obligatory, to mean that 'wujub al-'amal bi-muqtadaha' means the obligation of deriving evidence (istidlal) from them and issuing fatwas according to them, i.e., it is obligatory to derive evidence from them for issues and to give fatwas accordingly. This is a matter of amaliyyat (practical matters), so the qualification 'amaliyya' in this case would be an exclude for them. The author said in al-Tawdih: 'And shar'iyya is that which is not known except through the khitab of the Lawgiver.' In the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of the shar'i rulings', since hukm was interpreted as the khitab of Allah, at that time 'shar'iyya' refers to those rulings...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the definition of hukm shar'i, addressing several objections raised against it. The commentator first clarifies that the concept of validity (sihha) and invalidity (fasad) as presented earlier by the original commentator belongs to the theologians (mutakallimin), not the jurists (fuqaha). The Hanafi (and Shafi'i) jurists define validity as an act being legally valid (musqit li-l-qada'), which is a shari matter, not rational. The commentator then criticizes the earlier definition of mandub (recommended) as requiring a guardian to encourage, arguing that mandub simply means deserving reward, and the role of a guardian is external. This is supported by the example of Ali (ra) and the independent discerning child. 

The third objection: The definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah' does not include rulings derived from qiyas, Sunnah, or ijma', because these sources do not directly contain the divine address. The response: these sources are manifestations (muzhir) of the ruling, not its establisher; they unveil or identify the divine address already present in the texts. Thus, they are covered. 

The fourth objection: The definition excludes rulings related to heart actions (af'al al-qulub) like belief (iman). The fifth objection: The definition's connection to 'fi'l al-mukallaf' makes it specific to limb actions (af'al al-jawarih), so theoretical rulings (nazariyyat) are excluded, making the qualification 'amaliyya' in fiqh redundant. The response: 'fi'l al-mukallaf' is general, including heart and limb actions, so heart-related rulings are included. 'Amaliyya' specifically refers to limb actions, so it still serves to exclude purely theoretical rulings from the definition of fiqh. 

The text then delves into a deeper debate about whether the qualification 'amaliyya' is repetitive. If 'hukm' is taken in its terminological sense (khitab Allah), then 'shar'iyya' already excludes matters known by reason (like the necessity of iman), making 'amaliyya' redundant. Various responses are examined: one that rulings like the authority of ijma' are not themselves hukm in the terminological sense, so 'amaliyya' excludes them; another that such rulings involve obligation to act on their implications, which makes them practical. Finally, a possible defense is that the obligation of qiyas or the permissibility of qiyas are shari but not amali (practical), so they are excluded. Some scholars interpret 'wujub al-'amal bi-muqtada' as the obligation of istidlal (deduction) and ifta' (fatwa), which is not amali. The passage ends with a quote from al-Tawdih, reiterating that 'shar'iyya' means only knowable through the Lawgiver's address.

Throughout, the commentary defends the classical Hanafi definition of hukm and fiqh, showing how objections are resolved by careful attention to terminology and the scope of 'fi'l al-mukallaf'.

Key Terms
حکم شرعی (hukm shar'i): The divine address (khitab Allah) relating to the actions of the legally responsible persons (mukallafin), including demands and choices.
قیاس (qiyas): A method of deriving a ruling by analogy from an existing nass; it is a manifestation (muzhir) of an existing ruling, not an originator of a new ruling.
فعل المکلف (fi'l al-mukallaf): The action of the legally responsible person, including both actions of the heart (af'al al-qulub) and actions of the limbs (af'al al-jawarih).
افعال الجوارح (af'al al-jawarih): Actions performed by the physical limbs (e.g., prayer, fasting).
افعال القلوب (af'al al-qulub): Actions of the heart, such as belief (iman), intention, or consideration (i'tibar).
عملیات (amaliyyat): Practical rulings related to actions of the limbs, as opposed to nazariyyat (theoretical rulings).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the Hanafi school resolve the objection that rulings from qiyas are not covered by the definition of hukm shar'i?
A) By stating that qiyas is not a source of rulings.
B) By redefining hukm to include any ruling from any source.
C) By arguing that qiyas is a manifestation (muzhir) of an existing ruling.
D) By excluding qiyas from the definition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i as khitab Allah is robust and inclusive, with qiyas, heart actions, and practical matters all properly accounted for through precise terminological distinctions.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
The Hanafi Definition of Fiqh and the Rational vs Revealed Good and Evil Dispute
Analyzing the definition of fiqh and the objection regarding inclusion of rationally known actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh, distinguish between actions with rational good/evil and those with shar'i good/evil, and evaluate the Ash'ari objection and the proposed additional condition to the definition.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of shar'i rulings derived from evidence, excluding actions known by reason alone or by necessity from religion.

In this passage, we examine the classical Hanafi definition of fiqh and a critical objection: if all good and evil are determined by revelation, then every ethical action would be part of fiqh. The Hanafi (Maturidi) response distinguishes rational from revealed good/evil, limiting fiqh to the latter. We also explore why a proposed condition—'not known from religion by necessity'—is rejected as unnecessary. Understanding this definition clarifies the precise scope of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Definition
Identify the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of shar'i rulings from specific evidences'. Note that the passage clarifies that shari'i includes rulings derived via qiyas, because such rulings still depend on the Lawgiver's address in the original case.
This expansion justifies analogical reasoning as part of fiqh.
2
Understand the Objection
The objection: for those who deny rational good and evil (like Ash'aris), every action's moral value is shari'i, so even humility would be part of fiqh. This would make the definition too broad.
The objection targets the Hanafi definition by questioning its boundary.
3
Apply the Hanafi-Maturidi Distinction
Hanafis (Maturidis) hold that some actions have rational good/evil (e.g., humility) and some only shari'i good/evil (e.g., fasting on specific days). Only the latter are fiqh; the former are ethics. This preserves the definition's integrity.
This step shows how the definition remains valid for Hanafis.
4
Analyze the Ash'ari Counterposition
Ash'aris hold all ethical judgments are shari'i. Consequently, for them, the same definition would include ethically good actions, making it overinclusive. The passage notes this as a flaw in the Ash'ari framework.
The thamarah al-khilaf: what counts as fiqh differs between schools.
5
Evaluate the Proposed Additional Condition
Some scholars proposed adding 'not known from religion by necessity' to exclude obvious obligations like prayer. The commentator refutes this: knowing even many issues from evidence does not make one a faqih, so the condition is unnecessary and deceptive.
The condition is rejected because fiqh requires derivation from evidence, not mere knowledge of obligation.

یہ اسی اعتراض مذکور کی تفصیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک یعنی احناف جو ماتریدیہ کہلاتے ہیں ان کے نزدیک اور جمہور معتزلہ کے نزدیک بعض افعال کا حسن و قبح عقلی ہے یعنی ان کا حسن و قبح کا علم و
