شرط ہے وہ یہ کہ استنباط صحیح کے لئے جتنا ضروری شرائط ہیں ان کے ساتھ مقرون ہو۔
The author said in al-Tawdih: 'Rather, it is knowledge of all the practical shar'i rulings that have appeared with the descent of revelation.' The author presents this definition of fiqh from his side, the gist of which is that fiqh is called knowledge of all those shar'i rulings that have appeared with the descent of revelation and on which consensus has been established, that knowledge which is obtained from detailed evidences, provided that one also has the faculty of correctly deriving rulings from evidences, or the faculty of deriving analogical branches from the textual rulings. So the consideration is that one knows — meaning 'all rulings' refers to those that have been gathered at the time of the appearance of revelation, because revelation descended gradually, so at different times, as much as was gathered, knowledge of that is required. Thus the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) at the time of the descent of revelation were fuqaha, even if some rulings were revealed later; before that later revelation, knowledge of what had been revealed is necessary, and after their appearance, knowledge becomes necessary. So 'what appears' — this explains the benefit of the condition 'appearance of revelation': that until the appearance of revelation, knowing it is not necessary for the faqih. And its knowledge before appearance does not affect his fiqh. 'And the Companions, due to their Arabness' — this is the benefit of the condition of the faculty of istinbat, meaning the Companions, because they were Arabic-speaking, due to that they had knowledge of the revealed rulings by virtue of being Arabic speakers, yet not every Companion was called a faqih, rather only those who derived. So it is known that for a faqih, along with knowledge of the rulings, the faculty of istinbat is also necessary. 'And knowledge of consensus issues as a condition' — meaning knowing consensus issues is also a necessary condition for a faqih, but since there was no consensus during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), it is not possible for the fuqaha of that era to know them, nor is it conditioned. 'Not analogical issues' — meaning knowing analogical issues is not a condition for the fiqh of the faqih, but rather a condition for correct istinbat, because analogical issues are a result of the faqih's fiqh, which depends on fiqh. If fiqh depended on knowing analogical issues, then a circularity would arise, which is false. However, the faculty of correct istinbat is a condition, meaning that it must be accompanied by all the necessary conditions for correct istinbat.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of fiqh according to the author (al-Tawdih). Fiqh is defined as knowledge of all practical shar'i rulings that have been revealed, obtained from detailed evidences, with the additional requirement of having the faculty (malakah) of correctly deriving rulings from those evidences. The passage then explains various conditions: knowledge is required for all rulings that have appeared at the time of revelation (so a faqih must know the rulings that have been revealed up to his time). The Companions had this knowledge due to their Arabness, but not all were fuqaha; only those who possessed the faculty of istinbat. Knowledge of consensus issues is a condition for later fuqaha, but not for the Companions since consensus had not occurred. Knowledge of analogical rulings is not a condition for being a faqih, because that would cause circularity; rather, it is a result of having the faculty.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of practical shar'i rulings that have been revealed, with the faculty of deriving them from detailed evidences.
استنباط (istinbat): The process of deriving rulings from evidences using usul al-fiqh.
ملکہ (malakah): The faculty or ability to correctly derive rulings from evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition of fiqh in al-Tawdih as explained in this lesson, which of the following is necessary for a person to be considered a faqih?
A) Knowledge of all rulings including those not yet revealed
B) Both knowledge of revealed rulings and the faculty of istinbat
C) Only knowledge of ibadat
D) Being a sahabi

Key Takeaway
Fiqh in the Hanafi school is the knowledge of practical rulings combined with the faculty of deriving them from their detailed evidences.
